After I completed the book for you, O Sons, which is the last one regarding knowledge in medicine with its supplement, and I have reached the end of it through explanations of the same and the declarations, it seemed to me that I should complete it for you with this Treatise, which is part of surgery, namely, chirurgery with my hand.
Since operation with hand is laid low in our region and at our time entirely deprived of it: perhaps the knowledge of it has perished, and its trace is lost; and only small descriptions of it remain in old books, which have been altered by hands; and error and hesitation occur until the intentions are closed and the force is weakened: It seemed to me that I should revive it with the arrangement of this Treatise according to the way of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation; and that I should come with forms of iron tools of Cauterium, and the rest of the instruments of work; when it is done by addition to the declarations and from the necessity of its use.
The reason why a good artisan of it is not found with his hand at this time, is because the art of medicine is long, and the author must be trained in knowledge of anatomy before that, which Galen narrated, until he knows the means of the members, and their shapes, and their union and separation, and has knowledge of bones, nerves, muscles, and their number, and their movement, and the pulse vessels, and quiet ones, and their exits; and the locations of their origins.
And for that reason, Hippocrates said that name with name is much, and with work it is little, and especially in the art of hand.
We have already said about him at the beginning of this book.
Because he who is not knowing what we have said about anatomy, is already in danger of falling into error, in which men are killed: just as I have seen many of those who form themselves from this science and boast about it without knowledge, and without experiment.
Because I have seen a foolish surgeon remove an abscess on a woman's neck and cut some arteries in the neck: therefore, blood flowed from the woman until she died in his hands.
And I have seen another surgeon who presumed to extract a stone from an elderly man, and the stone was large. Therefore he came to him, and extracted it with a piece of the bladder. Therefore the man died on the third day.
And I was already called to extract it; and I saw from the size of the stone and the weakness of the patient that he would die.
And I saw another surgeon who was receiving a fee from one of our land's dukes on account of his medicine; and it happened to a black eunuch who was with him, that he suffered a fracture near the heel: and the surgeon, in his ignorance, bound up the fracture over an ulcer with plasters and needles, and strong bands, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he closed it according to his negligence. Afterwards he released him for some days and ordered him not to loosen the bandage; and he stood thus until an abscess formed on his leg, and his foot, and it came to his ruin.
Therefore I was called to him; and I rushed to unbind the bandage; and calm came upon him, and he was relieved of his pain.
However, the corruption had already been confirmed in the member; and I could not stop it.
Stop the corruption from walking through the limb, until it dies.
And I saw another physician who pierced a cancerous boil; and it became an ulcer until the malignancy of it was exposed with its lord.
Because when it is a pure cancer from black bile, then it is not necessary to reach it with iron altogether, unless it is in a limb that can endure, so that the whole of it may be cut off.
And because of that (the saying) "O Sons," it is necessary for you to know that the operation is divided into two divisions; namely, the operation associated with safety; and the operation, with which there is danger in many situations.
And I have already aroused myself in every place of this book where the operation comes where there is fear and dread.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to be careful not to divide it and to leave it alone; so that fools do not find a way to speak about it and to dishonor it.
Therefore, receive the measure with diligence and protection; and your weak ones with ease and firmness; and use a better way leading by God's grace to salvation and praiseworthy succession; and leave behind difficult diseases; and rid yourselves of that which causes you fear, so that hesitation in faith and comfort may not enter upon you.
For it remains more to your glory, and higher in this world, and finally to your rewards.
Galenus has already said in some of his warnings. Do not treat the evil disease; do not be called an evil doctor.
Now, however, I have divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
Chapter One.
On Cautery with fire and with sharp medicine, this subject is arranged from head to foot, and the forms of instruments and tools for cautery; and all that is necessary for the operation. ¶
Chapter second.
On incision and perforation, bloodletting and ventoses, and wounds: and the extraction of arrows and similar things: and the whole chapter, arranged in the forms of instruments. ¶
Chapter third.
On restoration, dislocation, treatment of twisting and similar conditions: the chapter arranged from head to foot, and in the forms of instruments.
Before I remember the operation with him, it is necessary to say the quality of his remedies and his harms, and in what composition they are displayed.
Therefore, the discourse on the quality of the Cautery remedy and its harm is lengthy, subtle, scientific, and a hidden secret.
Also, a multitude of wise men spoke about it and disagreed on it; for myself, I find their words sufficient, fearing lengthy debate.
Therefore, I say that the Cautery is applied universally to every composition, whether with matter or without it; except for two compositions, which are the hot composition without matter and the dry composition without matter.
However, in the hot and dry compositions with matter, they disagreed. Some said that the cautery is beneficial in it. Others said that the cautery is not suitable for an illness that is caused by heat and dryness; because fire is hot, it is inappropriate to heal from a hot and dry illness with fire and cold.
And the one who says contrary to that said: by means of cautery, a remedy is made for all hot and dry illnesses that occur in human bodies; because when you apply heat to a human body, you find it cold.
And I myself say by his words: because from experience, he has often demonstrated that to me.
Nevertheless, it is not necessary for him to come on that, unless he has been proven and trained in the chapter of Cauterii exercise at the end, and knows the differences in human compositions, and the dispositions of illnesses within themselves, and their causes and manifestations, and the periods of those illnesses.
From the remaining temperaments there is no fear for you; and especially concerning cold and moist illnesses. For, indeed, all physicians have agreed upon them (the cauteries); and they have not disagreed about the benefit when using cautery on these.
And know, my children, that through the secret of curing with cautery and fire, as well as its goodness upon the cautery with medicine burning, because fire is simple, whose action does not reach any other part than the one being cauterized; and it harms no other connected member except in a slight degree.
But the action of burning medicine reaches that which is extended from members; and perhaps it causes difficulty in healing the member, and perhaps it kills.
Fire, however, because of its subtlety and goodness, does not do this unless it is excessive.
But we have come to know this through experience, because of the length of service and study with art, and because of its steadfastness on truth; and therefore I excuse myself from the length of speech.
And if it were not forbidden to this book of mine, I would tell you the secret hidden in fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies in expelling diseases, which was demonstrated by the philosophical discourse, which would sharpen your minds.
And know, my children, that they themselves disagree concerning the time when cautery is to be made, and place better the time with truth.
And I say that cautery is fitting at all times; therefore, any harm resulting from time is submerged in the benefit which attracts it when cautery is applied. And especially if cautery is for pains from necessary strong, speedy pains which cannot tolerate delay; therefore it is feared that a greater evil may occur than slight harm caused by time.
And let not that thought occur to your minds, my sons, that they do not consider, except for the common people and foolish physicians, that there is no return always in the ailment which is cured by cautery; and they place this as a consequence, but matters are not thus as they think: therefore because cauterization is not, except in place of medicine, which changes complexion, and expels humidities which are the causes, wherefore pains occur.
Nevertheless, cauterization is superfluous over medicine due to the swiftness of its health, and the power of its operation, and the violence of its dominion; and it is possible that the ailment returns at some hour of time according to the complexion of the sick, and the location of his ailment, and the strength of it; and what has been prepared in his body from the accumulation of superfluidities in him; and what reaches him in acquisition from foods and similar things due to causes, unless there is an ailment where cauterization is administered.
A subtle ailment in a member of few superfluidities and humidities, such as cauterization of the tooth, due to pain, and similar things, it is possible that that pain will not return in him. But this happens in few cases.
Indeed, the speech of the common people again, that cauterization is the last medicine, is a correct statement; not regarding what they intend in it; for they believe that there is no cure which confers with medicine, nor with anything after the disappearance of cauterization.
But the matter is opposite to that which they intend regarding that cauterization is the last medicine; it is not so unless when we administer methods of cure for some ailment, and those do not confer with the medicine; then at the end of the matter we apply cauterization, and it confers; hence arises the notion that cauterization is the last medicine, not according to the intention which the common people and many foolish physicians understand.
The ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron; and they did not say this unless on account of the equality of gold and its nobility; and they said that it does not produce pus at the site of the cauterization. That is not absolutely true; for I have already proven it, and I found that this does not happen in certain bodies without others.
And cautery with it (gold) is good, and better than with iron, as they said. Nevertheless, when you put fire to the cautery from gold in fire, it is not made clear to you at what degree of heat it burns according to your will, because of the redness of gold; and when it approaches towards it (the gold), cold comes forth, and if you add more heating, it melts in the fire, and it turns into leaves.
Therefore, the craftsman falls into a fixation with it (gold); and for that reason, we use cautery with iron more quickly and closer at hand, because of its straightness in operation.
And I myself have already arranged this Chapter on Cautery, according to chapters; and I have arranged it from head to foot, so that the seeker may find what he wants in it.
Chapter II:
Here, the cauterization is applied for the mastery over humidity and coldness on the brain: which are two causes of soda (seizures), and of the abundance of fluid flow from the head to the parts of eyes and ears, and the abundance of sleep, and tooth pain, and throat pain: and universally every sickness that happens due to coldness, such as paralysis, sodae (a specific condition), epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar conditions due to sicknesses.
The method of cauterization is to instruct the sick person: that it should be evacuated first with a solution of medicine cleansing the head for three or four nights, according to the strength and age of the sick person and his custom.
Then command him (the sick person) to scrape his head with a potsherd. Then make him sit facing you, so that he has placed his hands on his chest.
Then place the root of your palm over the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever your middle finger reaches, mark that place with an unburnt (charred) spot.
Then burn the cautery in oil: this is its form.
Then place it (the cautery) on the marked and unburnt spot, while you press it gently with your hand and turn it around. Then lift your hand quickly, and look at the place.
If you see that the quantity of skull or the quantity of pus is exposed, then lift your hand. And if not, press your hand with the iron itself, or with another tool if it becomes cold: until the bones I told you appear.
Then take something from salt, dissolve it in water, and immerse the cloth in it, and place it on the spot: and leave it for three days.
Then place upon him a cloth soaked in butter, and let it remain over the place until the eschar (scab or dry crust) is consumed by fire. Then treat it with the ointment called tetrapharmacon, until it heals.
As they say, the more an open wound remains, the more it discharges pus; therefore, it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them say that the skin should be cauterized to the bone; and hold the cautery until something of the thickness of the bone is burned.
Then file away the burnt part from the bone, then treat it.
And others say that when you reach the bone with the cautery, an impression should be made in it as deep as a nail head, so that the bone falls out, forming a cavity like a cork: or an instrument that women use filled with the small alphabet (poultice): and they think that the vapors of the head are exhaled from this place, and leave the open wound for a long time.
Then treat it until it solidifies.
For me, these two types of cautery do not seem to be suitable for anyone except in certain men, according to the way of fear (fearful people).
And leave it alone, in my opinion, it is better with his own health.
For the head weakens from the resolution of its own continuity (natural state), as we have witnessed in other members: and especially when the head of a sick person is naturally weak: and the first species of cautery is safer and better for me, and I use it; therefore, operate with it for safety.
Head (chapter).
When there is a chronic pain throughout the head, and it persists in a weak person and uses heat-producing agents (herbs, hot baths, etc.), massaging the head, applying oils and plasters. And particularly if it has already been cauterized with one cautery, as I have said, and nothing is added to it from those [others]: then consider. If the head of the sick person is strong by nature and not weak, and finds violent coldness: then cauterize it with another cautery slightly. Then cauterize it over all the horn of its head with another cautery, so that the skin is not penetrated, and a quantity of bone, as I have said, is exposed. And cauterize it with one cautery on the back of its head, in a place called "the vase", and it is the place where the vent is placed; and lift your cloth (matum) in this and do not expose the bone. For the sick one finds intense pain because of that pain, and different from the pain of all other cauteries on the head.
And I will say that this Cautery is in its place: and it must be a cautery with which the horns of the head are cauterized, and the back of its head more subtlely with a cautery with which the middle of the head is cauterized.
Chapter IV.
When pain and swelling occur in a part of the head or extends to the eye, and the head is weakened with purifying medicines, and further treatment, as I have said in the divisions of diseases, does not help: then cauterization in this case is done according to two methods: either cauterization with hot medicine burning, or with iron.
The cautery with hot medicine burning is, that you take one tooth from an allium (onion or garlic), and grind it up, and cut off the ends from both sides. Then cut the painful spot in time with a broad lancet, until there is a place under the skin where the tooth can be captured.
Insert it there under the skin until it is hidden; then bind it above with a suitable plaster and leave it for fifteen hours, then dissolve it, and extract the onion, and leave it untouched for two or three days: afterwards place a warm compress over it submerged in butter, until the spot makes pus; then care for it with an ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish to do this with certain burning medications, which I wrote about in the twelfth treatise, on the Meidicines that Burn.
However, cauterization of it with iron is as follows. The form of the fire cautery is as follows.
And it is called "Clavilis" because the shape of its head is like that of a nail, in which there is some hardness, and in the middle of it there is a small projection.
Then place it on the spot and hold your hand; and you rotate the iron slowly with speed: and let the quantity to be burnt be of the thickness of the skin, as its half. And raise your hand so that not the artery below is burned and let blood flow out.
Then immerse the compress in water and salt, place it on the spot, and leave it for three days; then put the compress with butter; afterwards care for it with an ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemicania with the tip of a second-degree cautery knife. Avoid cutting the artery in this hemicania, not an old one specifically.
§ On the method of cauterizing in an old hemicania.
When you treat a hemicrania, with what we said in the preceding cure, and what we said in the divisions of illnesses, and the treatment does not help: and if you see from the illness that what we said about the first cauterization with medicine or with cauterization with fire is insufficient, then it is necessary to heat the cauterium with iron until it turns white after marking the place of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger or similar: and place one hand in its place, and press it until you cut through the artery, and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary that you avoid burning the jaw which moves during chewing, so as not to burn the side or nerve which moves it, from where a spasm may occur.
And be careful of the guard and caution for the flow of blood from the artery that was cut. For there is fear in its cutting and especially for him who does not know what he is doing or is not diligent, experienced: and he should first abandon the operation.
And I shall come with a reminder of the management of blood flowing from the cut artery according to its own manner, and at the place of this book.
If you see from the illness that this cauterization is insufficient and you see the body of the weak person bearing the cauterization in the middle of the head as we have narrated, then treat a wound until it heals.
And if you wish, administer the cauterization as we have said in the chapter on the extraction of the artery with a cauterizer having two blades. For this cauterization is better and more helpful.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in pain of the ear.
When cold pain occurs in the ear and it is treated with solutions, and the rest of the treatment as we said in division, and yet the pain does not subside, then cautery by fire: and this is called a puncture, whose shape is as follows.
Then, after the cautery, make a puncture around the entire ear as it revolves; or around both if pain is on both sides. And extend yourself slightly with the cautery from the root of the ear afterwards, after marking the places with pitch; and let the size of the cautery be ten punctures in every ear, and so on.
Then treat the areas until they heal.
Section on the method of cauterization in strangulation.
Chapter VII.
Strangulation, which is treated with cauterization, is not anything but those which occur due to phlegm, as we said in the divisions of diseases.
And avoid cauterization for species that occur due to exhaustion and spasm of the nerve.
When you treat this type of strangulation with hyssop, purges and gargarisms, and your treatment does not improve, then it is necessary to cauterize the weak one with three cauterizations: one at the root of the ear, second slightly lower than its opening, and third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cautery from the weaker side. Because softening does not occur unless in the part that appears healthy.
And the form of the cauterization is that you should cauterize yourself with the cautery directly on the extremity of the upper part of the ear under the horn of the head slightly; and another one in the opening: whose length should be according to the length of the thumb. And place your hand with the cautery until the thickness of half the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the Cautery, and it is a type from a knife, whose shape is as follows: nevertheless, it should not be too fine, as you see; and it is necessary that the knife in it should have little excess thickness.
Then care for the places, until they heal.
Chapter on the ancient method of cauterization in Apoplexy.
When the apoplexy becomes ancient and the care of it, as we said earlier, does not help, and the patient is not feverish, then cauterize him with four cauteries on every horn of his head, and a cautery in the middle of the head, as mentioned before, and a cautery on the occiput of the head, according to what was stated; and the method of cauterization should be as stated previously.
Also cauterize with a Cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and this is more final.
Then it should be taken care of when the previous procedure has been completed.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that in drink there be first of all the juice of large onions, and pills cleansing the brain.
Then shave completely the head of the sick person and place upon his occiput an ointment made from henna described in the treatise on ointments, and place it often.
For this is the method of cautery; make that same one according to the order I mentioned there.
If therefore he is healed by it, it is good. If not: then make for him three cauteries on the back of his head, which shall descend from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye, and place between each cautery a thickness of a finger.
Then care for the cautery with it (the same as before).
If however you wish an addition and the sick person can bear it: then make a cautery in the middle. What if you wish an addition: then cauterize him over two horns (of the skull).
Then care for it until he is healed; let the cautery be anointed according to the shape that was mentioned before.
On the method of cauterization in paralysis and softening (of a hardened mass).
Chapter X.
It is necessary that you proceed with the cleaning of the head with onions, and as I have said.
Then shave the sick person's head; then cauterize it with a mid-head cautery, and with a cautery on every horn of the head, and with a cautery on the back part of his neck, and with three cauteries on the spine.
If you need softening of the body by more of these (cauteries), and the sick person can bear it and the ailment is strong: then cauterize him with four cauteries on the spine, and the last one with cautery until it burns most from his skin, and take care to spare the hand. Then care for himself until he is healed: and thus cauterize with oil.
On the method of cauterizing in epilepsy.
A epileptic is not cauterized, unless his epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore it is necessary that you first clean the brain of the patient with hyson, and with the rest of the treatment that we have said in the division: when the sick person is serious, or is tolerant in receiving medications.
If however the patient is a child who does not tolerate medications, then administer gargarisma and cleansing chews that clean the brain, before that for many days with good nourishment.
Then shave his head, afterwards cauterize it with a single cautery in the middle of the head as was previously mentioned, and also with another cautery at the back of his head, and over all the horn of his head with cautery. If the sick person is strong and tolerant, then cauterize him with cauteries as was said in the case of paralysis, and with softening of the body over vertebrae at the neck and vertebrae at the back: and let the cautery be oiled according to the method that has previously been mentioned.
If however the sick person is a child, then place a subtle cautery according to this method.
Chapter on the manner of cauterizing in Melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize it with Cauteries, as we have said in the one having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess of declivity towards melancholy, and there is a weak body wet, then give him in drink what purifies his brain, according to what has preceded in division: then shave the head of the sick one, and make afterwards a correctly made plaster (tortellum) from linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head: and the sick one sitting square should be held from all sides.
Then present the liniment. And it is more suitable from ancient sheep butter. And heat it over fire with a moderate temperature measurement, which the finger can tolerate when it is introduced into it. Then evacuate it in the middle of his head in a circle, and let it out until it cools down.
Do this to the sick one once a week with the rest of his good regimen, until he is cured.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small punctures in it, besides which hold the hand with the cautery: let it be smelling.
For this kind of cautery moistens the brain with its nature.
Then put a damp cloth soaked in butter or goose fat on it.
Chapter on how to cauterize in water falling on the eye.
Chapter XIII.
When you are informed of the beginning of water flowing into the eye through signs that I have said in the division, then begin and give drink to the sick one, with what purifies his head.
And keep him away from all humidity, and make him sit in a bath for several days in fasting.
Then command him to shave his head and to cauterize it in the middle of his own head. Then cauterize it on both temples with two cauteries, if there is no descent of water in both eyes at once; or from one side, if there is no watery discharge in one eye; and cut off all veins and arteries that are under the skin with the cautery; and let the cauteries be long in width equal to the temples; and avoid bleeding.
If you see something from it, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible; and I will come with wisdom, which is in the extraction of veins, and the cutting off of them, and precaution against bleeding.
And at times it is cauterized on the neck, under two bones, with two cauteries extended to their utmost limit.
Chapter on the ancient method of cauterizing in tears.
When the tears of the eyes are chronic and continuous, and are above the veins and arteries that are manifest on the outside of the head, it is verified that this is due to an excess of cold, phlegmatic humors; then cauterize with the same cautery as I described in the treatment of watery discharge, cauterize in the middle of the head with a single cautery, and on both temples with two cauteries, and on the neck under two bones with two cauteries. And if it requires additional treatment, then cauterize it on every side of the eye carefully with a small cautery at the end of the eyebrow.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in nose smell.
When you treat it (the ailment), as we said in the division, and medication does not improve it: then hurry, and give three nights of infirmocochie in drink; afterwards, shave its head, and cauterize it with a medium cautery, with an oily cautery. Then cauterize it with two small cauteries, on each eyebrow under the hair.
And protect from an artery, lest you cut it.
This is the form of the Cautery of Claw.
[Section heading] On the method of cauterizing in the softening of the Eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye softens due to illness or wetness: then cauterize the eyelid with a single cautery, with this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows with two cauteries in all places; and let them extend from both temples; and let the length of all the cautery be according to the length of the eyebrows; and do not place your hand with the cautery at its end, rather according to the amount that the third eyelid is burned.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing an eyelid when the hair points towards the eye and pierces it.
The cautery is in it according to two modes: either the cautery with fire; or the cautery with burning medicine.
In the cautery with fire, command the patient to release his hairs if they are from those who clean them, until they extend and match. If they prick him at the place of its emergence: then bind his eyes with ointment so that they do not move until it is born.
When they are born and match, then place the head of the patient in your bosom: then mark on the eyelids of his eyes with encaustum (hot wax), marking it in the shape of a myrtle leaf; and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs.
Then place a cotton soaked in egg white or slippery elm bark decoction over the eye.
Then heat the cautery, whose form is as follows:
Then cauterize gradually in several places on the skin whose surface has the shape of the myrtle leaf, appearing completely.
And your mark of health for the operation is that if you see the eyelids contract and hairs raised at the prick on the eye.
So lift up your hand then: and dismiss him for three days.
Then place cotton with butter over him until the eschar is healed. Then treat him with ointment until he is healed.
If any hair returns after an hour and softens the eyelid, then repeat the cautery on that place as you did before.
If the hairs are in the lower part: then cauterize it until the hair grows back to its own natural place and matches so that it does not prick the eye.
Inform the patient to shave, until they grow long and are even. Make from cloth a shape like a myrtle leaf.
Then take from known soap and un-soaked lime, one ounce of each, or approximately the same amount; then grind them together with good friction, and do it quickly so that it does not become cold. Then place it on the cloth that you have prepared in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and put it on the eyelid of one or both eyes. And place raw egg yolk that has been soaked under the eye, and let the head of the sick person be on your chest.
Place your index finger on the medicine and press it slightly. And you move it as often as the sick person feels the bite of the medicine, for its bite is like fire.
And when this bite that he feels persists, then release the medicine and move it with your finger. When the bite ceases, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And then observe whether the eyelid swells as it does when heated by fire or cut; if so, it is good: and if not, apply more medicine to the place where the medicine does not press and does not darken, until your operation is complete and the eye contracts.
Then put raw egg yolk with butter on it until the burnt skin is removed. Then treat him with diaphinicon ointment or another, until he is healed.
It is necessary for you to keep the final precaution during the operation, so that nothing from the medicine falls into the eye.
If the eyelid becomes soft after days and some matter falls into the eye from the hairs, then apply more medicine to that place which has become soft from the eyelid, just as you did at first. Then care for himself until he recovers.
This is the form of the myrtle leaf.
And know that human eyes vary in size and shape. Therefore, according to this, your consideration should be: and the path of righteousness for him who is devoted to this art should not be hidden.
Section on the method of cauterizing in lacrimal fistula.
When you treat a Fistula, and your treatment does not improve as we said regarding the division of diseases: then, it is necessary that you cauterize it in this manner.
Command the sick person to place his head in your lap, and let one of his servants hold his head like this, so that it is not moved or shaken with his own head.
Then place warm oil soaked cotton or slippery elm on his eye, then apply the hot cautery of this form.
Let it be concave like the shape of a vulture's feather quill from one end, and make the cautery in this manner: if you wish it to penetrate to the other end, and if you wish it to extend upwards in this way.
However, this concave shape is better for your work.
Then open the fistula if it is open and drain the pus from it, and cut out the fistula; and if it is not open, then open it and drain its pus.
Then place the cautery on it, which has been heated very hot.
And hold your hand near the cautery from the eye to the nose, so that your hand does not stray or shake the sick person; and place the cautery on the fat of the eye and destroy it.
If you reach the beginning of your cautery to the bone, it will be good. And if not: then repeat the cautery once or twice, as needed; and leave it for three days.
Then place warm oil with butter on it, and treat it with an ointment for healing, until it is healed.
If it has passed forty days and is not healed: then place a sharp corrosive medicine on it until the bone appears; and scrape it as it comes in its chapter (layer).
And there is another method of cautery for a fistula, which some early ones said. Direct yourself to the location of the fistula, and find it; then place a thin cannula therein: namely, a thin cannula with this shape. Pour a quantity of drachmas worth of molten lead into it, and hold your hand with good retention by the cannula, and let not the weak one be moved at all, so that the molten lead does not run or reach his eye.
It is necessary that you place a hot cloth over the weak one's closed eye in egg white or water.
For lead burns the location of the fistula and heals it by a marvelous cure.
If the fistula is healed together with what we said from cautery, and cure, that is good. If not, then it is necessary to make an opening in the nose and lead the fistula back to the course of the nose, as it comes to its own proper place.
Section on the method of cauterizing in fissures of the lips.
Multiple splits occur in the Lip, which are called Hairs, and especially in the lips of children.
When you treat these splits, as we have said in the division of diseases, and the cure does not help, then use a small cautery with a scalpel, according to this shape.
And let the concavity of it be according to the subtlety of the scalpel.
Then place it heated quickly into these splits, until the cautery reaches the depth of the splits.
Then take care of it with caustic, until it heals.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing an Oral Fistula.
When a boil occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth: then it produces pus and bursts; afterwards it becomes old, and pus runs, and it turns into a fistula: then treat it, and the cure does not help, then it is necessary to burn cautery according to its size, which can enter the fistula. Then insert it heated into the hole of the fistula, and hold your hand, until the iron heated reaches the bottom of it and its end: do this once or twice.
Then take care of it afterwards, with what we have said about the treatment, until it is healed.
If the pus is cut off and heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to expose the place, and remove the rotten bone according to what comes at its head.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing a Softened Gum and Tooth.
When the gum softens due to dampness and the teeth move, and it is treated with medicine but does not help; then place the head of the sick person in your lap.
Then place the cautery tool, whose shape will come later, on top of the tooth, and insert in it a heated cauterium quickly. Hold your hand briefly until the weak feeling of fire heat reaching the root of the tooth is felt.
Lift the cautery tool. Then repeat the cauterization several times, as desired.
Then fill the weakened mouth with water and salt, hold it for an hour, and then spit it out.
For a tooth which moves, its firmness is strengthened, the gums are softened, and corruption of moisture is dried up.
[Paragraph] On the method of cauterizing teeth in pain.
When the pain of a tooth is due to coldness or there is coldness within it, or worms, and treatment with medicines does not help: then use the cauterization in two ways: either the cauterization with butter; or cauterization with fire.
The cauterization with butter is as follows: take cow's butter and boil it in an iron cauldron or earthenware. Then take the cup and turn it over on top of the stitched edge. Then immerse it [the cup] in boiled butter: and place it on the painful tooth quickly, and hold it until it cools: then repeat it several times, until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, immerse wool or a cup in cold butter, and place it on the painful tooth: and place hot iron on top of it until the heat reaches the depth of the tooth's hollow.
However, cauterization with fire is to shape a brass or iron cannula. And let there be something of substance within his body so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the weak bone.
Then with the cautery, let its shape come: and place it on that tooth: and hold your hand until the cautery cools.
Do this several times, for the pain will be removed either on the same day or on another day.
And it is necessary that the weak bone be filled with good butter during the impression of the cautery and hold it for an hour: then spit it out.
And this is the shape of the cautery.
Cauterize with whatever end you wish, according to what is possible: and this is the form of the cannula.
Chapter on how to cauterize in blisters.
When blisters are caused by phlegm and cold humors, and they do not respond to digestion with medicines, and you wish a quick digestion: then with the hollow cautery shaped like this.
Having two open ends so that the smoke can escape from one end of the cautery: and place it hot on top of the boil once, and twice if necessary, until it reaches the depth of the boil.
If the ulcer is small: then place the cautery according to the size of the ulcer.
Then let it be for three days, and put on top of it a hot pot filled with butter, until what burned by fire is removed.
Afterwards, care for it with tooth ointment, until the form of the channel heals.

Chapter on the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When cold and many humidity occur in the stomach until it separates from its composition, catarrh multiplies towards it and continuous methods of treatment do not help; then it is necessary that the sick person lies down on his back, extends his legs, and his hands. Chapter on the method of cauterizing Epar (cold iron).
When there is pain in the liver due to coldness and dampness, or from large flatulence, until it exits from its natural exit of superfluous matter and the sick person recovers with what we have said and does not improve in that: then it is necessary that the sick person lies down on his neck, and marks with encaustrum three cauteries according to this shape, and the same size below Epar where the arm length reaches: and let the space between every cautery be the thickness of a finger: and let the cautery be according to the length of the body straight: and do not press your hand much with the cautery.
And let the size of what is burned be according to the thickness of the skin, without addition: and let the sick person stand on his feet.
If it is not standing, then let it lie, which already extends its legs, and raises its arms.
This is the form of cauterization.
And indeed it is possible for you to perform this cauterization with a small knife cautery when subtlety and wisdom are present with you in the art.
And beware that you do not overly proceed in cauterization so that the thickness of the skin is burned throughout, wherefore the body is burned entirely and reaches the bowels; because the skin there is delicate, know this.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing liver abscesses.
When it happens that there is a discharge, and you want to know if the abscess is in the flesh of the liver or its membrane: then if it is in the flesh of the liver, there comes a mild pain and heaviness without sharpness; and if it is in the membrane of the liver, with intense pain there is a severe sharpness; and you see now that the treatment of this person has exhausted the doctors.
Therefore the sick man should lie on his neck. Then shape the place of the abscess with a brazier; then light the cautery that resembles a rod. And this is its form. And cauterize it with a single cautery until the skin is burned entirely and reaches the membrane, until all pus comes out; then treat the person by means of treatment for discharges, until he is healed.
And it is not necessary to use this cauterization method, unless the zeal for the study of medicine prolongs one's life; and when these illnesses converge in one person with experience on occasion: then let him dare to perform such an operation.
But rather to abandon it, is better in my opinion.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing pleurisy.
The ancients said, cautery with the roots of Aristolochia for cold pleurisy according to this method. And it is, that you receive from the dry roots of Aristolochia (long ones), one longer root which is found among them, and let it be as thick as a finger. Then immerse it in oil, and light it on fire. Then cauterize with one cautionery where it is between the neck of the collarbone and the neck, and with two small cauteries below in the hollow areas near the area that is under the beard.
And with two small cauteries also where it is between the fifth and sixth ribs on the sides a little towards the back, and with one cautionery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three small cauteries from the back: one where it is between the scapulas (shoulder blades), and two from the sides of the chest, below, one where it is between the scapulas.
And you should not press your hand with the cautionery, rather it should be in open air to smell the skin.
And some of the ancients have said that there are men who use a cautery made of iron similar to a ray (probably a reference to a tool called radium), and heat it, and put it inside where it is between the ribs until they reach the abscess with it, and the pus comes out; as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
But in this perforation with cautery, there is fear that either the sick person dies immediately, or a fistula occurs at the site, which does not heal.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing the spleen, XXXII.
When you treat the illness of the spleen, as we have said in the treatment of diseases, and your treatment does not help, then there is a need for cautery on it according to three methods, which are all correct.
One (method) is to make three or four cauteries, by drawing them along the length of the spleen according to the shape of Epatis' cauterizations, whose preceding figure it is.
And let each cautery be of thickness equal to that of a finger, or more or less.
Let the method of cauterizing, which we mentioned in the cauterization of the liver, be done equally.
And do not press your hand with the cautery; let the patient be weak and lying on his back.
Another method of cauterization is: holding the cautery with two openings, as we said in the chapter on dislocation of the shoulder; and peel off the skin that is directly over the spleen, where the elbow of the weak left arm comes to; and your peeling should be in the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall along the length of the body.
Then insert two openings with very hot fire until it penetrates the skin from the other side; then remove the cautery; thus there are four cauteries.
And if you wish to cauterize using a cautery with three openings.
Then take care of the cautery after you release it, let it discharge pus for many days; for it is more effective than the rest that preceded in treatment.

The cautery does not fall in dropsy unless it is properly applied.

Then let the open cautery emit pus for a long time.
And do not evacuate the weak patient from treatment after cauterization with it: this should be done so that two intentions are gathered to him: and healing will hasten towards it with God's help.

When they suffer from hydrops and are filled with citrus water, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot in the nail area, which is between the earlobe and ankle; and hold the cautery with one hand and do not twist it; then remove your hand; and do not return to it at all.

Chapter on the method of cauterizing an anal fistula.
Chapter 38.
When the sick person does not obey the cutting and operation that we have described in its place, and is afraid of it, perhaps he will heal with cautery.
If an anal fistula arises and becomes inflamed, pus flows from it, and the surrounding tissues become corrupted (rotten). Therefore, as is fitting, it should be examined with a probe of fine thread. Then, recognize the depth of it with the probe.
Then heat the cautery which is similar to a rod. Then insert the heated instrument into the fistula up to the depth of the probe (clamp).
And repeatedly cauterize over it until all the corrupted tissues are burned away, once, twice, or three times, according to your need.
And be careful not to burn the nerve or large vein if it is there; or if the fistula leads to the bladder or the intestine, then be cautious in these areas.
Do not do this unless when the fistula is in a fleshy area; and reflect that it does not penetrate (pass through).
Then take care of the place until it heals.
If (the wound) is sealed and the matter within it is removed, and it remains in this state for a long time, then you will know that it has healed completely.
If the matter is not removed from it, then you will know that it is penetrating, or that the bone within it is rotten, or as if from one of those (things) whose memory comes to mind in its place.

Then mix that water with another lime: and boil it until it returns.

[Section heading] On the cauterization of back pain.
Sometimes pain occurs in the back due to many causes, either from a fall, strike, excessive evacuation, or similar things, due to the influx of cold and moist matter. And cautionery does not apply except in this single case, which is made by the influx of cold matter.

And the cauterization should be done with cauteriopuncti.

Chapter on the method of cauterizing in hump-like growths.
This illness often occurs in small children many times.

On the method of cauterizing in gout, and the pains of joints.
When the pains of joints are due to cold and moist humors which flow into any part of the body, then when such pains occur in the feet, it is proper for physicians to call it gout (Podagra).
Since gout caused by cold is treated with various methods of treatment and the pains are not removed, then cautery removes them.
And it is that one should cauterize it after evacuation around the joint of the foot, with many cauteries; and let the cautery be Oilburner.
And if you need to puncture the sole of the foot, then do it with a cautery point. If the pains rise up to the knees or other joints and it frequently happens so, then cauterize it over the whole knee with three or four cauteries from all sides, using this same cautery called Clauile.
If more than one cautery is required for you, then cauterize it. And do not immerse your hand with the cautery, rather let it be about as thick as the skin.
If the pains rise up to the knees and the back, then administer what was said in the chapter on it.
If the pains are only in the hands, then puncture around the knuckles, as if two lines were turned over.
If pain remains only in the fingers, then puncture them all, on every knuckle and on the back of the hand.
If the pains rise up after days to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize both from all sides.
And do not evacuate the weak from good management, from receiving medications. If good care is taken and phlegm is evacuated, it will be cured with God's help by means of this cautery.
On the method of cauterization for ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groins and the intestine or the scrotum descends, and it is beginning nearby: then one should order the patient to abstain from food on his own day. And let him use laxatives, so that he may expel feces from his belly.
Then let him sit on his back before you; and order him to hold his breath until the scrotum appears or the intestine does.
Then reduce him with your fingers and mark the place of rupture on his chest with hot wax, using a sign whose end is similar to the diameter of half a circle above his body.
Then heat the cautery of this shape until it becomes white and throw pieces of hot iron on it. Then return the intestine or scrotum to its hollow. Then let the servant place his hand on the place, so that the intestine does not come out; and you have already opened between the legs of the patient, and you placed a stone under him, and another servant is on his thighs, and another on his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery on the mark, with your hand holding the cautery upright. And hold him until you meet the bone with it; or use another place if you are not able to meet the bone with it until the bone.
And carefully observe the exit of the intestine at the hour of your cautery, so that you do not burn him and it comes over him, or he dies from it or suffers great harm.
And know that when you do not meet the bone with the cautery, your operation is of no avail.
And it must be a small, delicate cautery for children, according to their size.
Then treat with the remaining ointments until he is healed.
The patient lies down for forty days until the wound is sealed.
It is necessary that you place the nourishment for him according to the length of his treatment time, so as to soften his stomach; lest his intestines go out during attempts at evacuation and famine.
Then when he wishes to rise after forty days, then administer a well-made bandage and let him hold it for another forty days.
Let him be lessened in labor, and fullness of food and drink, and violent voices.
For when he uses this regime, thus is he cured with complete healing.
And I will say the cure for hernias with an incision in its own chapter.
When hernias occur in the rest of the abdomen and are beginning and they fear that they will increase, then cauterize the hernia with a round cautery according to its size; and let it be what is burned from that point on as one third of it. Then care for him as I have said; do not add to it.
And some of the first ones have said that the hernia should be cauterized with a triangular cautery in this shape.
After it is signed with pitch and a line is placed that is across its width on the upper side of the hernia, and another line downwards. And place your hand in the middle with the awl (clavius).
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing for pain due to a blow or impact.
Chapter XLVIII.
When pain occurs in some limbs due to a blow or impact; and the pain persists for a long time and there is no help with medications, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the puncture cautery.
And let the cautery be for every member, according to its size and its smallness, and its weakness, and its strength, and its location of twisting, and the pain from it.
If he is cured by the first cautery, it is good. If not: then repeat the cautery upon him.
Because it is customary for these pains to change from one member to another that is near it. Therefore, you must follow them with the cautery until the sick man is cured.
Chapter on the mode of cauterizing in Leprosy.
The leprous, however, are sometimes helped greatly by the cautery. And particularly the species of leprosy which is caused by putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy: when you consider the need to cauterize it.
If the leprosy is incipient and you have treated it as we said in the division, and it does not decrease nor cease: beware of the sick man, lest corruption spread over his entire complexion: then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head, known, and the second below it facing the forehead at the end of the hair, and two above the two horns, and one behind it over the nuchal bone of the neck.
And lay your hand with the cautery a little longer, until it makes an impression smaller than the palm in the bone, and the cortices will be displaced: so that the expiration of gross vapors from it may be alleviated, and cauterize the spleen also with the cautery according to what has preceded.
If the leprosy is already spread over the sick person and it is evident: then you must cauterize with these cauteries which we said in the head, and a cautery on the tip of the nose, and two cauteries on the two cheeks, and two cauteries on the spondyles of the neck, and six on the spondyles of the back, and one large one over the alhahosos near the gran caudae and one on it, in the almeidat: and two over the ankles: namely over every ankle with one, and two over the knees, and two over the shoulders, and two over the elbows, and two over the forearms, and two over the softnesses of the chest: and cauterize it over every joint of his fingers on both hands, and feet: and cauterize over all calcaneum of his feet, and focilia of his hands.
Beware that you do not burn the nerves which are on top of the last heel bone, so as not to burn them.
And sometimes it is cauterized with a cautery on the chin, and another time on the belly, and another time on the epigastrium.
And know that the more you add cautionary substances, the more beneficial it is, and the more conducive to success.
And know that the sick do not feel pain in cautery, as the healthy do; therefore, because his body is already numb.
It is necessary that the cauteries be of suitable size and shape according to the members and joints; accordingly, they should be made from a particular type of iron.
Then care for the cautery with flour of herbs mixed with honey, and the rest of the treatment until it heals.
Chapter on the method of cauterization in stupor (faint or delirium).
When any member becomes numb and is treated with medicines, oils, plasters, and yet does not heal, then the affected member should be cauterized with cauteries according to the size or condition of the member.
Let your cautery enter the thickness of the skin a little way. Then take care of it with an ointment until it heals.
Furthermore, when the cautery is applied to some numbness that happens in the hand and foot, in the joints of the back near the nerve exits that move that member, the numbness will be removed.
However, do not presume to act upon it unless he is wise in the knowledge of the structure of members and the exit of nerves moving the body.
Title LXI.

Chapter on Cauterization for Cancer.
When cancer is beginning and you wish to stop it: then cauterize it with a circular cautery around its circumference, as is customary.
Wise men have said, it should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle.
But that does not seem right to me, for I fear it would cause an ulcer; and I have already seen that happen several times.
It is rather right to cauterize around it with a circular cautery, as we have said; or with multiple cauteries.

Chapter on the method of cauterizing in a cancerous ulcer.
Chapter XXXIV.
Corrosion is only corruption walking in a limb and consumes it; just as fire consumes dry wood.
If you see a corrosion in a place that can bear cautery with fire, then apply much cautery, small and large nails, according to what suits the place where the corrosion is located.
Then cauterize it from all sides until you remove the entire corrosion, and nothing remains of it in depth.
Then leave it for three days, and place over the cauterized places ground sulfur with oil until all scabs are removed and all corrosion.
Then treat it with ointments that cause flesh to grow.
If therefore you see that after three days flesh is born through healthy growth, in which there is no corrosion, it is good.
And if not: then repeat the cautery over what remains from the corrupted places.
And corrosion is sometimes treated with a strong medicine. Indeed, it arises in the place of cautery.
However, cautery with fire is quicker in helping: and I myself have already said that the cauterization of it with a strong medicine is in the division; therefore take it there when you need it.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing nails and warts.
Chapter 50.
It often happens that this illness occurs in the lower parts of the feet and is bulky, filtered, which injures the foot.
Indeed, cautionery in these [cases] is according to two modes: cauterization with fire and cauterization with hot water.
As for the cautery with fire, it is made concave like a bird's feather; which should be made of iron, according to the size that contains the nail from all sides; and it should be thin on the edges.
Then place the hot iron on the nail. Then turn the hand with the hot iron around the nail until the hot iron reaches the depth of the nail; and let it be for three days, until it begins to emit pus. Then plaster it with wild herbs crushed with salt; and let the plaster remain on it at night. It will be uprooted from its roots.
Then treat the place with a good ointment for flesh until it is healed.
If they are not converted and often recur on the surface of the body, especially in hands and feet; then administer cautery with hot water: and it is, that you receive a cannula from brass, iron, or from an eagle's feather; and place it on the nail or ulcer. Then pour a small amount of hot water into the cannula; hold your hand and turn it with the pressure of your hand for a while, so that the tip of the cannula is pressed against the root of the nail, and let the hot water find its way to the depth, to the root of the nail: and let the patient wait for a short time on the bite of the hot water for one hour.
Then let it go, as the nail will be uprooted with its roots.
Do this to them one by one, until you have reached all who are affected by it in the body.
Then care for them after they have been uprooted, with that which generates flesh from ointments.
Chapter on cauterizing tremor.
When trembling happens to anyone in a nerve due to cold, or quartan fever, or something else: then it is necessary that you cauterize it with four or five cauteries on the dorsal vertebrae, and with a cautery between each vertebra, and with a cautery on its chest, and with a cautery on its stomach.
The trembling ceases with cauterization by oil, and hastens the health of cold sickness.

Chapter on the method of cauterizing in bleeding from an artery in a wound.
Many times there is bleeding from an artery which has been cut at a wound, which happens externally, or at the incision of an abscess, or cauterization of a member, and similar cases; and it is difficult to separate it.
Therefore, when it happens to someone, then you quickly go with your hand to the opening of the artery, and place your index finger upon it; and press strongly, until the blood is compressed under your finger, and nothing escapes from it.
Then place in fire a small oil lamp cautionery, and many of them more: and blow upon it until they become very hot.
Then take one of them, either small or large, according to the wound and place where the artery is broken, and place the cautionery upon the vein, after which you remove your finger quickly: and hold the cautionery until the blood is severed.
If it is expelled with the removal of your finger from the opening of the artery and you extinguish the cautionery, then take another cautionery quickly, from those which are prepared in the fire.
Therefore, do not stop doing that with one after the other until the blood is severed.
And beware, lest you burn the nerve that is there, and an additional harm falls upon the already weakened person.
And know that when blood flows from the artery, then it is not possible to sever it: particularly because the artery is large, unless with one of four methods. Or with a cautionery, as we said. Or with extraction, when it has not been extracted. For when it is extracted, the ends of it contract and the blood is severed. Or it is tied with a strong thread. Or medicines that have the property of stopping bleeding are placed upon it and it is compressed with a suitable tourniquet.
He who administers the amputation with a ligature and compression with cloth, or by placing hot things upon it and similar ones, does not give him completely, unless rarely.
If that happens to someone and the doctor is not present nor medicine: then let him begin with the position of the index finger upon the opening of the vein as we said, and compress it very strongly, until the blood is besieged from above the wound, and upon the artery. Do not remove the finger, upon it always apply cold water of violent coldness until the blood freezes and swells, and then cut it off.
And meanwhile consider what requires cautery or medicine in it.

Chapter on the treatment of water collected in children's heads.
Chapter 1:
Know that this weakness often occurs in children during childbirth: or when the midwife tightens the child's head without ease.
And also it sometimes occurs due to hidden causes which are not known.
And indeed I myself have not seen this illness in anyone but children: and to every one of them that I have seen death followed: for this reason it appeared to me that the operation should be abandoned in it.
And indeed I myself have seen a child whose head was filled with water and his head swelled every day until he could not sit on himself due to the size of his head: and moisture increased until he died.
And this moisture, it accumulates between skin and bone: or accumulates under the bone on the skull.
And the operation on him, if there is moisture between skin and bone, and an abscess is small, then it is necessary to make a crack in the middle of the head, one fissure in width: and the length of the fissure should be like two fingers, until the moisture runs out.
And this is the shape of an enostome (spatula).
If therefore the moisture has increased more and the abscess is larger, then place these two fissures, according to this shape.
And if the moisture is under the bone and its sign is that you see the openings of the skull everywhere: and water is pressed when you compress it with your hand towards the inside, and it does not hide from you: then it is necessary to make three fissures in the middle of the head, according to this method.
And after the incision, extract all the moisture entirely. Then tie the fissures with linen and wool threads. Then anoint it above with wine and oil until the fifth day.
Then remove the bandage, and take care of the wound with ointments.
And thou shalt not loosen to bind the head with equality. Feed the sick man with any dry food of slight moisture, until he strengthens the limb and is healed.
Another method of cutting is to consider where it appears that the abscess is in size, and the collection of water.
For sometimes it is in the occiput more, or in the head, or in the right, or in the left.
Then rise with cutting where it appears to you that there is an abscess and filling of water; and cut it, according as it is possible for you.
And observe that you do not cut an artery, and let blood flow, and the sick man dies from this flow along with the evacuation of moisture.
Chapter on the incisions of the arteries that are after the ears.
Chapter II.
When catarrh happens to someone's eyes or chest, and it becomes chronic and medical treatment does not help: then the last cure is in that, incision of these two arteries.
Therefore, when one wishes to cut them (the arteries), let the sick person shave his head. Then rub the place with a rough cloth, so that the arteries appear. Then let the sick person tighten his neck with any cloth he has. Then observe where the vein pulsates. And the places of both (arteries) are the places that are depressed behind the ears and rarely hidden except in some people.
Then mark both (arteries) with wax on each side and cut one on each side with a knife, the incision reaching to the bone, making it wide across the width of the head.
And if you wish, insert the knife under the artery and cut it above with an incision.
And let the length of the incision be like two fingers joined together.
For when a vein is cut, blood flows out with a pulsating exit, which leaps to the inner parts with frequent jumps.
If the artery does not appear to the sight, then it is necessary that the measurement of space from the ear should be three fingers in width. Then mark with wax and cut through to the bone.
And what must be expelled from blood is about six ounces and perhaps you will expel more or less from it. All of this should be done according to the quantity that appears to you from the strength of the sick person and the filling of his artery.
Then observe for a wound. And if there remains some flesh on the bone after the wound, then cut it so that an abscess does not form; then bind the wound with linen rags.
Then take care of it with an ointment until it heals.
On the Extraction of Arteries which are in the Temples.
Third Chapter:
When an old hemicania or acute catarrh occurs in a man due to acidulous humidities and warmth in the temples, or an old soda, violent, and similar: and it is treated with methods of curing medicine, but it does not improve: then we are experienced in these illnesses in the extraction of arteries from the temples, or cauterization of them, as we have told.
And the method of operation for their extraction is that the sick hairs which are on the temples are shaved off, and he should direct himself to the appearing artery in the temple. Itself is shown to you by its pulse, and it seldom hides except in a few men or extreme coldness.
If it is hidden to you, then the sick man should press his head with any cloth of his, and then rub the place with a rough cloth. Or apply heat to the place with hot water, until it appears to you in a clear manifestation. Then take the cannula, which I have prepared previously. Then burn away the skin with it easily, until you reach the artery. Then insert the hook into it, and pull it out upwards until you pull it out of the skin, and make it come out from all sides through the layers that are under it.
If, however, the artery is delicate: then roll it up with the tip of the hook. Then cut the part according to its length so that its ends are drawn together and contracted, and there is no blood flow. For if it is not cut and separated, the blood does not rise up deep within.
Then let six ounces of blood flow out, up to one-third.
If the artery is large: then it must be tied in two places with a double thread, strong, of silk; or with alum threads, so that decay does not occur near it before the wound is healed, and there is no blood flow.
Then cut the surplus which is between two ligaments. Do this at that hour, or another hour.
And if you wish, cauterize it with a cautery up to the bone, with a knife-shaped cautery, until its edges are cut through and it remains in place for this same operation.
And it is a better procedure unless the patient has a fever or is affected by calefaction. Because the cautery is made of those things which help to end moisture. Therefore it is better as a remedy.
And after the extraction of the arteries, it is necessary that the place be filled with cooked old material; and pulverized lice should be placed on top of it evenly.
And after the dissolution (of pus or inflammation), it is to be cured with dry medicines which cause new flesh to grow, and with linen, until it heals.
If during the operation, bleeding occurs from an artery, then hasten to cut it off with a cautery, or fill the place with alum; and press your hand until the bleeding stops. If there is nothing available to you from those things (to stop the bleeding), then place your finger on the place until it becomes frozen. And irrigate the place with water of intense cold, until the pain subsides and it is bound according to what is necessary.
And from what is lighter and easier to extract, it is that you cauterize the vein with this cautery having two knives; and let the sharpness of the two knives be similar to alum. Nevertheless, they are much less sharp than two knives. Because if they are as sharp as two knives, cold should be applied to each; and they will not cut through the flesh quickly. When there is a certain amount of swelling in them, heat from fire should be applied and the flesh should be quickly cut off: when this operation is needed, it is better than any other work, and easier and less laborious.
And this is the shape of the cautery.
The space between the two knives should be the size of a finger's width after you mark two locations with pitch; then place both heated [instruments] closely, until they reach the bone and cut the vein in two places: so that what is between the extremities may be removed. They do not fully coagulate with this cautery.
Chapter IV.
Chapter on the care of chronic, acute tear ducts from the eyes.
When the tears are chronic and there is a channel from the veins that are on the outside of the skull of the head; and if no medication for healing is applied to them with medications, then you will see the face of the sick person becoming red, and it feels like walking as ants do on the forehead: and the eyes are weakened, moist, so that the hair has already been corroded by the corrosion: and the eyelids have been heated due to the sharpness of the tears: then the ancients resorted to this treatment for them, and they called it a cure with a knife.
And you should advise the sick person to shave the hairs on his forehead. Then make three incisions on the forehead equal in length to the forehead; and let the length of the incision be like two fingers, and let one incision be at the same level as the nose in the middle of the forehead, and the second one slightly below the movement of the arms, and the third one on the other side: and avoid cutting the arteries that are on the sides; and stretch your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and let the space of all incisions be the size of three joined fingers: and prepare a piece of sponge or dry cloth with which you can absorb blood.
Then insert a probe with two sharp ends, which follows this form. From the incision on the side of the temple, up to the second incision: excise along with it all the skin that is between the two incisions, together with the sifac which is above the eye. And place the sharp side of it towards the attached flesh with the skin, and the blunt side towards the bone; and push it in until it reaches the midline; and cut along with it all the contents that descend from the head to the eyes, except that it is connected by an incision up to what appears on the skin.
Then do the same in the midline up to another fissure.
And when an equal amount of blood flows out, squeeze the places from the clots of congealed blood.
Then place a linen cloth from an old garment into every fissure and place over them pledgets soaked in wine, oil or vinegar. And see to it that no hot abscess occurs.
And on the third day, loosen the ligature and administer a large infusion with warm water. Then care for it with basilicon ointment, and the other remedies used for wounds until it heals.
Chapter 5.
Chapter on the treatment of sharp tears and catarrhs of the eyes from the inner parts of the head.
When sharp, acute, frequent catarrhs occur to someone; and you see the eyes of that person weakened, small, and already the appearance is diminished; and the eyelids are ulcerated, hairs fall out from them, and in the depth of the head there is severe pain, which hurts, and sneezing follows: then take from these symptoms, that those substances, and catarrhs do not come unless from many veins.
A better treatment for them is this one. And it should be ordered that the sick person shave their forehead. Then make a single cut in the middle of the forehead or slightly less wide, and start with the cut from the left temple to the right temple; let the incision go as far as the bone; and move your hand away from the temples that are moved during chewing until the bone is exposed; then dry up all the blood with a sponge.
Then separate the edges of the wound with spatulas or linens. Then pull together with sutures and soak the sutures with wine and oil to prevent a hot abscess from forming.
And when you loosen that (the suture), and see that a hot abscess is beginning to subside; then it is necessary to scrape the bone until flesh begins to grow in it.
Then care for the bone with dry dressing to make flesh grow; as if you take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of pitch, prepare a plaster from it and administer it for the growth of flesh in these wounds.
Chapter 6.
[Section title: Treatment for injury to the ear]
Everything that falls into the ear is one of four kinds: either it is a mineral stone, or resembling a stone such as iron and wax; or it is from a plant, like chickpea and beans; or it is fluid, like water, vinegar, and similar things; or it is an animal.
When therefore a stone falls into the ear or any other kind of stone that does not grow in the ear, expose only the ear: if you see a stone then pour something from violated oil or sisamo into the ear. Then administer the extraction of it and make him sneeze with a snuff containing catharpic herbs, and close the nostrils near the onset of sneezing, when you place around the ear fragments from cloths or wool, and stretch the ear upward.
For many times it comes out with this care.
If it does not come out, then administer the extraction of it with Guesthwi, that is, finely ground pigeon droppings; its form is as follows.
If it comes out with guesthwi, it is good.
And if not, then administer the extraction of it with a fine blind hook few times.
If it does not come out through that, then make a tube from copper and introduce the end of the tube into the ear opening as much as possible, and close what is around the tube with beeswax softened with oil so that there is no way for the wind except the tube; then extract it with your strong suction.
For many times it comes out with what I have said. If it does not come out this way: then take from helkalimb or urine, that is gluten prepared as birds are caught, a small amount; and place it at the end of the radius when you place a well-centered cup over it; then introduce it into the ear opening with ease after you have pulled the ear away from moisture.
If it does not come out with all that I have mentioned, then hurry to cut, before a hot abscess or a spasm occurs.
The method of lancing is as follows: first, the unwell person should be lanced in the head; and extract from him according to the strength of the phlebotome. Then make the sick person sit between your hands, and turn his ear upward, and make a small incision in the base of the ear at the fat in the depressed place; let the incision be in the shape of the moon until you reach the stone; then remove it with what is possible for you with your tools.
Then lance the incision from your own time and take care of it until it heals.
If something falling into the ear is one grain or more, which swell and grow; then administer its removal.
But if it does not obey you for the evacuation, then take a thin, subtle probe according to this shape.
And administer with it the cutting of that species from grains which fall into the ear, and do not do this when you think that the grain is already wet by earwax, until you put a lot of it; then remove it with forceps or with a fine probe or with suction, as we said, for the extraction of it is alleviated.
In water that enters the ear, the sick person should use sneezing when he first lies down; and his ear has already been filled with some cooked old one; it is lying on top of it where the water is. If it comes out through this, it is good.
If not, then take many small stones according to the length of the finger, soft and smooth, and heat them slightly with fire; and the sick person should insert one from these into the ear's opening; and let him sprinkle water on one foot from that side, and strike the stone in the ear with another stone. Therefore, it should not cease to be done with the stone and the stone, until all the water comes out.
And now the water is coming out so that you may take one from parchment or reed and insert its end into the ear; and heat the other end with fire until it burns most of it. Then take another reed and do the same thing many times until all the water comes out; and draw it out with a cannula according to what was stated above concerning the stone.
In the case of an animal entering into it (the ear), if its body is small, like a louse or similar, care for it as I said in the section on division.
But if it is of a large body, which appears to the senses: then administer its extraction with tweezers and hooks; and its removal is easier for all those who are holding onto the ear.
In the case of worms generated in the ear, when you care for it with what I said in the section on division and in the treatise on distillations, and your treatment does not help: then you should look at the ear in sunlight. If therefore something appears there from worms, then draw it out with tweezers or fine hooks.
If nothing appears there, then take a cannula with this shape: narrow below and wide above; and insert its fine end into the ear according to the amount that the sick person can tolerate; then suck with strong suction. Do it many times until all worms come out.
If they do not obey you for their exit, then use poppy seeds surrounded by a cannula with wax as I said in the stone.
If they do not come out with what I said: then administer the distillations that the ancients were experienced in for the destruction of worms; and you will find it in the treatise on distillations.
And let your drainage be with oil and medicine into the ear using this instrument, whose shape is depicted here. As you see, make it from silver or brass, narrow at the bottom with a small hole, and wide at the top.
Therefore, let what is within the concavity of the tube (cannula) be made of brass. And if you wish, take radium (a heated metal) and wrap it at the end with a suitable covering; then pour oil, juice, or any of these medicines into the cannula; let it be in the ear; then introduce the heated radium with the covering on top, and press it gently with your hand until the oil is forced out into the concavity of the ear, and the sick person feels it inside; and whatever is poured into the ear should already have been slightly heated by fire. And take care that no substance distilled in it is very cold; medicines cannot tolerate this.
Chapter VII.
