[Chapter title] On the treatment of a perforated ear.
Whenever some infants are born from their mothers' wombs without being perforated.
And it also happens to some people that the perforation of the ear occurs from a wound or tissue born in it.
And this perforation sometimes occurs in the deep part of the ear canal, which does not affect vision; and sometimes it occurs near the outer part of the ear canal and affects vision.
Therefore, the one that occurs in the deep part of the ear, which does not affect vision, is difficult to cure in many cases.
And in the one that affects vision, it is necessary to place the sick person's ear on the sun and observe it; then if you see the perforation, open it with a fine spatula whose shape is as follows: its end should have a small notch, part of which is sharp; the rest of the spatula should be flat on both sides to avoid damaging the ear.
If therefore an opening is born from the flesh within the ear: then hold it with a delicate hook, and cut it with great force, until all the flesh is removed.
If therefore an ulcer is deep within the ear: then take a thin probe, soft and warm it slightly with fire; then insert it into the ear.
If therefore you find an ulcer accompanied by weakness and difficulty of hearing: endeavor to open it with ease; but be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear.
Then place a linen cloth of the size of the opening you have made in the ointment of Egypt; do this for several days until you are certain that the wound has healed.
Or take linen and immerse it in rosewater, powderize upon it the ground zinc, and use it.
If you see the ear already discharging pus: then extract the linen and allow it to dry with another piece of linen which has been soaked in a pot made with rose oil, until the warm pus settles; then take care of it until it is healed.
If bleeding occurs: then immerse sponge or cloth in cold water and place it over the ear; and use the rest of the treatment to stop the described bleeding using methods of distillation.
Chapter on the care of Althaea's (Marsh-mallow) eyelids.
Chapter VIII.
Those Althaea's which occur on the eyelids of eyes, are sometimes moist and sometimes dry.
Therefore they should be held with tweezers or with a hook, and cut from their roots. Then apply ground zinc on the place.
If blood flows from them, then cauterize with a fine lens-shaped cautery.
And it is better to cauterize [the wound] after making an incision. For many times they come back when something remains from their roots. And when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
Chapter on the care of the eyelids of the eye.
Chapter IX.
Often something happens in the eyelids that resembles sand in its firmness and hardness, and it is called gravel due to this. And it is an accumulation of thick moisture in the upper eyelid and the lower eyelid.
Therefore, the operation for this is to see if there is gravel proceeding from it, which appears in the eyelid, and to move it around in all parts, and its nature is easy.
Find therefore a fissure over it in length. Then scrape it off from all sides with ease, until it comes out. Then hang it up with a hook and cut it off itself.
If however you do not prepare to cut it off unless after you have pierced the eyelid with a slight incision, then it may harm the weak in some way.
If however there is a large fissure: then bind it up with suture: and care for it until it heals.
And if it is small, no harm will come to you from that. Oil therefore restores it and fills it in.
If the gravel is directed towards the inside of the ear and turned on the inner surface, then turn the eyelid over, hang the gravel with a hook: besides which you will need an incision, and press it from all sides.
If the eyelid is stretched by an incision, then it will not harm anything.
Then clean the eye after the gravel incision with salty water, and care for the place with it until the weak heals.
[Title: On the Care of Eyelids.]
Chapter X.
The adhesion (Axirnath) is a deposit that is generated in the outer layer of the upper eyelid; and it most certainly occurs in children; and it weighs down their eyes, and they get cataracts in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun, because tears flow towards them, and because of this you see them lying on their faces constantly, and they sleep on these, and their eyelids are always wet under the eyebrows, which has already been covered by swelling; and the appearance of Axirnath is visible to the eye, and when you press the place with your fingers, you feel the Axirnath among them.
The method of its operation is that the sick one places his head in your armpit.
Then take a clean cloth and prepare within it linen, and make from it a circle according to the size that contains Axirnath on all sides. Then place him upon it and press with your fingers from all sides, so that the Axirnath is gathered in the middle of the circle.
Then find in the middle of this humidity with a blunt probe producing cracks along its width, and let the crack not be larger than that which is made during venesection in depth.
Or it is necessary that you find the entire skin until you reach Axirnath, for in many dispositions, the Axirnath proceeds from the crack according to the shape of a fatty white peach pit.
So draw it out with the cloth that you have moistened between your fingers on the outside; and you shall turn your hand from right to left until it is dispersed; be careful not to add in the crack so as not to reach with the probe to the eye, and do not harm it.
If it does not appear to you at first that the Axirnath is in the crack, you should gently add more in the crack until the Axirnath comes out. Then draw it out as we said before.
Then immerse the cloths in vinegar and water, and place them on the spot and press with small stones.
And among men there are those who grind salt, and they place it in the hollow of the crack, so that what remains from that moisture softens.
Then care for it until it heals.
If there occurs in the spot an abscess that is hot, then care for it with soothing plasters until it heals.
Part on the methods of A taximir eyes, that is, when the eyelid becomes soft, so that it droops as it should not.
Chapter XI.
When hairs grow in the eyelids over and above the course of natural hairs, and become old: then they harm the eye, and bring about types of diseases, such as constant tearing, softening of the eyelids, and clouding, until that cause results in the destruction of the eye.
And Ataxmir indeed is cured according to four modes. Or by cautery with fire. Or with sharp medicine, according to what was mentioned in the chapter on cautery. The sentence translates to: "It is treated by incision and suturing (of) Ataxmir. "Or by cannulas, as I shall say.
"It is necessary that you place the head of the sick (person) in your lap. "Then turn the eyelid of the eye with your left hand.
"Therefore, if it is turned (back), it is good. "And if not: introduce the needle into it (the eyelid), where there is a thread from its lower part of the eyelid, and let the needle penetrate through the thread above, and let it be near hairs themselves or close to the margin of the eyelid, where hairs grow: and pull the thread upward with the eyelid, and turn it with the rod.
"Then find (the) conjunctiva on the inside of the eyelid, under added hairs, where the spatula meets from the greater lacrimal to the lesser lacrimal.
"Then extract the thread and place a small amount of cotton or cloth under the eyelid; then mark the eyelid with wax, so that it is like the figure of the leaf of myrtle.
"However, it is necessary that the figure be made according to the size and elevation of the eyelid: because it varies greatly among humans.
"For there are those who need to be cut according to the size of the eyelid, in accordance with the softening (of) the eyelid.
"Then with the spatula find (the) two lines that you have marked, and start from the greater lacrimal to the lesser lacrimal, and let there be a split near natural hairs, as the thickness of a rod.
"Then insert the hook into one (of) the two angles of the skin. "Then scrape it completely. "Then join the two lips with a suture using a sharp needle and thin woolen thread; remove blood and make the excess from the threads adhere to the eyebrows, if you want to do this: and if not, do not treat it.
Then let the suture go and the threads until three days, or four: afterwards take care of it.
And if you wish, let the wound heal without suture, and take care of it so that it dries and contracts. For the eyelid is to be raised during sealing of the wound and its dressing; but it will be better in future.
This method of healing they taught, the ancients.
Yet there is concern for the sick one in it, and it is from a good operation, and there is no fear in it.
And another method is also in Ataxmir: and it is to make signs on the eyelid with a shape like that of a myrtle leaf, as we have told before.
Then lift the eyelid with three separated or joined uncini, according to the following shape, then cut what is excessive with small forcipes according to this shape, with equal incisions.
If it is not possible for you to hold the uncinus, and it does not match; then take a needle with thread, and insert it in the middle of the shape: and insert another thread near the larger tear duct, and another thread near the smaller tear duct: and bind threads between your fingers with equal tension.
Then lift your hand equally with the lever: and lift the skin over which the incision is made, as we have told before.
Then bind together the two lips of the wound with suture: and take care of it until it heals.
If however an abscess occurs at your incision or split; sew up the abscess with wax and similar materials from soothing ointments.
And sometimes the eyelashes also turn over.
Therefore, it is necessary to use what we have said in the incision: but suture for both is more artificial. Treatment for Ataxmir with dogs.
It is necessary to turn the eyelid and make a cut along the inner fissure, as I have previously described. Then, using skill, make two small dogs or thin sticks of such length as that of the eyelid and narrower than the distance between the teeth; and you have already made incisions at both ends near where the sutures are located on either side.
Then gather both together with finesse on that which projects from the eyelid of the eye, and bind two small dogs tightly from either side with a strong ligature, and leave it for several days. For the contracted skin will die, darken, and rot until it falls off by itself.
If it slows down (the dying process), then make incisions with scissors. Then take care of it until it heals.
When it has solidified, lift the eyelid and do not pluck out the hairs.
And this is the shape of two dogs which you will make according to this form and size in length and width.
Chapter 12.
On plucking out hairs that are pricking in the eye with a needle.
The operation is to take a fine needle and thread a thin silk filament through it gently. Then gather the ends of this together and tie both with a very fine knot; let the length of the filaments be one palm.
Then prepare another thin silk filament shorter than the first and tie its ends if you wish.
Place the patient's head on your lap and let it be close to the sun so that the operation can be seen; because this is a subtle or small operation.
Then insert the needle with the thin silk into the root of the eyelid and make it penetrate quickly into the eyelid until you pull out the natural hair from above.
Then pull out the needle above the aneurysm and insert it into the aneurysm. If there is one, or two, or three, do not more than that.
Then draw your hand with it, until the needle comes out with the aneurysm along with the natural hair of the eyelid.
If the aneurysm is drawn out and the needle does not come with it: draw the aneurysm downwards with the thread you have made in it, until the aneurysm comes out through the upper opening, and you see it with the eye. Then draw out the aneurysm and the thread, and remove both, and close the eye; and let it remain closed for two or three days, until the hair grows back to its place, and flesh grows over it.
If the hair is short, then attach a long hair from the natural hairs and draw it out with it; or let it be until it grows longer, and then draw it out.
Chapter 13.
When this Xanthema happens to the eye, it is called Leporina.
And this Xanthema is either natural or accidental.
Therefore, the accidental one results from the consolidation of a wound, a cut, a cauterization, and similar things.
And the method of treatment is to find the consolidated area and separate its lips, and place a linen cloth in it, and tie it until it heals.
Do not use on its treatment things that dry and constrict it; for if you do so, the Xanthema will return worse than before; rather, use things that soften it, such as fenugreek; and embrocation with water in which althea has been boiled, with flaxseed; and unguento dyaquilon, which has been made liquid with some oil; and anoint with this linened cloth and treat with it.
Thy treasure of cure is that thou strive with all thy wit, so that it not be consolidated, according to the form which it was firstly.
This operation indeed that I said is no more than a correction of Alzahrak, so that the form of the place does not return to what it was altogether.
On the care for Alzahrak in the lower eyelid, and it is a wrinkle or contraction upward towards right and left.
Chapter XIII.
This that is below, is that which is truly named Alzahrak. And it is natural, and it is accidental.
And the accidental arises from wound, or split, or cautery, and similar things.
And the way of operation in it is that thou takest a needle, in which there is double thread, and thou dost anoint it with flesh, and maketh it penetrate from tear-duct left to tear-duct right, until the thread cometh at two extremities of the flesh.
Then extend the flesh upward with a needle, and cut it with a wide knife. If therefore the form of the eyelid returns as it ought to be, that is good.
And if not, take a cautery, and place it in the split, and turn with it the eyelid; and make two splits on the inner side of the eyelid, and let them be extremities of two splits from two corners of the cut, until they come together and make an angle: until when they are gathered together, this figure is made, and it is the letter lambda (λ) Greek.
Then remove that flesh by measure, which is its acute lower side, from that which follows the eyelid. Then gather together the separated parts; or it with thread of wool.
Then take care of them with what we said about softening medicines and liniments until they heal.
If Alxatrati occurs from a fissure, and suture or cautery: then it is necessary to clean the fissure flat under eyelashes, as previously described. Then separate with a linen cloth, as we have said.
The summary of the treatment for Alxatrati, whether it is above or below, is to perform the operation according to how it is prepared in the form of Alxatrati.
For it has many variations in shape: and the skillful craftsman prepares his intellect with whatever method is possible for him, so that he may return the figure to its natural form or close to it, and the sick person himself, according to what suits him from the operation and instruments in various positions.
Chapter XV.
Chapter on the adherence of the eyelid with conjunctiva or cornea.
Sometimes this consolidation happens to many people, so that the upper eyelid adheres with whiteness of the eye and prevents it from performing its natural operations.
Therefore, you should insert the tip of the rod under the eyelid and push it upwards: or extend it with a hook: then cut the adhesion with a thin spatula without sharpness, but rather slightly blunt: so as not to disturb the sick one during the operation, and remove the spatula, and harm the eye with its sharpness: and your incision should be like you peel off that adhesion with ease, until when the eyelid returns to its natural form, and the adhesion is healed completely.
Then pour salty water into the eye, while washing it with water: or drip it onto him from a syringe made of sheep's horn, or from vinegar diluted with water.
Then separate the eyelid from the eye with a linen cloth: and put wool soaked in egg white over the eye: and after three days, use vinegar, and with solidified substances, until it is healed.
Chapter on the Incision of the Toenail and Protrusion of Skin around the Eyes.
Chapter XVI.
Know that the toenail is in two ways. Or it is horny and is like a hard shell, subtle. Or it is not horny, similar to frozen white moisture: which when touched with iron or attempted to be picked up with a hook, is cut off and the hook does not stick to it.
And neither of these types starts unless from the greater tear duct, until it gradually reaches the eye, covering it and preventing light, and moving the eye.
And the method of operation in the incision is: that the sick person places his head in your lap. Then open his eyes and raise the eyelid with your hand. Take a few of the nails with a small forceps and extend it towards the upper part. Then take a point and insert it into the hair of horse, ox or sheep; let it be a thread, and slightly sharpen the tip of the needle and fasten it in the middle of the nail; push it with the needle and tie the nail with the thread, and extend it towards the upper part; scrape off the side of the nail following the pupil, as if you were holding it with the hair up to its end.
Then cut the remaining part at the root of the lacrimal duct with a thin spatula or with small forceps; and let the natural flesh of the lacrimal pass through, so that not due to the incision there is a continuous flow of tears.
And when the nail extends with a nail pick only; or with thread, as we said. Then it is scraped with a soft spatula, whose form this is.
And be careful that the spatula does not touch the corneal membrane and there is a rupture, and the pupil is pierced through.
Then after the incision, throw something crushed salt or made from snow into the eye and let it remain until another day. Then care for it with what is necessary, until it heals.
If the nail is not nerve-related and you cannot insert an awl into it or a pick does not fit into it, then this type of nail is frequently treated with medications and heals as I said in the division.
If you want to cut it, then open the eye of the sick person and take a thin, soft, fragile spatula with blunt end, according to this form. And smooth down the nail with a razor of fine sharpness. If you see that it thickens and cracks, and the razor presses into it, then pour snow made from your snow or red snow or crushed salt onto the eye and cover the eye until another day.
Then repeat the operation until the entire thing is removed. Unless it is a warm abscess in your eye; then let that be and treat the abscess until it heals.
Then repeat the operation on it with a razor until it heals.
Prominence of the tear duct (lacrimal caruncle), if it causes great harm to the eye, should be suspended with a hook and a portion of it cut off; not at the very end, so as to avoid damage to the tear ducts.
Then drain the pus from the tear duct (lacrimal) or make it red (rubefy), or apply a mustard poultice until it heals.
Chapter on incision of Alguardenic and the flesh born in the eye.
Chapter XVII.
When the red flesh is born in certain human eyes, composed or superimposed, until it covers the pupil, approaches, or contracts over the eyelids and perhaps turns the eyelids toward the outside; it resembles a balaustine rose.
And there is also an operation for this: that you place your head on your shoulder. Then open the eyes of this person and collect the entire flesh with appropriate hooks; hold it with a single forceps or tweezers.
Then cut the flesh at first until you finish the whole thing with a knife. And be careful not to harm the eye during the operation; make your cut be such that you cut it (the flesh), or with a spatula, as we said in the incision of the nail; or with small forceps, as used for collecting scabs, according to what shape it will take after this chapter.
When your cut is completed and the entire Alguardenic is removed, then fill the eye with crushed salt; or pour in red powder and similar to it from corrosive medicines; place a piece of cow's fat on the outer eye with egg white: to protect it from hot infection.
If there remains anything of Alguardenic and hot blood dominates you, and you fear a hot abscess; then let the eye be, and treat the abscess with what calms it.
Then repeat the procedure over him until he is healed.
And likewise do with the added flesh that occurs in the eye of this type.
However, it is necessary that all weak eyes, whether from natural causes or accidental ones, be treated with the iron: and do not introduce your hand into any of these operations until you see that the limb can bear this operation.
Chapter on removing a Sebula from the eye.
Chapter XVIII.
A sebula is a red vein that covers the eye and prevents the operation of sight; and it weakens the eye day by day.
Therefore, first you must determine if the eye in which there is a sebula is strong and there is no other illness besides the sebula; then remove the sebula from it.
And it is to be ordered that the weak one should put his head in your lap.
Then suspend the veins with a single hook or two according to your discretion; and let the hook be fine of double thickness, in this shape, or let there be two hooks in one body, in this shape.
Then remove the veins with fine forceps with precision and let the blood be drained an hour after an hour until you see the veins removed from the eye and resolved; and be careful not to harm the eye with the points of the forceps.
Let your work be done at midday under the sun, and let you be very firm in your operation; so that you do not cut except the veins themselves.
And when you have finished, then pour into the eye either green or red; so that its sharpness may burn what remains of the sebula.
If it is not possible for you to remove it all in that hour, then cover the eye with plaster, so as to ease the pain of the eye; and leave it for a few days until the pain subsides; and apply heat to it; then repeat the procedure according to the same method until healed.
And this is the form of the forceps.
Of the Reduction of a Sore Nasal (Nasal Abscess).
Chapter XIX.
The surgeon named Arisatha treats a fistula, which he cures with a cautery or with medicine burning sharply, according to the account that precedes it.
And if it is not cured, then there is no skill in it: except to open an abscess at its birthplace, and draw out all the moisture that is in it and pus, until the bone is exposed.
When the bone is exposed and you see corruption or blackening in it, then scrape it with an instrument that has this shape.
It is called the scraper of the skull.
Make it from iron indo and let its head be round like a compass (azir), with tiny holes made by the grinding of a file or a fine, pointed tool: place it on the corrupted part of the bone.
Then turn it with your fingers and press your hand slightly, until you know that the corruption has been scraped away: do this several times.
Then restore the place with dry, astringent medicine.
If the place consolidates and flesh grows up there, and the flow of pus ceases: and it remains for forty days without being renewed or abscessed, and no incident occurs in it: then you will know that it is cured.
And if not, then there is no skill in it, except to reduce the fistula to the nostril opening, according to this shape.
And it is to expose the second bone with iron or with sharp medicine: when the bone is exposed, then take a trephine according to this shape, its tip should be triangular and iron at the end: and the wood of the trephine should be extended like a pyramid until the end, as you see.
Then place it on the bone itself: let it be close to the tear duct, and extend your hand slightly from the eye. Then turn your hand with the lancet until it penetrates the bone and feels weak. By this you will find air escaping from it when you hold your hand over its nose.
Then restore the place with drying medications, as I have taught you.
When the flesh is born and the place hardens, then the matter that flowed outward returns to the nose; therefore it becomes lighter above the weakened (wound).
Chapter on reducing protuberance of the Eye.
Chapter XX.
When the eye protrudes completely and no visual harm or diminution occurs, then it should be softened; then use a phlebotome on it; afterwards place fumigating vapors on the neck without making incisions, but with suction.
Then place over the eye a poultice made from acacia, aloe, myrrh and saffron. Then compress the eyelid tightly above with plaster containing many small lumps.
And the method of small lumps is to take soft cloths, many, and cut all the cloth into four equal pieces; make many from them; then place one over another according to the quantity required by the eye; then compress strongly upon them with a strong bandage.
And repeat this fumigating vapor with suction but without incision.
Then remove the fumigating vapors and allow the eyelid to remain closed during the day and night.
If the bandage becomes soft again, then it should be tightened very much; then remove the bandage after a day and night, as previously mentioned.
If you see the eye has returned to its normal state, that is good; and if not, then repeat the plaster, small lumps, tightening bandage, and fumigating vapors until it heals.
On the incision of the empty bladder.
Cum in urinando, si vis inspexeris
If you observe urination and it breaks, then a bladder stone is emitted outside the eyes like a grain of sand and it spoils human form due to this, and the urge to cut it arises: then operation on him is performed as I have told, and it is, that you insert a probe from the base of the bladder from below towards the upper part.
Then insert another probe with a double thread from the lachrymal side and make it penetrate, and release the first probe according to its position.
Then cut the place of the double thread and bind a part of the bladder around the probe with it and tighten it much.
Then remove the probe, and place wool soaked in oil over the eye and let it go until the thread comes out with the bladder.
After that, take care of the eye with something that comforts it, until the wound heals.
And sometimes the bladder is tightened all around with a bandage of cloth until the eye protrudes greatly.
Then it is perforated with a fine spatula that reaches to the depth of the eye, and moisture of the conjunctiva is let out and the eye descends, and enters immediately; then bind it until it heals.
On the treatment of Alopecy.
Cum uir aliquis aetas uigilet
This disease that is called Alopecy, is nothing but pus that gathers in the eye, similar to water descending and it is not the same.
And the method of operation on this is, that you make him sit on a prepared chair or a straight one.
Then take his head with both your hands from the sides and shake him until you see pus reach the lower parts of your eyes. Then it is fashioned and does not descend, and the passage is opened: let the sick one see as he saw before: and if it does not descend further, know that it is water.
But if no descent of pus occurs with what was said, then make the sick person sit between your hands. Then take a fine probe and puncture it together with the cyst at the junction of the conjunctiva and the corneal membrane in the corona, until the pus comes out.
When it comes out, then pour warm water into the eye in which you have mixed honey; or warm water in which you have already boiled fenugreek and honey; afterwards treat with the remainder of the treatment until it heals.
On the cure of water that descends into the eye or cataract.
Chapter XXIII.
We have already said the appearance of water in division and which is suitable for puncturing when it speaks and expands, then take the same according to health.
Then it is necessary that you make the sick person sit facing your hands, opposite the light, near the sun; and tie the healthy eye, and press it hard; afterwards close the eyelid of the affected eye with your right hand, if the water is in the left eye; or with your left hand, if it is in the right.
Then take your right hand, if the affected eye is the left; or your left hand, if it is the right.
Then place the tip of your thumb near the cornea on the white part of the eye visible as the smaller lacrimal; then press with force; and you turn with it your hand, until it penetrates into the white part of the eye; and feel that your thumb has reached a void area.
And it is necessary that the measurement of the journey be great enough for depth, the measure of the space which is from the pupil until the end of the blackness: and it is the corona of the eye. You will see this in itself in the vision of the eye, because of the clarity of the cornea coat.
Then place a great [distance] until the place where there is water. Then press it downwards once after another.
If therefore the water descends immediately, then the sick person sees that which opens his sight immediately, and a great [distance] in his own eye.
Then rest a little. If therefore the water descends, then place it again, except that the great [distance] comes out.
When therefore it is pressed and does not rise: then extract the great [distance] with ease; and you turn your hand little by little.
Then dissolve something from clear salt in water: and cleanse the eye with it inside. Then place outside the eye all flaxseed or wool soaked in rose oil and egg white: and bind the healthy eye with it.
We, and those who are of our time, place upon him caraway seed ground with egg white.
If the great [distance] does not obey you in entering into the eye because of its hardness, since it is a man whose eye is very hard: then it is necessary that you take the spathule which is called Albarid, whose form is as follows.
Therefore pierce it with it only the conjunctiva, and not your hand into the opening: and it is not until you make a way to the great place subtle.
Then insert the great [distance], as we have said.
And for the completion of your work, prepare for the sick a bed properly made, in which he will sleep on his back in a dark house: and prevent him from all movements, and from coughing: and place his food that softens his nature: and do not move his head to the right, nor to the left at all.
And let the suture be according to its arrangement until the third day.
Then dissolve it in that dark place and test its sight: let it see things. Then return the suture until the seventh day.
And it is not proper to do that at the hour of cure, or immediately after the incision; on the contrary, it should be left to others, because water rises quickly through a violent wound.
If it happens to be a hot abscess: then it is necessary to dissolve the eye before the seventh day; and correct it with what soothes the abscess until it is soothed; then without its sight, place it on his face orally, which regulates its vision for several days, as long as it remains in that dark place.
Then he should go out of the house gradually, and convert himself to his own cases.
And know that in surgery a student is not excused from observation often; then he dares to perform an operation.
And indeed a certain one of those from Alayrach has come to us who said that a wound was perforated in Alayrach, through which water flows out.
Therefore I have not seen anyone in your country who has done that; nor read it in any of the old books; and it is possible that it is new.
And these are the shapes of species from magdan, to stand over him who does not know them.
Make them out of bronze; and let the ends of them be with this same triangular subtlety, and the end sharp.
Chapter XXIV.
Chapter on care of newborn flesh in the nose.
Sometimes numerous different types of flesh are born in the nose, one of which resembles a scorpion with many feet; and from this is cancerous flesh, stony, dark colored; and from this is soft flesh, not dark colored.
Therefore, for the soft flesh among these that is not fraudulent nor cancerous, you should have the sick person sit facing the sun with his nose opposite it, and then open his nostrils; next, insert a hook into those fleshes; then pull them out towards the exterior; and cut what you have caught with a subtle, sharp spatula on one side until you know that all the flesh has been removed.
If something remains of that which cannot be cut off: then shave it with a small and gentle instrument until nothing remains from it. If blood controls you or a hot abscess occurs: then oppose it with what is necessary; or if it is from malicious abscesses, then hurry and cauterize it until the blood is separated, and all the flesh is removed.
Then vinegar, water or wine should be poured into the nose after the cut. If the nose opens and moisture comes out to the palate, then you know that he is already well.
If the moisture does not penetrate as required, then you know that there is flesh born in the upper bones of the nose, which was not reached by the cut with the instrument.
Therefore, you should insert a linen thread with several knots and let the sick person send one end of the filament into his nose with a reed or whatever he can do after making it similar to a syringe; and draw out the smell until it reaches the skull, and comes out on top of the throat.
And indeed many boys do something similar to what Attomus did in school, and it is an easy thing for him who wishes.
Then place two ends of the thread, one which comes out over the nose and the other which remains inside the nose. Then with scissors, cut the flesh together with the knots that are on the thread. Do this until you know that the flesh is already with the knots of the thread.
Then draw out the thread and place linen in the nose after bleeding has ceased, which you have soaked in Egyptian ointment: do this for three days or more, until the ointment completely eats away all that remains of the flesh.
Then put a tube made of lead at the end of the procedure into the nose for some days until it heals.
If it requires drying treatment, use that.
For capping the head while oils and other medications are distilled into the nose, make it from silver or copper, similar to a small lamp, open like a shell and its opening likewise.
And if you wish to make a closed tube, as a tube (cannula).
And the shell-shaped instrument for capping the head should be full, perforated: with a handle at its end, which you hold when heating oil or whatever you wish from distilled substances and liquids.
Chapter 25.
Often a Thelum grows at the tip of the nose and becomes more prominent with days, until its appearance becomes disgusting.
And for this reason it is necessary to cut off the beginning of its appearance and to remove all of it. Then place on that spot a caustic or burning medicine in its place.
If therefore the incision is delayed until it enlarges, then consider if it is hard, stone-like, dark in color and has few senses: then do not touch it with iron, because the ulcer is cancerous.
I have often seen that one who has incised a boil and malignancy has happened to the one who had it.
And if the ulcer is soft when touched and not dark in color, and you see that an incision can be made throughout it, then evacuate the weakened part, and cut it without fear or concern, and care for the place with it, because it extracts and constricts it until it heals.
Chapter 26.
Chapter on nasal suture, lip suture, and ear suture.
Know that when dislocation of continuity occurs in one of these cartilages, the operation contributes little to it unless in certain men.
Therefore, when something happens to anyone from that, you must consider if it is a recent wound with its own blood: and then collect the edges of the wound with suture; then care for it until it heals.
And if the dislocation of continuity has already separated the lips and each part is healthy: then it is necessary to remove all the tissue from its visible skin until it bleeds. Then collect the two lips with suture, bind them and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood, pulverized aloes and asafoetida on top of it. Place a piece of emplaster (diafinicon) over the powders, and another consolidated emplaster. Leave it bound for two or three days. Then dissolve it (the suture) and change the medicine. Leave it until the threads are removed by themselves. Then care for it with ointment until healed.
The method of suturing is that you gather the solution of continuity, or with needles, as we have told in abdominal suturing; or gather the solution with thread, as I have informed you.
Chapter XXVII.
On the extraction of lip nodules.
Many men indeed have hard eruptions similar to grains of herbs on their lower or upper lips; some are smaller and others larger.
Therefore, one should turn the lip, find above every nodule of it, and hang it with a hook, and cut it from all sides.
Then fill the place after the incision with boiled linen cloth until the blood is separated.
Then it is rubbed with vinegar and the place where there is an inflammation is treated with it until the wounds heal.
Chapter XXVIII.
On the incision of the born flesh on the gum.
Often a flesh grows up over the gum which is called ablus by the ancients.
Therefore, one should hang it with a hook; or hold it with forceps and cut it at its root, and let pus or blood run out.
Then put over the place boiled linen cloth, or other healing powders, drying.
If that flesh returns after treatment, for it often returns, then cut it a second time and burn it; for it does not return after being burned.
Chapter XXIX.
On the scraping of teeth with iron.
When they are gathered on the surfaces of teeth from both the inner and outer parts, and between the gums and rough cortices, they become decayed, turn yellow and green, until corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul because of it.
Therefore it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands and place his head in your lap, and grind away the cavity and tooth, where the cortices appear to you, until there remains nothing of them; similarly do for blackness, greenness, yellowishness, and others until they are clean.
If what is within them is removed at the beginning of the reasoning, it is good; and if not, then apply the razor to them on another day, on the second, and on the third, until finally your study reaches the end that you desire.
And know that a tooth requires razors of various shapes and forms, many figures; according to what is prepared for your operation: because the razor with which a tooth is shaved from below is different from the razor with which it is shaved between teeth, in accordance with other shapes.
And these shapes of razors should be prepared by you, which you see.
Chapter 30.
Chapter on the extraction of tooth pain.
It is necessary that you cure the tooth from its own pain with all your skill, and proceed slowly in extracting it. For there is no substitute for it when it is extracted; because it is a substance that is raised up; until when there is no excuse for the extraction of it, then it is necessary when the patient is compelled to extract it himself, that he may be strengthened and assured by you that the tooth causing pain will be replaced.
For often pain deceives the patient and believes that there is pus in the tooth and extracts it himself; then the pain does not subside until the diseased tooth is extracted.
We have already seen that from the operation of phlebotomists.
When therefore it is certified to you that a hard tooth itself is painful, then it is necessary that you lancet around the tooth with a spatula, in which there is something virtuous, until it softens from all sides: then move it yourself with your fingers, or with fine forceps first of all gently, until you shake it.
Then place large forceps in those places well, and hold the head of the weak between your knees: what you have already firmly held, so that it does not move: then pull out the tooth in a straight direction, so as not to break it.
If therefore it does not come out, then take one of those instruments and introduce it under it from all sides with ease, and try to move it as you did first.
If however the tooth is perforated or corroded: then it is necessary that you fill that hole with a cloth and bind it with the end of a fine radius so as not to break it during your compression on it with forceps.
And it is necessary that you be careful with the lancet around the gum from all sides much.
And keep your strength so as not to break it and a part remains of it and returns to the weak from that illness which is greater in pain at first.
And be careful not to do what ignorant phlebotomists do in haste and the arrogance of their extraction, beyond what we have said.
For often they bring great illnesses upon men, whose more difficult ones are to break and all roots remain or some of them, or to extract it with certain bones of the jaw as we have testified many times.
Then it is to be covered after its removal with wine, or with vinegar and salt.
If there should be bleeding from the places (for it often happens), then rub something of the alum and fill the place with it; and if not, cauterize it if you do not have alum.
The handles of the fine forceps by which the molars are moved should be long at the ends, short in the arms, heavy, so that they do not break when pressed on the teeth; they should be like those of large forceps, until they do not bite themselves or become bent when squeezed with them; the ends should be short, and made of hard iron, or skillfully made from brass, with sharp tips at the ends; and in their tips there should be teeth, some of which enter into others and tighten with a proper constriction, strong.
And sometimes the ends are like the shape of a bird's beak called "ciconia", and they are strong in constriction.
Chapter XXXI.
Chapter on Extraction of Teeth and Removal of Fractured Bone of the Jaw.
When a tooth that breaks off remains after its extraction, then it is necessary to place hot compresses with butter for one or two days until the location becomes softened; then introduce into it alum or forceps, whose tips resemble the beak of a bird called "ciconia". The form is that of forceps.
The ends should be made like a plane blade or an aliskilfegi.
If these forceps do not obey you in extraction, then it is necessary to cauterize the root and to peel off all the flesh and to introduce an instrument called "Palanca parua", whose form is as follows:
The extremity should be short and not too thick; and it should not be filled (or swollen), so that it does not break.
If the root comes out through (it), it is good; if not, help with other tools of similar form.
The first (one) has a triangle-shaped end, in which there is some thickness.
Triangle-shaped thin end.
And with other tools and implements that came before (in the ratio of teeth).
Also helps with this tool similar to a large nail, of the same form, triangle-shaped twisted end with some thickness, so that it does not break; and let it not be filled (or swollen).
And know that there are many tools for the teeth; and similarly, other implements are not counted; and the wise artisan, skilled in his art, finds for himself the tool according to what the operation and the disease itself require.
Because among diseases there are those for which the ancients did not create a tool, due to the diversity of their forms.
If the bone is broken from the jaw, or from other bones of the mouth, or putrefies; then examine it at its location with that which suits it among the tools and forceps mentioned for root extraction, and help with the one whose shape is this (described earlier).
Let there be some thickness gradually, so that the bone can be pulled or held with it and does not escape and move, until the bone comes out; and restore the place with appropriate medicines for that.
If there is a small putrefaction in the bone, then scrape it off from its own putrefaction, and take care of it until it heals.
De Serratura dentium quibusdam protrudent
On the serration of protruding teeth.
When some teeth protrude not according to their natural course, it gives rise to an ugly form, and especially when this happens in women and girls, that is to say, those of a venereal condition.
The surgeon must examine the matter carefully. If a tooth is born after another tooth and does not fit or can be serrated or filed, then pull it out; and if it is attached to another tooth, then cut it off with this tool, whose shape is as follows:
It resembles a small beak made of iron and has an extremely sharp tip.
Make your cut several days apart, due to the hardness of the tooth and so as not to disturb another tooth.
If it is protruding for filing, then file it with a file made of iron, whose shape is as follows:
The whole is made of ivory, and its handle is of many small points like a limed lime-stone, with which it is ground gradually for many days with ease, so as not to disturb the tooth, and fall: then smooth it with it, at the end, grind it again with some rasps.
If it is a tooth, from which a part breaks and injures the tongue: then it is necessary that lime be applied to it, until the roughness of the fracture is removed, and it is made smooth: and it must not injure the tongue, nor corrupt speech.
Chapter XXXIII.
On the filing of teeth with gold threads.
When it happens to the front teeth that they are struck or shaken due to a blow or accident, and the weak person cannot hold what he eats lest it fall: and you have treated them with medicines for splints, and the treatment was not effective: then it is appropriate for them to be held together with a gold thread: because silver becomes green and rots after days, but gold never changes.
And let the thread be of intermediate fineness and thickness according to its quantity, which fits between the teeth.
And the form of filing is that you take the thread and insert its double between two healthy teeth: then you weave with two ends of the thread between the moved teeth, whether there is one or more, until you reach with the needle up to the healthy tooth on the other side. Then you weave again to the part from which you began: and tighten your hand with delicacy and wisdom until it is not moved at all: and let your compression, by which you hold the thread, be near the roots of the teeth, so that it does not escape.
Then cut off the superfluous ends of the thread with scissors: and bring together both, and turn them towards yourself: and hide them between the healthy tooth and the moved tooth, so that they do not injure the tongue: then let it be so tightened until it remains.
If it is opened or cut open, bind them with another thread and let it remain in that condition for a period of time.
And this is the form of teeth, and the figure of the intertwining of two healthy teeth, and two moving teeth, as you see.
And sometimes it happens that one tooth or two teeth return to their respective places after loss, and are retained as we have said, and remain: this does not happen unless the skilled and experienced craftsman performs it.
And sometimes a tooth is fashioned from the bones of a calf: and it is made like the form of a tooth, and placed in the place where it is secured and bound as we have said; and it remains, and serves for a long time.
Chapter XXXIV.
Whenever this ligament that occurs under the tongue is natural, when man is born, or accidental, from a healed wound.
The procedure in this case is to open the weak bone in his head within your pouch, and raise his tongue; then cut the nerve-ligament across width until it is released from its hold.
If there is something hard and knotted within it, and it comes from the consolidation of a wound; then throw an awl into it and split it across width until you cut the ligament, and the knotting is released.
And beware, lest there is a split in deep flesh, and you cut an artery there, and blood flows out.
Then it is washed with water and rose petals or vinegar or cold water.
Then place a flax cloth from linen under the tongue for the patient to keep all night so that it does not consolidate again.
If, however, there is blood flow, then place on it a piece of powdered hematite. If the blood overpowers you, then cauterize the place with a lentiginous cautery that suits it; then take care of him with the rest of the treatment until he is cured.
Chapter 35.
Whenever under the tongue there occurs an aposteme resembling a small frog that prevents the tongue from performing its natural function; and it may perhaps grow so much that it fills up the bone.
And the procedure is to open the weak bone facing the sun and examine the aposteme.
If you see it (the patient) of a dark or black color, hard, who does not have a weak sensation: then do not touch it, because it is cancer.
And if it is hollowed out towards whiteness, in which there is moisture: then throw in a hook, and cut it with a thin spatula, and free it from all sides. What if blood constrains you during your operation hour? Then place upon it a piece of burnt alum, until the blood is cut off; then return to your operation, until you extract it with its contents.
Then wash (it) with vinegar and salt; and take care of it with appropriate treatment until it is healed.
[Title: Treatment for an abscess of two tonsils]
Chapter XXXVI.
Whenever a swelling similar to goitre occurs near the throat, that is, glands, which are called double amygdalae: when you treat them as we have said in division, and they do not heal, then consider.
If the abscess is hard, dark colored, with few senses: then do not touch it with iron.
And if it is red in color and its root is thick: then do not touch it even with iron, fearing blood flow, rather let it be until it matures. Then either pierce it yourself: or it will burst by itself.
And if it is white in color, round and its root is thin: then it should be cut.
And the operation on it is that you consider before the operation itself if the abscess of it has ceased to be warm and completed its quiet, or it decreases somewhat: then let the patient sit in front of the sun, and his head should be in your lap: and open his mouth, and the servant holding him by hands, press his tongue downwards with the instrument whose form is as follows.
Let it be made of silver or copper, which should be thin like a knife.
When you press the tongue with it and the abscess is shown to you, and it falls onto it under your sight: then take a hook, and attach it to the amygdala, and pull it out as far as possible, taking something from the tunics with it.
Then cut it with the instrument whose form is as follows. It is similar to forks: but its extremities should be curved, so that the opening of each one is on a straight line, perpendicular to the other, thus care must be taken that it is made of iron or copper coated with aluminum.
If this instrument is not present, then cut it with a spatula, whose form is as follows: Sharp on one side, not sharp on the other.
And after cutting one almond, cut the other in the same shape of the incision.
Then, after the incision, the sick person shall rinse his throat with cold water, or with vinegar and water.
If blood flows, he shall rinse with water in which have been boiled the peels of pomegranates or leaves of myrtle and similar ones from boxwood, until the flow of blood stops; then care for him until he is cured.
And sometimes boils other than almonds grow in the throat. Cut them accordingly as I said in the incision of two almonds equally.
I myself have already been treated by a woman from a boil that was born in her throat, which drew towards the neck, with few senses, which almost closed her throat; and the woman breathed through a narrow nostril, and had already prohibited food and drink; and she was almost at death if she remained for one or two days.
And the boil rose only so high that it had sent out two branches until they came out over two nostrils.
Therefore I rushed quickly and fixed a hook on one of them. Then I pulled it out, and a large part came out with it.
Then I cut off the part where I had grasped it from the nostril.
Then I did what came out of the other nostril.
Then I opened his mouth and pressed his tongue; and afterwards I fixed a hook on the boil; then I cut off a part of it, and no more came out except a little blood; so the throat of the woman was healed, and she immediately began to drink water, then received food.
I did not stop cutting from that ulcer for a long period of time: and the ulcer succeeded in its place which I was cutting, until it was extended too much and with it that (something).
I therefore cauterized the ulcer located at the throat.
Therefore it stood still after addition: then I walked away from there, and I did not know what God had done with it after me.
Chapter on the incision of the ulcer in the throat.
Chapter XXXVII.
When the catarrh descends to the throat, and an ulcer forms, and it is long: then it is called a perpendicular; and if it is thick and round at the lower part, it is then named as a boil.
When it is cured along with what I said in the division, and the cure does not work: and you see that the ulcer has become warm and has subsided, and is subtle: then it is necessary to cut it.
And what is attached to it, round, and not long, and is bloody or dark red or black, and there is no sensation in it: then it is necessary to make an incision of it. For there is fear over the weak (one) in it.
Therefore when you see it according to the manner which I said from whiteness, and its length: make the weak person sit before the sun; and press his tongue with the tool whose story preceded; then put a hook in the throat, and pull it downwards: and cut it with one of two tools which I said in the incision of the two salivary glands.
And it is necessary not to cut from it, unless what is added exceeds a natural limit without addition.
For if you cut more from it, you will damage the voice and speech.
Then after the incision, use what was said about the incision of the two salivary glands: and cure it until it heals.
If the sick person is afraid of incision: then it is necessary that you use your skill in the cauterization of him without fear and dread.
The method of cauterization is not otherwise, except with sharp water: and it is that you place the head of the sick one in your armpit. Then press his tongue with the instrument which we said. Then take water which I told you in the chapter on cauterization and make a not-extinguished ladle with it, and do not make it thick or thin, and fill this instrument's hollow with it, whose shape is as follows: (Here, there would be a drawing of the tool)
Let the end where the medicine is placed have a hollow like that of a snail's shell.
And place the instrument with the medicine on the wound itself: and let the sick one lie on his side, so that saliva runs out of his mouth from the internal medicine, so that nothing comes down from it to his throat, and it does not harm him.
Then hold your hand with the medicine. And you from the first apply it to the wound in quantity of half an hour, until you see it already turned black and quieted the biting of the medicine.
And if you want to receive a cup and cover it over the end of the radius, and pour the cup with the medicine, and insert the radius with the covered cup on top, until the cup adheres to the wound.
Do this many times, until you achieve what you want from the cauterization of the wound. Then let it go: for it will burn and fall off after three or four days.
If you need to apply medicine again, do so: and after cauterization wash the wound around it with a cup immersed in butter, and cleanse what is around it from the medicine: and wash it with cold water.
And it shall be treated from outside with cupping glasses, and from inside with gargles, until it heals.
This method of treatment is healthier than incision and farther from fear.
And sometimes the ulcer is also treated with a method more subtle than cautery and incision: it is treated with fumigation, according to this method. Take calaminthe, hyssop, origanum, rut, sseah, chamomile, abrotanum and similar herbs: gather all of them or some of them in a pot, and immerse them with vinegar, and boil them: the pot should be coated well with clay, and there should be a hole in the middle of the pot, over which you arrange an instrument concave according to this method.
Make it of silver or copper: and the end is inserted into the mouth of the sick one, until the vapor reaches the ulcer through a tube, until the ulcer is completely covered.
Then repeat this over and over again, until it burns.
And beware not to perform this treatment at the beginning of an abscess. Usually, however, you add [something] to an abscess: it should not be done unless at the time of the decline of the heat of the abscess.
If this instrument is not available to you, then take a reed and fill its tip with the bark of an ox's horn: so that the bone of the sick one is not burned: because the bark of the ox's horn prevents the vapor from burning the bone: and this is part of good treatment with safety.
Chapter on removing thorns and bones from the throat.
Chapter XXXVIII.
Often a bone or a fish spine adheres to the throat.
Therefore, it is necessary to remove what appears from among them that lies beneath the sight, after you press the tongue with an instrument near the sun, and it becomes clear to you that there is something in the throat.
And what is not apparent to you and hidden in the throat, it is necessary that you make a man vomit before the food is digested in the stomach. Perhaps therefore it will come out attached matter through vomiting.
Or the sick person swallows a piece of nutmeg, or the root of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread: or let him take a piece of dried sea sponge that is gentle: and tie it up with a thread, then let him swallow it. When it reaches the place where there are thorns or bone, and it is pulled out, then it comes out.
If it does not come out as we said: then use an instrument made of lead in this shape.
Let it be thicker than the radius by a little, and at its end let there be a bent part, which he introduces into his throat easily: and let him himself hold his head raised up.
And let him avoid touching his epiglottis, so that he does not get a cough, and push with it the bone or thorn, or introduce it himself with his hand.
But what the sick person introduces is better: because of his knowledge of the place of the attached matter: and let him push below or pull his hand with the instrument upwards, all of it according to the size that is prepared for him, until it comes out.
Chapter on the extraction of Leeches.
Chapter 39.
When the leech is cured with what I said in the division of cure with medicines, and it does not work: then examine in the throat of the sick person facing the sun, or after pressing his tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
If your sight falls upon the leech, extract it with a small hook or with pointed forceps well placed.
If it is not possible with them (the instruments): then take a concave cannula and insert it into the throat of the sick one, up to near the throat; then insert into the concavity of the cannula hot iron with fire. Do this often: and let the sick person abstain from water all day.
Then let him take a vessel full of cold water, and open his mouth in it; and wash his mouth with it, and swallow nothing from it; and move the water one hour after another with his hand. For leeches it falls immediately when they feel water.
If it does not come out with what I have said, then fumigate the sick one with bedbugs, or with ash with the instrument that I have mentioned for fumigating the ear.
Do this often, because it will fall by itself.
And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot, in which there are live prunes with fire; and let the pot be covered with a cover, through whose middle there is an opening; and arrange the end of the instrument in it.
Then throw the fumigation, and let the sick one place his mouth at the end of the cannula, and close his mouth so that the fumigation does not come out, until you know that the fumigation has reached the leech. For leeches fall immediately.
If it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation often.
Let the sick person endure thirst, and eat salt and other things, and drink no water.
Therefore it is necessary that it comes out with this regimen.
And this is the shape of the instrument with which a leech is extracted from the throat, when it falls on its face.
It resembles forceps, as you see; except that there is a bend in it which enters the throat. The end of it is similar to the mouth of an owl, which is called a ciconia, in which there is roughness like a file. When it grasps something, it does not let go of it completely.
On the opening of abscesses and their cutting and treatment in general.
Chapter XL (40).
The species of abscesses are many, according to their recollection, that is, one kind and one kind only in this book; and they are diverse in the perforation of them, and cutting of themselves from two ways.
One kind is a type of abscess by itself, and that which it grasps from moisture.
And the second way is due to places, where it happens from the body.
Because an abscess occurring in the head is different from an abscess occurring in the anus; and an abscess occurring in a fleshy place is different from an abscess occurring at the joints; and each of them has its own judgment according to the operation.
And among the abscesses are those that should not be perforated unless after the maturation of pus in them and its completion; and there are those that must be perforated while they are raw and do not mature according to their completion.
As abscesses which are near the joints.
Because an abscess when it occurs near a joint and prolongs itself until it rots what is around its circumference, perhaps the ligaments or nerves of that joint are corrupted; therefore it is the cause of a more pronounced contraction of that member.
Or is an abscess near the main member; because if you delay the perforation of it until it matures, it will harm either him or through the main member itself.
Or it is near the anus; therefore perforate it immaturely. And it is not necessary to perforate a raw abscess, not fully digested, unless it is near the anus, so that it does not rot deeply and extend to the interior of the anus, and become a fistula or remain in its end which cannot heal.
It is necessary that you know the hour of perforation of the abscess, which has matured according to completion; and it is at the sedation of pain, the recession of fever, and the diminution of redness, and pulsation, and acuity of the head of the abscess; and the remaining signs.
And it is necessary that you make the same perforation in the lower part of the abscess and of greater protrusion; and the perforation shall proceed along the length of the body, if the abscesses are in the parts of hands and feet, shoulders, necks, tendons, nerves, arteries, and ultimately in all places where there is no reflection.
In those which reflect, proceed with the perforation according to that member.
When the abscess is in fleshy places: then it is better to wait for the perforation of its digestion, as we said according to completion.
Because if you perforate it before that, the course of the virus from it is prolonged and there are many filths and putrefaction, and possibly its edges harden and its depth increases.
And some abscesses are perforated according to the width of the body when necessary; or according to that which the member needs.
And it is necessary that you administer a small perforation to small abscesses and a large perforation to large abscesses; or many cuts according to the similarity of the size of the abscess.
And among abscesses, there are those in which the skin should be hollowed out; and it is cut when it has become like a cloth and reached the end that is already dead; as what happens often with buboes and swellings.
And among those, there are some which are cut with a section having three angles. And from them (the instruments) is one, when it is cut as in the figure of a myrtle leaf.
As an inguinal abscess.
And among them (the instruments) are those for administering round and crescent-shaped sections, and similar ones for other sections.
But that which has no head, such as superficial abscesses, should be punctured with a superficial lancing or only by incision.
And when the abscess is large and has already collected much pus, it should be punctured so that it does not burst and all the pus is drawn out at that hour; rather, draw out a part of it from it. Then wait for another day before operating on an abscess. Then draw something more from the pus again.
Do this repeatedly according to degree until it comes out; especially if the patient is weak or of poor strength, or a woman in pregnancy, or a small boy, or an old man decrepitus; for animal spirits are often resolved with the release of pus; and perhaps the weak one may die, and you will not benefit.
Be careful therefore, for this chapter requires great caution.
And after your puncture of the abscesses, it is necessary to clean the wound; and be mindful. If the wound of the abscess is small or the incision is flat, then administer linen cloth or an old bandage. And if the abscess is large and there are many cracks of puncture, then it is necessary to insert linen into each crack until they meet.
And if you have removed a piece of skin from an abscess or hollowed out the surrounding area, then it is necessary to fill it with an old bandage, as when fabric is woven or flax is combed without moisture; and bind it for three days.
Then cut it open and care for that which is necessary with an ointment until it heals.
If there should be a flow of blood at the time of your operation, then give cold water and vinegar, after it has been soaked in cloths; and place this over the area of blood flow many times.
If the flow of blood persists, then it is necessary that you give a regimen, treatment and powders, which I have described in many places of this our book, and from division.
If it is in winter time, and the place of the amputation is of many nerves; then it is necessary that you pour powder with wine and warm oil, and place them over the places.
And if it is in summer, and the places are fleshy; then it is necessary that you place powders soaked in water, or oil, or wine and oil, and cool everything. Until the third day, as we have said, then it is necessary that you remove the amputation, clean it, and administer for its treatment whatever suits it, until it heals.
This is therefore what is necessary from the knowledge of the treatment of amputations universally.
According to the method of distinction, I have already said about every amputation, how is the way to its treatment separately chapter by chapter.
Chapter XL (40).
Chapter on the sectioning of amputations that occur in the skin of the head.
Pustules small, of the nature of knots, occur on the head's skin, which are contained by sacs like they were pouches of a hen.
And their appearance is manyfold.
Some of them are fatty: some contain moisture similar to paste: some contain moisture like that of a scab and plaster: and those alike, and from them there are hard stones.
And in the cutting of all [of them] and their extraction, there is no fear, as long as it does not cause opposition to an artery at their cutting.
And the operation in cutting them is to try it with the instrument whose shape comes after these words, which is called "Intromissum," until you know what it contains.
For if it is what contains moisture, then cut it with a transverse surface-cut along its length in this manner: according to this shape.
And begin with the cut from line b to line g. For when the moisture is evacuated, then scrape off the cyst that contains this moisture, and do not leave anything inside of it.
For often it returns if something remains from it.
Then immerse the wound in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; and if not, in water and salt; and fill the wound with it, and let it remain until another day. For that which remains from the cyst corrodes itself.
Then repeatedly over the wound with Egyptian ointment second and third times, as often as needed, until you believe that nothing remains from the cyst; then treat the wound with ointment until it heals.
If the pustule contains a fat knot: then cut it according to this shape, with a transverse cross-cut; and thrust needles between the folds of the cut, and scrape off all of it from every side: and strive in extracting the skin that contains it.
If however an artery opposes (you), then do what I shall tell you afterwards.
And similarly do in cauterization (if it is a stone), by cutting and the same cure, as we have said before.
Cutting over a stone-like aposteme is easier; because it has little blood and moisture. Sometimes there are some of these apostemes in the head in certain men, with which there is no moisture.
This is because I have cut over an aposteme on an old woman's head and found the aposteme to be as hard and solid as a stone, rough, white, which could not be broken; and if anyone struck it with force, he injured himself.
In other cases of apostemic occurrences in the head, with the exception of these specific apostemes that occur in children's heads and at the roots of the ears, the incision of all of them should be a superficial incision.
Or make a perforation of theirs always from the lower part of it, so that the flow of pus is directed towards the lower areas.
Then care for these with what fits them in terms of cure.
Section on Straphules (boils) in the neck.
Chapter XLII.
These abscesses often occur in the neck, under the buttocks, and in the groins; and sometimes they occur elsewhere in the body.
On the abscesses that occur on the neck, there is one, and many; they are generated from opposite sides; and every boil from them is within its own layer, as it is with knots and abscesses of the head, as we have said.
The types of these boils are numerous. For from them are the stone-like ones; and from them there are those containing moisture; and from them are the malicious ones, which do not obey treatment.
In the good disposition of that boil which you see in touch, whose evident is near to the skin color, and moves towards every part, and is not attached with the neck muscles, nor with the groin, nor with the artery, nor is deep: it should be cut off by superficial section from above to lower part of the body along the line, b. to line, g., and scrape it from all sides; and stretch two layers of skin with a knife or with several knives if needed, as we said in the abscesses of the head, and draw it out gradually.
And it is on caution, that no vein or nerve should be cut.
Let the knife not be very sharp; so that your hand should not hurt with the incision, or disturb the sick one, and cut what is not necessary.
If you cut a vein or an artery, it prohibits you from operation, then place in the wound linen soaked with powder that removes blood, and tighten the wound, and leave it until the sharpness of the abscess subsides and the wound softens; or it begins to rot.
The blood is to be cut through the skin, therefore return to your operation until you are finished.
Next, ask with your index finger if there remains anything of the straws (stitches) small: therefore cut them and clean them.
If there is in the root of the stitch a large vein, then it is necessary not to cut that stitch from its root: rather tie it with a strong double thread and leave it until it falls by itself without harm.
Then fill the wound with an old patch that you have already soaked in Egyptian ointment. Then take care of yourself.
If the stitch is cut entirely, then gather together the edges of the wound and sew it up immediately after you see that there remains no superfluity.
If, however, you see that there remains superfluity due to the size of the stitch, then it is necessary to stretch out to cut its root and pull it out: and apply the suture as we have said.
And what contains humidities from the stitches, pierce it with a superficial puncture to make its place appear to you: and place the puncture below that which follows lower in the body, as we have said.
Then apply linen with ointment after the puncture and similar things to burn what remains from corruption until you see that the wound is clean: then take care of yourself with a more potent ointment for flesh until it heals.
Chapter XLIII.
Section on Epiglottis after amputation within the throat occurring.
The ancients said this section on the Epiglottis, and I have not seen anyone in our land who has done it: this is their writing.
In those with synanchias, it is necessary to be cautious about section of the Epiglottis: as no help is provided by that; because all veins and lungs are weak.
In those who have a hot boil in the mouth, throat or both amygdalae, when there is no illness in the canal, it is necessary to use section of the Epiglottis to avoid ruin which happens through strangulation.
Therefore, when we want to cut the Epiglottis, it should be done under three or four circles of the Epiglottis with a small section along its width, in that which is between two circles by quantity; this should be a section in sifac, not cartilage; and indeed this place is suitable for cutting because it lacks flesh and blood vessels are distant from it.
If the physician is afraid, then it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat with a hook. Then he shall incise the skin until he reaches the canal; be cautious of blood vessels, if he sees any from them.
Then he shall cut the sifac as we have said; it is indicated by the phlegm that comes out from there, with what is burst and separation of voice.
And leave an open wound for some time.
When the hour comes when strangulation is feared, gather two lips of the wound skin, and the skin itself alone without cartilage.
Then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow until it heals.
Says Albucasis. The sum of the speech that I have related is not exposure unless they see that one of these boils has already choked the throat of a weak person; and he has risen up sickly near to death, and wishes to cut his breathing; they go to cut the Epiglottis so that the weak one may breathe over the place of the wound with some kind of breathing, and be saved from death; and for this reason they have commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness is consumed, which lasts three days or so itself; then therefore they have commanded to sew up the wound and take care of it until it heals.
And what I have seen with my own eyes is that a maidservant received a knife and sent it into her own throat and cut a part of the trachea of the lungs.
And I was summoned to treat her, and I found her gasping, as is the gasp of the dead.
So I examined the wound, and I found that blood had come out from the wound in a small amount. Therefore, I suspected that she had not severed an artery nor vein; and a wind was coming out of the wound.
I therefore approached the wound and cured it until it healed; and nothing happened to the maidservant except a cough; and she returned after days to a better condition of her health.
Therefore, from this I say that there is no fear in the tracheotomy (section of Epiglottis).
Chapter on the tracheotomy (section) of a hernia of the throat.
Chapter 44.
This called hernia of the throat is a large aposteme (abscess), according to the color of the body; and it occurs more in women.
And it is according to two modes: for it is natural, or it is accidental (acquired).
In the natural one, there is no inborn defect.
The accidental one is according to two modes: of which one is similar to fatty nodes (nodules).\]   Et hic nullo modo debet procedi ad operationem, nisi sit necessarium; et illud debet operari a magistro, qui hab And the other mode is similar to an abscess caused by nodulation of an artery.\[ Et hic nullo modo debet procedi ad operationem, nisi sit necessarium; et illud debet operari a mag And there is fear in this one, and it should not be proceeded with operation unless necessary; and if it must be operated upon, it should be operated on by a master who has\[ Et hic nullo modo debet procedi ad operationem, nisi sit necessarium; et illud debet operari a mag\] skill in inserting (instruments). If therefore you find the same sort of fatty lump and it is not suspended with any vein: then cut it off, as knots are cut off; and draw it out along with what it contains from the chest, if it is in the chest: and if not, then examine all around it. Care for the place with whatever is necessary for healing, until it is healed.
Chapter XLV.
Chapter on incision regarding lumps (knots).
There are many types of lumps (knots), and I have already said all their species in the division; and it is necessary that I here explain the difference between a knot and an exitration (excision) when there is doubt.
Therefore, when the exitration (excision) is accompanied by heat and fever and intense pains until the boiling of superfluity subsides and the rotting is complete: then the fever and the heat cease.
When the knot is not accompanied by heat, fever or pains and contains them in a chest (cavity) which is its proper sac: it is closed like a chickpea, and made like a gourd (melon), and larger or smaller.
And they are according to two species: either fatty: or containing moisture. The colors of the moisture (humidity) are many, as I have said in the division.
Therefore, when you approach the healing of a knot, you should examine it first with an instrument called "Intromissum", according to its form which will come in the chapter that follows this one.
The method of examination of abscesses and all knots is to take this instrument, and insert it into the moistest place which you find in the abscess: and you shall turn your fingers gradually with it until you know that the instrument has already penetrated the skin. Then, your last hand according to the measure of the size of the abscess.
Extract (it), and observe what comes out with its trace.
If (it) comes out running moisture, whatever its color is: then cut it with a superficial incision, according to what I said about other abscesses.
And if no running moisture comes out in the trace of (the foreign body), then you know that it is fat: then cut over it with a section having the form of a cross, according to this form, as I taught you: and hang it up with tweezers, and strip off the skin from all sides easily: and keep a pot on it if possible, in order to extract it along with the knot.
If it breaks during the operation from the pot and cannot be extracted whole, then extract it piecemeal until nothing remains of it.
For if something remains of it, little or much, the knot returns most of all.
If it overpowers you, and something remains of it: then fill the wound at your completion with certain corrosive powders: and stitch up the wound, and put on top of it what sits on the abscess, hot, and take care of it with the rest of the cure, until it is healed.
