If therefore the knot is large, then separate its two lips, and take care of it with that which makes it grow together.
If however it is a pulsating vein or not pulsating to you: then flee, and fill the place with boiled pitch, and leave it tightly sealed for two days or three, until the wound rots, and the boiling of blood subsides: then return to cut what remains of the knot.
De usu fori in sectionibus et perforationibus.
Exterior instruments for cutting and perforating.
Of the forms of instruments introduced, there are three kinds.
For one is great, and one is medium, and one is small.
Let them be made from iron of square tips well-balanced, so that they enter smoothly into the wound.
And these are the forms of the experienced ones, and it is called perforation; and one of them is named bery, that is, piercing; and there are three kinds.
Amongst them there is a large one, a middle one, and a small one.
They converge so that they may be incised through abscesses, boils, fistulas, and buboes because they are among bones.
And some are made round, smooth, blunt, like the large needle that is set in handles, either from citrine or brass, iron, or silver.
Those which are made of citrine are better.
They are also made of black lead, which converge so that they may be used to probe fistulas, the concavity of which serves as reflection, so that they reflect with their smoothness along with those reflections.
And again, there are three kinds. Because amongst them there are long ones, medium ones, and short ones according to the size of the fistula and its constriction.
Forma of vaginas, and there are many kinds.
Because amongst them there are simple ones, that is, those which have a single curve; and there are three kinds as you see, large, medium, and small.
And amongst them there are blind vaginas; and there are three kinds.
And amongst them there are vaginas with two curves; and there are three kinds: and amongst them there are vaginas with three curves; and there are three kinds: and all of these are necessary in their place.
And these are the forms of scalpels with which knots and abscesses are cut and scraped; and there are three kinds because amongst them there is a large one, a middle one, and a small one.
The extremities for making a section are sharp, the other extremities are not sharp: they are not placed thus unless to provide help during excoriation of Nodules because of fear of incision of vein or nerve, and so that the sick one may be healed by it, and find some tranquility briefly as in burning which is found during excoriation of an abscess.
They are made of copper and resemble a thermometer, with a hidden spatula-like hole at one end; it runs through to the inside or outside as desired, as you can see.
The shape of spatulas hidden among the fingers during incision of an abscess; the sick do not feel these; they are of three kinds, large, medium, and small.
The forms of vein-tied bandages for cutting blood flow; they are of three kinds, large, medium, and small.
Make them of copper or citron, round, slightly long, as you can see; they should be fine.
And it is necessary that these vein-tied bandage forms be large and small with you; so that you can cut blood with them quickly when there is need, and then when medicine is not present with you.
However, do not use them for cutting blood in any part of the body, nor use them except in fleshy parts; such as thighs, hips, arms, breasts, stomach, groin, and similar places, from fleshy areas, moist.
And sometimes they are made into small instruments similar to the covers of fists, according to their form; with which blood is cut when it flows from the place of phlebotomy or incision of vein or artery; and sometimes they are made round in this shape.
Chapter XLVII.
On the treatment of human breasts resembling those of women.
Sometimes the breasts of some men swell during sleep (that is, when they begin to dream) until they resemble those of women; and they remain foul smelling afterwards.
Whoever abhors this (condition), it is necessary that he cuts the breasts with a lunar incision according to this form along the line, 'b' to the line, 'g'. Then scrape off all the fatness. Then fill the wound with a ointment of resin. Then join two lips of the wound with stitches, and take care of it until it heals.
If the breast, however, droops downwards and becomes soft due to its size, as happens with women; then it is necessary that it be opened in two lateral incisions on both upper sides, each similar to the shape of the moon, one contained within the other at their ends so that the larger line contains the smaller one, according to this form from line 'b' to line 'g'. Afterwards scrape off the skin that is between the two lips and remove the fatness, and administer what I have said about stitching and powders, which is necessary for treatment, until it heals.
If the incision is not complete as required for you to make it, either due to the restlessness of the patient or due to bleeding; then fill the wound with a cauterized substance submerged in a corrosive ointment, and leave it until it corrodes what remains from the fatness. Then take care of it until it heals.
Chapter on the perforation of a boil that occurs under an armpit.
Chapter XLVIII.
These ulcers that occur under the titillico, are of the species of hard worms, which contain cysts, and among them are those containing moistures.
Among those containing moistures, it is necessary that they be cut with a lunar section according to this form, from line b to line g. When everything within the ulcer is evacuated through pus, then fill it up with an old cloth and leave it until another day.
Then remove the cloth, and treat it with a suitable ointment until it heals.
If the ulcer is of the species of hard worms resembling knots, then cut it across, as we said in the section on cutting off worms equally.
If the wound extends so as to discharge pus, then administer cautery to it, according to what we said in that which was previously mentioned.
Chapter XLIX.
[Paragraph on the sectioning of ulcers due to an artery or vein.]
When an artery is torn and the skin above it hardens, there often occurs an ulcer; similarly, the same occurs with veins so that an ulcer and swelling occur in them.
And the signs by which it is recognized that an ulcer and swelling are due to an artery or vein, are: because when an ulcer is due to an artery, it is long and gathered in the depth of the body; and when you press the ulcer with your fingers, it feels as if there is a grinding sensation.
And that which is due to a vein, is round and apparent on the body.
And cutting into this ulcer is a mistake, and particularly when it is under the shoulders, groins, neck, and in many parts of the body; and it is very great. It is necessary therefore that his care with iron should be avoided, and what is also from them (the iron tools) at the extremities, or at the head, it is necessary to avoid.
Over that which is from them due to swelling of the artery opening, find in the skin incision along its length. Then open the incision with scissors, afterwards the artery: and release it from the tunics until it is exposed.
Then insert beneath it the awl and make it penetrate to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread at two places, according to what I taught you regarding the extraction of two arteries which are in the temples.
Then prick the place which is between two ligaments with a lancet until all blood comes out, and dissolve the abscess.
Then administer a treatment that produces pus until the ligaments fall off: afterwards treat it with appropriate ointments until it is healed.
If it is an abscess due to a vein cut, then it is necessary that you hold with your hand what is possible from the abscess with skin. Then insert the awl beneath the place that you held with your hand, and make it penetrate: and let there be a double thread in it until you pull it out from the other side. Then tie the abscess with a good ligament: according to what I said to you regarding ligating a vein, from two parts with double ends of thread.
If you fear that the thread may be pulled out, then insert another awl with another thread beneath the entire abscess near the incision: press and tie your threads at four places.
Then cut the abscess in the middle of it until when it comes out what is in it: then cut off excess skin and let go of that which was tied from it.
Then place on top of the smallpox blister that you have submerged in wine, and oil. Administer the treatment which is made with linen cloths and ointments until it heals.
Head L.
On paralysis that occurs due to twisting of the nerves.
As an aposteme occurs in arteries and veins, so does it occur in nerves; this happens to them due to a blow or excessive labor, or similar causes; and they mainly happen in places of joints, heels, and in any place where the connections are moved; and this aposteme is severe.
It resembles its color to the rest of the body and is found in many forms without pain; and when it is tightened with violence, it feels weak, like in a state of numbness.
And the aposteme is not gathered deep within the body, but it is under the skin; and it moves to all parts, and does not reach forward or backward.
Therefore, what is found in joints should not be pierced with iron. Perhaps it will cause a contraction.
In the one that is found on the head or forehead, puncture the skin with a lancet. If the aposteme is small, then hold it with forceps and cut it off at the root.
If it is large, then hang it up with a hook and pare it; afterwards remove it, and sew the wound with suture; and treat it until it heals.
Head LII.
On incision of an aposteme that occurs in the abdomen.
Occasionally, certain men have recurring boils in their bellies and in other parts of their bodies, which are called "Fungalia," due to their similarity with mushrooms.
Their root is subtle, and the head of them is thick, and they have turned-over lips on them. And from it there is a small one: and from it there is what can be magnified greatly.
I myself have seen a man whose belly had two boils, which were more like mushrooms than other things: there was no difference between them; they were white, with thin roots, and their lips were turned-over, and they burst, and moisture always flowed out of them.
I then cut them, and found that one weighed about X and VIII ounces, and the other about VI ounces. The operation for cutting them is this: if the patient is weak and the boil is white, moist, with a thin root, then cut it with a wide spatula, and have cautery ready in your presence.
For often blood is expelled at the cutting of it: so beware if you are overcome by blood, then cauterize it.
If you see a weak, fearful and timid person afraid of cutting with iron, then take a well-made silk thread, and bind it with it: its method is the one I have said, and let him go for two days.
Then add to the binding of the silk thread. Therefore do not cease to bind the lead thread as often as it presses on the boil until it is cut off and falls out without effort.
If the boil is large at the root, then there is a fear and terror in cutting it, especially since it is in the belly.
It is possible to cut it in half. Then cauterize it, so that it does not return.
Then cure it, until the wound heals.
And beware of cutting what is black and has few senses, with a foul appearance; for it is a cancerous aposteme, and I will pay (for) this when reminded of Cancer afterwards.
Chapter LII.
Chapter on the treatment of the protrusion of the umbilicus.
A protrusion of the umbilicus arises from many causes. It arises either from fistulas (sifac) above the abdomen and out comes the althub or the intestine, according to what happens in other ruptures. It arises either from blood flowing from a vein, or from an artery, as mentioned before. It arises from a constriction of wind there (in the navel area).
But if it is due to a fistula (sifac), and the passage of pus: then its colour is like that of an abscess; it is filled with pus without pain; and its position appears different. And if it is due to the passage of the intestine: then its position, as previously mentioned, is of a much more pronounced difference. When you press it with your fingers, it disappears; then it returns and perhaps there is a sound; and it swells greatly at the entrance of the bath, and there is much pain.
But if it is due to moisture: then it is soft; when you press it with your hand, it does not disappear, nor can it be constricted, nor does it increase in size.
If it is due to blood: then with these signs (inflammation and swelling) the abscess appears black at the navel.
But if it is due to fleshy matter: then the abscess is large, hard and solid, and its size increases by a single degree.
If it is due to wind: then when touched, it is soft.
And the operation in this case is to examine whether the protrusion of the navel is due to blood from an artery or vein, or wind: then it is necessary to forbid treatment of it. For in this case there is fear and dread, as I taught you in the chapter where I spoke of abscesses due to an artery or vein.
If the protrusion of the navel is due to an intestine or hernia: then it is necessary that you instruct the patient, so that he holds his breath and stands still, extended. Then make the signs with encaustic around the entire navel. Then instruct him to lie down on his back between your hands. Then surround with a broad spatula around the navel on the place you marked with encaustic. Then extend the middle of the incision upward with a large hook. Then tie him up around the navel with strong thread or silk cord: and let the knot of the ligature be alexandrine.
Then open the extended incision above the ligature. If you then find it already captured by the ligature: then extract the hernia, and introduce your index finger into it, and push the intestine towards the interior of the abdomen: and if you find a hernia, then take it with a hook, and cut off its excess.
If however, it is an artery or vein opposite to you: then surround it much. Then return to your operation. Then take two needles and insert two strong threads into them: and insert two needles into the circle you made around the tumor in the manner of a cross, which you make penetrate.
Then string the tumor in four places on the needles: and if you wish, remove the needles, and leave room, until the extended flesh rots away by itself: or cut it when it becomes tender and rots.
Then take care of him with what is necessary from ointments until he is healed.
If the protrusion of the navel is from a sore in him, or from moisture: then it is necessary to hollow out the tumor, as we have said. And draw out the blood, or moisture, that you find in it.
Then take care of him with whatever solidifies the place.
Chapter LIII.
[Title: On the Treatment of Cancer]
We have already said about the species of Cancer in division, and the way to treat it with medicines; and beware when treating it with iron, not to ulcerate it; we have said that Cancer is generated in the matrix, and cautery should be avoided in its treatment.
The ancients said that sometimes Cancer is in a place where it can be eradicated; such as Cancer which is in the breast or hip and similar limbs, to extract the entire thing of it; particularly when it is beginning small.
When however it becomes old, and is large, it should not be approached [for removal].
For I myself was unable to cure anyone from it; nor have I ever seen anyone else who has reached that point.
And the operation on it, when it is located as we have said, is to precede [the patient] and dissolve the weak from black choler several times. Then, if you find a phlebotomy with a clear overfilling.
Then prepare the patient with a preparation, in which it is located during the operation.
Then throw hooks that fit [the cancer] into Cancer. Then hollow out Cancer from every part with the skin, according to examination, until nothing remains of its roots; and let the blood run out, and do not cut it quickly, but rather press out the places and remove all the coarse blood by hand or as possible there with instruments.
If however a flow of coarse blood from the incision of an artery or vein opposes you; then cauterize the vein until the blood is cut off. Then care for it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
[Section on the care of hydrophysis.]
Chapter LIV. [44] We now speak of the classification of hydropic conditions, and how water accumulates; and the signs of every type, and its treatment with medicines.
That which is treated with iron, is only the scrofulous type; it should not be treated with iron for the tympanic condition; nor deeply for the hypersarcous condition, for that is fatal.
When you have been treated for this hydropic condition of the tympanic type with medicines and the treatment has not helped, then consider it. For if weakness has already come to the sick person or there is another illness besides hydropic condition, such as cough or loose bowels, and similar ones, then beware not to treat it with iron, for that is dangerous.
If however you see the sick person with excessive strength and no other illness besides hydropic condition; and if he is not a child or an old man, then there is room for operation in him. You raise the sick person standing between your hands, and the attendant presses out his belly with his hand to force water down towards the lower part of the chest.
Then take a splint with thorns, in this shape. Let it be made of two sharp parts, long, and with pointed ends like a splint. However, let there be something short within it, so that it does not penetrate as far during the operation to the intestine and injure it.
Then consider it. For if the hydropic condition is generated from the intestines, then it should be extended by cutting with a measurement of three fingers below the navel towards the lower parts above the breastbone.
But if the hydropic condition is due to liver disease, then your incision should be on the left side, three fingers below the navel.
If its generation is due to the spleen, then make a section on the right side: and it is not necessary that there should also be a section on the side toward which the sick person will lie, so as not to run superfluities to that weak place.
Then, perforate the entire skin with an instrument. Then insert into that incision and elevate your hand with a spatula beneath the skin, as if you are scraping it; and let the quantity that is scraped off be about the size of a nail or slightly more.
Then pierce the spatula until the spatula reaches an empty place: and that is the location of water. Then remove it (the sponge), and insert into the opening an instrument with this shape. And it is similar to a cannula: it is made of silver or copper or brass, polished; at its lower part there is a small hole, and on the sides there are three holes, two on one side and one on the other; and its end is cut like the end of a reed, as you see; at its upper end is a ring.
For when the instrument reaches water, then it (the water) immediately descends upon the instrument, therefore evacuate from the water an amount equal to a half hour.
Since if you evacuate more than is necessary from it, perhaps the sick person will die of a resolution of his animal spirits; or an approaching syncope occurs which approaches death.
But evacuate from it according to its potency and according to what the signs of the sick person's condition indicate to you by the force of his pulse and by the quality of his humors.
Then remove the instrument and retain the water.
Because it (the water) is retained immediately because of the skin which holds the hole that is on the sponge; about which I told you to pierce it in this way.
Then on the second day, if you see the patient can bear it: extract also a small amount from water.
Carry it out for some days without fear, and be careful to avoid error until there remains in the water only a little.

Chapter LIX.

Chapter Sixty.
Chapter on the Extraction of a Stone.
We have already said about the types of stones, and their cure with medicines; and we distinguished between a stone generated in kidneys, and bladder, and its signs; and we explained that an operation is performed on the stone when it is in the hand or sectioned; and this stone specifically arises in the bladder; and that which is formed in a rod; and I am telling you this with clear explanation and abbreviation.

Perhaps a finger, which is within the anus and presses against the stone during surgery, comes out easily.

Chapter 61.
Chapter on the extraction of stones in women.
Stones are scarcely generated in women.
If a stone happens to any of them (women), then the treatment is difficult and it is forbidden on account of many reasons.

Then insert the ray upon that cut. If he feels the stone, then he should enlarge the cut according to the amount proportional to the stone's exit.

Chapter LXII.
Section on a watery hernia.
A watery hernia is not anything but an accumulation of moisture inside the albido sac, which is under the skin containing the testicle and egg: and it is called the albido sac.
And sometimes it is within its own panniculus, which nature has prepared for it near the egg, until it appears as if it is an egg; and this is another egg, and it is between the albido sac of the testicle, which we have said: and this does not often happen.
And indeed the generation of this [watery hernia] is due to weakness that happens to testicles: therefore this matter flows into them. And sometimes it occurs from a blow on the testicles.
And this moisture has many colors. Or it has a color that is sloping towards citrinitas, or it is blood red, or feculent, black, or watery white: and this is what is more common.
And the signs by which one knows where the accumulation of water is located are these. Because if it is in the albido sac as we have said, then it is a tumor round and slightly smaller than an egg's length; and the testicle does not appear because moisture keeps it from all sides.
If there is moisture within its own sheath (sac), then the boil is round with part of the eye, and therefore man fears it because it is another egg.
If there is moisture between the skin of the testicles and the scrotum, then it falls under the sense (feeling or touch).
When the eye perceives the knowledge of the moisture's color, then to test the color of the moisture in a boil with an inserted square probe, whose shape precedes it. Therefore, according to what comes out in the footprint (impression) of the inserted probe, judge about that which is between it.
When we come to the cure with iron, then it is necessary that you command the patient, if possible for him, to be bled and see his body full (swollen).
Then he lies on his back on a raised bed, and place many cloths under him.

And if it appears to you that the operation should be one, then do it; afterwards remove the blood. And sometimes artificially this ramie stalk is medicated with a cautery in place of a section with iron: and it is to receive the subtle cautery-knife and cut the skin of the testicles with it: and it is to be heated, according to what we have narrated: until when the sifac album containing water is revealed: then receive the cautery, according to this form.
The letter forms resemble Greek letters.

And be careful not to let fire touch the egg.
And know that this operation is safer and more distant from bleeding than the operation with section, and better.

Treatise on the care of fleshy roots.
Know that in the section on this fleshy root, there is danger of slipping into ruin in many positions. Therefore it seems to me that its release is saved from that.

Chapter LXV.
Chapter on the care of Intestinal Roots.
The outlet of this root is from an incision which occurs on the extended sigmoid colon in the inguinal part of the stomach.
Because the intestines descend through that rupture to one testicle. And this rupture is either from the sigmoid colon or its extension.
And these two types occur due to various causes: either from a blow, a jump, a shout, lifting a heavy object, and similar things.
And the mark, when it is from extension of sifach. It happens gradually over a long period of time and does not occur suddenly; it is an abscess deep in the direction of the extension; therefore, because sifach compresses the intestine.
And its sign is when it is from section of sifach, because it causes a sudden intense pain at the start; and it is an abscess different, appearing under the skin close by; and that is due to the outflow of intestine and its course towards exterior sifach.
And sometimes it comes out with the intestine called zirbum; and this is called an Intestinal Ramification, and zirbia; and sometimes it happens with flatulence.
And sometimes it runs into the intestine with feces and is retained there; and that brings about the peril of the sick person; because it causes a bad pain, especially when it is compressed.
And in treating the affliction of this disease with iron there is fear; therefore, one must be careful about the occurrence in it.
And the method of operation is to order the sick person to push his intestine back with his hand towards the hollows of its own cavity if he obeys the command. Then he lies down on his neck over your hands and elevate his legs.
Then stretch the skin that follows the skin to the upper part, and cut the entire skin of the testicles in length. Then make two cauls on the lips of the incision according to what you need to open the incision with them; and the incision should be according to the quantity, so that it is possible for an egg to come out from there.
Then scrape the sifach, and what is under the skin of the testicles until the white sifach appears hard from all sides; then insert your index finger into what follows the testicle, in that which is between the white sifach, which is under the skin of the egg, and between the sifach and the abscess, without adhesion to it that is in the back part of the egg.
Then move your right hand towards the inner skin of the testicles, and as you do this, extend the albumen upward with your left hand, and lift out the egg with the albumen to the part of the incision. And command the servant to stretch out the egg upward. You solve the adherence which is behind complete solution.
Ask your fingers if there is nothing there from the intestine rolled up in the hard albumen. If you find something from that, then push it down towards the lower belly.
Then take the probe, in which is a thick thread made of linen from ten threads, and insert it at the last albumen, that is, the membrane which follows the incision: namely, under the skin of the testicles. Then cut the ends which project from the thread until there are four threads. Then arrange some of them over others in the shape of a cross, and tie the thread we mentioned (the strong ligament under the skin of the testicles) to them until it cannot let any of the secretions which nourish them pass through to them, so that no hot abscess occurs there. And place another ligature beyond the first ligature, at a distance from it less than two fingers. And after these two ligatures, release the thread which is under the skin of the testicles, a quantity equal to the size of a finger, and cut the rest in a rounded manner and remove the egg.
Then cut at the lower part of the skin of the testicles with an incision from which blood and pus flow, as we said in what was mentioned before.
Then apply the thread soaked in oil and place it on the wound, and apply the ligature we mentioned. And sometimes cauterize the hard albumen which we said before, after the incision of it, fearing from the flow of blood. Multotiens enim accidit illud. translates to "It happens often that this occurs." in English. "Let go of the ligament until it falls by itself." (in English)
"If the case does not proceed, then boil it with hot water; and place on top of it what I said until it falls." (in English)
"Then take care of the wound with the usual treatment for wounds, until it is healed." (in English)

"Chapter LXVII" (in English)
"[A Case] On a Rupture that occurs in the groins" (in English, title of the case)
"When a rupture occurs in the groins, as I have said, and there is an empty place, and nothing from the intestines descends to the testicles; and if it does descend, that is not enough, and it returns in all hours; but if it lasts for a time with this, a tear is added in the sifach [hernia], until the intestines descend into the sifach." (in English)
"And this occurs due to extension of the hernia, which is in the groins, as I have said." (in English) "That is because the hernia extends; then it is softened and the place is stretched out, and it emerges." (in English)
And its treatment is with a cautery, as his previous narrative states.
And sometimes it is treated with iron, according to this method: and there is [a way] for the sick person to lie on his back upon your hands. Then cut the place of the rupture and protrusion, with a cut across its width, according to the size of three fingers.
Then tie the alsi-fak and whatever is beneath the skin until the white al-sifach appears, which is beneath the skin that follows it.
Then take a probe and place it over the protruding part of the al-sifach and press it to the depth of the belly.
Then make two incisions on the extremity of the radius from the al-sifach and sew them together with a stitch; then remove the extremity of the radius.
Do not incise the al-sifach at all, nor tear the ovum [yolk sac], nor anything else, as I have instructed you in treating intestinal branches.
Then treat that with wound treatment. When you make stitches, clean it and heal the wound until it heals.
The sisycon [certain type of plant fiber] contracts, and does not add to the protrusion of the rupture.
And the cautery is better for this place, because it is closer to healing.
Chapter LXVIII.
Chapter on softening the scrotal skin.
The skin of the testicles is often softened in some men, on account of which the meats between them are softened and its appearance becomes foul.
Therefore, it is necessary for the one who is asked to treat it (the testicles), that he makes the sick man lie on his back and cuts off all the softened skin that is on top of the natural skin.
Then gather two lips together with stitching: and if you wish, or even more so, remove the excess of the softened skin by three or four stitches, and make a firm stitch.
Then cut between the stitches.
Then care for the healing of the remaining wounds until they are healed and the threads fall off.
Chapter LXIX.
[Title: On Castration.]
Know that castration is forbidden by our law: and therefore it would be appropriate for me not to remember it in this book of mine; and there is no need to remember it except for two reasons.
One reason is that it should be known by the physician when he is asked about it: and so that he knows the treatment for the one who suffers from it.
And another method is that we often need castration of certain animals, for the benefit of our needs through it, such as sheep, hyracids, and cats, and similar ones from animals.
Therefore, I say that castration is done according to two methods. Or by grinding. Or by cutting and separation.
In that which is done by grinding, the way of the operation is: what we should do is make the animal sit in warm water until its testicles soften and relax and hang down; then grind them with your hand until they resolve and no longer appear upon touch.
In castration by cutting and separation, it is necessary that you hold the animal and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.
Then tie the sack, and cut above all the egg in one section, until when two eggs come out: then cut what is left after you have scoured each one, and do not leave anything on it beyond the thin skin, which is over the vessels.
And this method of castration is better than the one by grinding, since grinding possibly leaves something from the testicles, which causes the animal to desire coitus.
Then take care of the wound until it heals.
Chapter 70.
Chapter on the care of Hermaphrodite in two methods.
Hermaphrodite from men is according to two modes. One of them is that it appears in him in the space between the testicles or on the skin of the testicles, in which is located a figure resembling a female vulva with hairs; and sometimes urine flows out from the part that is on the skin of the testicles.
In women, however, there is one species, and it is a female vulva on the mons pubis like small testicles of a man, projecting to the outside; of which one is like the priapus of a man, and two are like two testicles.
And the treatment of three kinds, two from males, and one kind from females, is: because it is necessary that you make incisions in the added flesh, until the impression of them flees away. Then treat those wounds with the remedies used for other wounds.
Furthermore, in the second kind of male, which originates from where urine comes out that is on the skin of the testicles, there is no operation, nor is there any treatment for it at all.
Chapter 71.
Chapter on the incision of Tentiginis and the protruding flesh in women's wounds.
A Tentiginis may be added beyond what is natural, until it becomes foul and ugly to look at; and sometimes it swells so much in certain women that it spreads like in men and reaches copulation.
Therefore, you must hold the excess of Tentiginis with your hand or with a probe, and make an incision; not deep into the incision, especially at the root, so that there is no bleeding.
Then treat the Tentiginis itself with the remedies used for wounds, until it heals.
The flesh that arises is the flesh that is born in the opening of the womb until it fills it; and perhaps it comes out on the outside, similar to a tail; and therefore some call the condition 'caudated'. Therefore, it must be cut like the Tentiginis is cut and treated until it heals.
Chapter on the treatment of an abscess in a woman that has not burst open.
Chapter 72.
An abscess in a woman that has not burst open or has a small opening is called Alratic. And it may be either natural or accidental.
An abscess caused by a preceding illness is accidental; and it may be formed from added flesh, or from fat or pus; and it may occur in the deep parts of the womb, or on its sides, or above or below it; and it prevents copulation, conception, childbirth, and perhaps menstruation.
And the knowledge of it is obtained through an obstetrician's examination, if the circumcision is apparent nearby.
If it is not apparent, then seek it with your fingers or with a probe.
If the circumcision is from a subtle sifach and is close to two lips: then pull it out, and tear it apart.
And it should be placed on two lips (lips of the vulva).
Then place your index fingers of both hands together, and let the woman be on her back with her legs spread apart. Then stretch the two lips with force until the subtle sifach tears and the circumcision opens up.
Then take wool and moisten it with oil, and place it on the site; let the woman apply it every day to prevent the area from healing in another way.
If the sifach is large and thick: then it should be cut off with a broad spatula or a leaf of myrtle.
If the circumcision is of flesh born, then suspend it with hooks and cut it; have medicines with you that stop blood flow without causing pain, such as acacia, dragon's blood, and onion juice mixed with egg white.
Then administer a wide cannula made of lead to prevent the wound from healing quickly, hold it for several days; then apply linen cloth, then treat the rest of the healing process until it heals.
And sometimes a birth of flesh (of other creatures) occurs in the womb: therefore, they should be cut according to this method: if there is no cancerous abscess, do not make any contrast with iron at all, because it may cause harm.
Head LXXIII.
Chapter on the treatment of hemorrhoids, by Athehelil and Botheor for women.
Hemorrhoids indeed are the opening of the vein's outlets, as long as much blood continuously runs from them.
If hemorrhoids become chronic, they become piles; and I have already said about their species and their signs in the division of them, and here I will say what receives treatment from them and what does not.
Therefore, I say that hemorrhoids which are in the opening of the womb and do not appear to the sense, then there is no treatment for it with iron.
But those which are on the opening of the womb above where the sense falls upon them, are those that can be treated.
Therefore it is necessary to introduce a woman into a cold house. Then stretch out the piles with forceps or rough cloth, and cut them from their roots.
Then sprinkle powder over them near the flow of blood from one of the incisions without biting; such as alum, dragon's blood, sulfur and similar things.
Then press his feet against the wall at the hour of one. After that, place her in cold water.
If the flow of blood persists: then make her sit in a decoction of sumac, rind of pomegranates, and walnuts, and similar things.
Then take barley flour, mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it on his back.
If the blood is cut off with it, that is good; and if not, make adhesive windbags and breasts, without scarification.
Then take wool, immerse it in the juice of tarathith, or the juice of arnoglossum, or the juice of the branches of aalaulatus (that is, alanthe), Pontic wine and make it adhere to the wound.
When the abscess becomes quiet, then care for the place with ointments until it heals.
Albarth is red and resembles the heads of a scallion (alhaasse), and has a rough appearance.
Therefore, it is necessary to excise what appears from it, as I said regarding the onion (thelil), equally; and take care of it until it heals.
Chapter LXXIIII.
[Chapter] On the Perforation of the Extrusion that occurs in the Womb.
In the matrix (womb) various appearances of abscesses occur, such as cancer, stone abscess, ulcers, adubelati, alekilati (herpes), fistulae, hemorrhoids, ragadiae, thelil, and hot abscess.
And I myself have already said all these illnesses and their appearances, their signs, and their cures are divided. It is necessary that in this treatise I speak about the hot abscess in the matrix (womb) which occurs among the abscesses which gather pus, and you should know how to open it with iron.
Therefore, one must consider. Then if the pain of the abscess at its onset is sharp with beating and burning and fever, and it appears red; if it lies upon the sensation, then do not puncture it; and cure it with what gives relief according to its maturation, until the acuity of the symptoms subsides.
Then one must make the woman sit on two seats with a gap between them and recline or lean against her back, and place her feet to the lower part of the belly; and let her hips be spread out, and put her arms under her knees and tie each arm with a bandage connecting them to that.
Then the midwife should sit on the right side, and administer the instrument for opening the matrix (womb) orifice.
And it is necessary when you are to administer this instrument that you form a point with the rod deep into the woman's matrix (womb); so that what enters from the instrument is not more than the depth of the matrix, and does not harm the weak.
If the instrument is more than deep, then one must place powder (pulverized charcoal) on top of the depth of the matrix; so that the entry of the instrument is not to the full depth of the matrix; and one must place a weight (lead) which runs in the instrument from the upper side, and hold the instrument and rotate the worker (assistant) with the weight, until the depth of the matrix is opened.
When it appears to be excised and touched by hand, and is soft and yielding: then it is necessary that you cut it off at its base with a broad spatula.
When pus is discharged, then it is necessary to place a linen cloth soaked in rose oil or green oil, which has some styptic property, on the wound; and then make an incision into the matrix deeply.
And place outside [the body], on the matrix and on the comb, a clean wool soaked in water in which bitter apples have been boiled.
Then it should be treated with an appropriate ointment for two days until it heals.
And at times the matrix and the wound are cleaned so that it is cleansed with water and honey; then with water in which the root of the lily has been boiled, or long aristolochia; then return to the ointment.
If the wound is hidden inside the matrix, then it is necessary to refrain from treating it with iron; rather, treat it as we have said for division.
Chapter LXXX.
Book of Obstetrics: How to treat living embryos that have emerged abnormally.
It is necessary for an obstetrician to first know the shape of a normal delivery.
From the signs of this, it is known that when you see a woman pressing downwards and she desires to smell the air, and urine is passed over her in childbirth, and she hastens the exit of the embryo: then know that this delivery is according to its natural shape, and the outlet is above the head and second outlet with it; or suspended, or hanging from the navel.
When you see these signs, then it is necessary to press the abdomen of the woman so that the embryo descends quickly.
When it [the instrument] descends upon his head, it [the second one] also descends with it, and it is to be cleansed from those superfluities with good purification.
Whoever is beyond this delivery is unnatural, inaudible.
Because sometimes the fetus comes out with its feet first, and its body comes out before its head, and its feet or one hand: or the head comes out and one hand: or the intestines come out: and perhaps it turns over on its neck, and similar unnatural figures.
Therefore it is necessary for the midwife to be prudent, subtle in all these matters and to guard against error and deception; and I am showing every figure of them, and how there is skill in it, and it will be indicated by that, and it will stand upon it.
When the fetus comes out with its head in a natural delivery, and it becomes violent upon the woman, and the delivery is difficult for her, and you see its strength already weakened: then make her sit on a stool, or women hold her; and have her take deep breaths with fennel water boiled, and with moist oils.
Then the midwife introduces a small spatula between her fingers, and grabs the second one with it, and cuts it with her nail until it runs out of moisture; and she presses the woman's abdomen until the fetus descends.
If it does not descend, then it is necessary to cleanse the woman with mucilage of fennel, with oil of sesame.
Then command her after the cleansing to press down; and make her sneeze with pepper, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour. The fetus will come out immediately.
If two hands of the fetus emerge first, it is necessary to reduce them gently and gradually. If it does not obey at the entrance [of childbirth], then place the woman on a seat, and lift her feet upwards; then strike the seat upon the ground; and hold the woman, so that she does not fall during the shock.
If the hands do not emerge and the fetus dies; then cut them off, and extract the remaining fetus; and bind its hand with cloth, and extract it equally; for it will come out by itself.
The emergence of the embryo is upon the feet of itself. When the fetus emerges upon its feet, then it should be pushed upwards; then it should be slowly turned; afterwards, it should be delivered equally.
Then, take one of his feet and stretch it out gradually.
When they [the legs] emerge up to the hips, then command her [the woman] to bear down and make her sneeze with a blow; for it will come out if God wills.
And if it does not come out as we have said, then draw the fetus back gradually until you place it in its natural position. For it will come out then with an easy delivery.
If it is prevented from coming out as we have said; then take some mucilage of aloe, and oil of sesame, and dissolved gum; and grind it all together in a mortar with good blows; afterwards, apply the paste to the woman's vulva and below her belly. Then make her sit in warm water until the uterus descends [to its normal position].
When you see that the lower parts have become warm, then give her something to drink made of myrrh; and place it [the myrrh] beneath her. When therefore the hour is one, then make her sit on a chair. Then make her sneeze: and pinch her own nose and nostril: and press the lower part of the abdomen gently with compression. For the feces will come out immediately.
Delivery on the knees and hands. When it comes out in this manner, then insert your hands gently. Then the woman lies on her back with her head down and legs hanging: and she remains lying on the bed and folds her hands. Then press gently on her abdomen. Then take out what is under her feet from the bedding, until it is prepared below. If the fetus does not come out, then take hold of her feet and move them vigorously. Then press gently on what is above the pubic bone until the fetus rises towards the upper parts. Then insert your hands and guide the fetus gently: and command the woman to press until the fetus is born.
Delivery of the fetus, hanging sideways from the hands. Insert your hand to reduce [the size]. If it cannot be reduced, then lift the woman and make her walk.
If she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed: and strike her legs with a violent blow.
Then apply the ointment you have prepared from gums [of certain trees].
If she gives birth, then make her sit on a chair. Then strive to reduce the hand [or arm] and guide the fetus according to its natural shape: make her sneeze and command her to press until it is born.
The outcome of the fetus is above its neck, with open hands, and its face is towards the back of its mother. The midwife must hold the baby's hand, then gradually turn it, and adjust it easily.
When it is adjusted, then place it over the mouth we previously mentioned with oil and mucilage.
Then command him to move slowly. When you have done that, then make her sit on a seat, and command her to lean towards the right side. Then command her to compress (the birth canal), and cause her to sneeze with a strong blow.
The prepared baby comes out on the side. When the second child descends into the mother's birth canal in this manner with the afterbirth, then cut the afterbirth with your nail until it is expelled due to moisture.
If the baby hangs over the face and its neck, then cut it from the navel so that it is not retained and dies.
Then push the baby inside until you place it as required; and command the woman to compress herself several times, for it will come out easily.
The birth of twins or multiple babies. Know that twins often give birth; and sometimes they give birth to three, and even four. However, that is unusual and rarely occurs.
Five is indeed an abnormal thing, and they do not live long; it contains them, even though there are many afterbirths; and they are separated by the cord, distinguishing between them tied at the navel of each one.
Sometimes they come out like a single baby does naturally and easily; and sometimes they come out in an unnatural way as we have described.
If some of them are difficult during childbirth and reach what we said in unnatural figures, then treat them as we have described: it should be subtle and do what is done with ease and slowness, and adapt according to every figure with what is prepared for him guided by his intellect towards recovery.
¶ Remember that which is formed in the womb from embryos and are aborted.
Sometimes one, two, three, four, five, six, seven and more than ten are formed in the womb: and it is already verified by me, that a woman, while giving birth, has emitted seven, and another fifteen, all of them formed.
What was done through the measurement of the glorious wise man.
Therefore, all of this should be in the knowledge of Obstetrics. Perhaps it will reach a similar one: oppose to it, as necessary.
Chapter LXXVI.
¶ On the extraction of the dead fetus.
When you care for a dead fetus with what was said in the division of medication and it does not leave, and you will be forced to use an operation with hand, then it is necessary that you consider.
If the woman is of good health and has no accident from which her death is feared: then it is necessary that the woman lies down on the bed, on her back, and her head should be inclined lower, and her legs raised: and the assistant should hold her from two sides, or she should be tied to the bed, so that her body does not be pulled during the extraction of the fetus.
Then, the womb is moistened with oils rich in moisture (humid oils) with almond mucilage and fenugreek seeds, and linseed.
Then the midwife shall insert her hand along with those oils and mucilages; then she shall introduce it into the womb with ease. Then let her seek a place where to fix hooks on the fetus, and locations suitable for that.
Then consider whether the fetus is prepared to descend upon its head: then fix hooks into its eyes, or at its neck, or mouth, or palate, or under its beard, or at its armpit, or near the ribs, and below the hips.
If it is a descent upon its feet, then fix hooks in the chest, and at the middle of the ribs.
And it is necessary that she holds the hook with her right hand; and let her place a loop on it between the fingers of her left hand; and introduce it with her hand with ease, and fix the hook in one of those locations which we mentioned, until she arrives at the emptiness.
Then fix another hook, or a third one if necessary, on the opposite side: so that the contraction may be equal and not incline to any side.
Then it shall be extended with an equal extension, and the extension should not be straight only, but rather moved to all sides, so that the passage may be alleviated: just as it is done with a tooth during its extraction.
And let there be softened at that place the extension. If a part is held back from it, then the midwife should insert some fingers with oil on that side, to turn what is being held back along with them.
If a part of the fetus is coming out, then the hooks shall be changed to another higher location; do this until the entire fetus comes out.
If a hand or another part is coming out and it cannot be returned because of its constriction; then let a cloth be wrapped around it. Then extract it completely until it emerges wholly, cut it either at the joint of the foot or at the elbow; and so it must be done in one hand, and in both feet.
If the head of the fetus is large or it encounters dislocation during birth, or water has accumulated around its head; then one must introduce a spiny spatula between the fingers and crush the head with it, and extract the water, or rupture it with the instrument called Almisdac; whose form comes among the forms of other instruments in the chapter following this.
Likewise, if the fetus is of large head nature, then one must make a cut with scissors (algengematu); or extract it with forceps (misdach), as we have said. Then draw out the bones with forceps.
If the head emerges and becomes dislocated at the neck; then it should be crushed until the moisture within the chest is released.
If it does not twist and does not comply for birth; then cut the head piecemeal, as far as you can manage.
If below the abdomen there is an apostema or it has hydropsy; then one must puncture it until the moisture runs out from it.
If the fetus is above its feet, then its extraction is easy and its guidance towards the birth canal is light.
If it becomes dislocated in the abdomen or chest; then one must extract it with a swaddling cloth that you have wrapped over your hand; and puncture the abdomen or chest until what is within them runs out.
If the rest of the body is removed and the head returns; then the midwife must introduce her left hand. If the birth canal is open, then introduce your hand deeply into the birth canal and search for the head, and extract it with your fingers up to the birth canal; then insert a hook or hooks and extract it with them.
If the bone of the matrix is strained, due to a hot abscess that has happened to it: then it is not appropriate for him to be operated upon on it, but rather it is appropriate at that time to administer an infusion of moist substances, oily; and apply plasters; and sit in waters which soften and moisten.
If the fetus is on his side, then it can be turned: then administer what was said for a living fetus.
If that cannot be done, then cut it in pieces and extract it.
And it is necessary not to leave anything from the second part inside at all.
When you have completed your operation, then administer what was said for hot abscesses that occur in the matrix.
If bleeding occurs, then descend into waters of sulfur, and administer the rest of the treatment.
And indeed I have seen a woman whose womb contained a dead fetus; then she became pregnant again on top of it, afterwards another fetus also died within her. After a long period of time, an abscess occurred in his navel, and it became swollen until it was opened; and he began to discharge pus.
I was therefore summoned for his treatment, and I treated him for a long time; but the wound did not heal.
Therefore, I placed on it from some strong plasters of attraction; and the bone came out from that place. Then a few days passed for him, and another bone came out. I was astonished then, because there is no bone in the womb.
Therefore, it occurred to me that they were bones of dead fetuses.
I therefore asked the wound, and extracted many bones, the woman being in good condition; and she lived thus for a long time, and scarcely discharged pus from that place.
And I did not bind here this foreign one, except because in it is knowledge, and assistance to that which the healing artist administers with his hand for treatment.
Chapter LXXVII.
On the forms of necessary instruments for extracting the fetus.
The form of the screw (screwdriver) that opens the cervix (matrix).
Here is the form of the Tortoise-shaped forceps (Stricture), which equalize books, having equally two screws at the ends of two pieces of wood. Moreover, this Screw should be finer than the forceps: and to make it so, either from ebony or from boxwood.
And the thickness of all the wood should be as two fingers: and the edge of each of both is as one finger, and the length of each of them is a palm and a half: and in the middle of two pieces of wood there are two additional parts made from the same kind of wood, which have already been firmly attached to each, whose length is half a palm or less: and the width of each of them is as two fingers or less.
And these two additional parts are inserted into the cervix (matrix), so that it opens with them when you rotate the screws (two vertical screws).
Another form similar to it, finer and lighter.
Make it from ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of the forceps. Moreover, at the end of it (the second form) there should be two additional parts as you can see here above: and the length of each additional part is approximately a palm: and the width of each of them is as two fingers.
When you wish to open the cervix with it (the second form), then make the woman sit on the bed, with her legs apart, opening what is between her thighs. Then insert these two joined additional parts into the cervix: and you hold the end of the instrument below, between her thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument as you do with forceps, equally according to the degree of opening of the cervix, until the midwife does what she wants.
Form of Vertigo different from that which the ancients called Form of Pushing, by which the fetus is pushed.
The form (instrument) of Moldac, with which a large head is crushed, resembling a pair of forceps, as you see, having teeth at the end.
And sometimes it becomes hook-like, like forceps in this form, as you see, having teeth like the teeth of a saw, with which it is cut and crushed.
The form (instrument) of Uncus having one spine.
The form (instrument) of Uncus having two spines.
The form (instrument) of Spathulis having two ends for cutting off the head.
The form (instrument) of two wider Spathulis.
All these instruments are applied, and the more varied their forms become, and the more prepared they are by the craftsman, the faster they are in their action, and higher among humans, due to their quantity.
Therefore, do not disregard one of these instruments as being prepared for you. Indeed, it is inexcusable for their necessity.
Chapter LXXVIII.
Chapter on the second extraction (cesarean section).
When Second is retained during childbirth, then it is necessary to command the weak one to hold her breath. Cause her to sneeze when you bind [her]: and press your hand upon her nose and her own nostrils. If it comes out by this means, that is good.
If it does not [come out]: then take a pot and make a hole in the covering [of the instrument]; and put into it herbs opening the womb, such as camomile, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia bark, centaury; take all these herbs or some of them, and immerse them in water, and place them over fire.
Then place a wick made of reed over the hole of the pot, and hold the other end upon the womb; and let it be until vapor reaches the concavity of the womb.
Then make her sneeze as we said before. For Second will come out easily.
If it remains after this treatment and does not come out: then order the midwife to dip her hand in sesame oil or marsh-mallow mucilage. Then insert [the instrument] into the cervix and seek Second with it. When you find it, then take it out gently.
If it is attached deeply in the womb, then insert your hand as I told you before until when you find Second and draw it out gently so that it does not fall down the womb with violent attraction; on the contrary, it should be moved easily from right to left; then add more to the amount of pressure. It will follow as a result, and she will conserve [the child] and it will pass from the adhesion.
If a bone of the matrix (womb) is dislocated, as we have already said: treat it with inducing cough and medication from an oil pot with herbs.
If it does not come out with everything that we have mentioned, then beware of exhausting yourself in the repetition of extraction.
It is necessary that what comes out from the bone of the matrix to her, you tie it to the woman's hip. Then enema her with four-ingredient ointment. For this reason it will rot her within days, dissolve and come out.
However, when it rots, the bad smell is raised to the stomach and head, and it harms the weak one (the woman). Therefore, suitable fumigations must be administered for this purpose.
Some of the ancients have already experienced that fumigation with nasturtium and dried figs is effective.
The form of the instrument with which a woman is fumigated during retention of the second delivery and menstruation.
Make it like a vessel similar to an alcama, or from zere: and let the wide end be above the fire: and the fumigation should be placed over plums: hold her until the fumigation is consumed: and repeat another one.
Chapter LXXIX.
[Section heading] On the treatment of an unperforated anus.
Many boys are born, and the anuses of some of them are not perforated, which have already been circumcised with a sharp scissors. The obstetrician must therefore pierce it (the cervix) with her finger; and if she cannot, she should pierce it with a spatula sharp (instrument); and let her be careful not to touch the muscle (with it).
Then place warm wool soaked in wine and oil on top of it (the wound). Then care for it with ointments until it heals.
If there is a fear that it may close up again, then place a lead cannula in the opening and remove it when the child wishes to be born.
And now, obstruction of the anus also occurs from the hardening of wounds or abscesses. Therefore, it must be cut (the obstruction), then treated with what was previously mentioned from treatment and lead.
Chapter LXXX. (80)
Chapter on the cure of fistulas that occur in the lower part (of the body).
Fistulas that occur in the lower part (of the body) are nodosities and swellings that occur near the anus outside; or in a space of one part; and there is one fistula, or more than one.
When the nodosity becomes old (hard), it opens and there runs from it a watery whiteness, or thin pus.
And sometimes they penetrate these fistulas. Therefore, they are recognized by what comes out during the discharge and wind, when a sick person uses it; and perhaps worms come out of them.
And there are fistulas (when they are) in spaces penetrating up to the bladder and to the intestine. And there are fistulas that penetrate up to the hip joint and to the coccygeal node.
From this (fact) it is known that a fistula penetrating up to the anus, even if not penetrating, is when you insert your index finger into the anus; and insert a thin probe made of copper or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting (of the intestine).
If there is a twist in it, then insert into it a slender probe made of lead or a horse hair, until you feel the probe, or a hair on your finger.
If you do not feel it fully or if nothing comes out through the opening nor any wind nor worms as I mentioned, then you will know that it is not penetrating; therefore, proceed to treatment.
When the fistula penetrates to the bladder or the membrane of urine: then its sign is the outflow of urine from it, and its prevention is that the location should be sealed with medicines.
But if it penetrates to the junction of the hip or to the hip bone: then its sign is that the probe reaches it, unless there is a twist in it up to the bone; and the discovery of pain around the area, and that pus always comes out from it; and that medicine does not work in it, nor does it heal with an ointment.
And in all these fistulas that penetrate there is no cure at all; and the cure for them is futile effort upon a fool, over whom it forms.
But in the one that does not penetrate and is not old, recovery is hoped for with a cautery; according to what I tell you, and I have already proven it: and there is, as I inform you, that the patient lies weak on his back between your hands; and you lift his legs up to above his hips, and his hips are inclined towards his abdomen. Then insert a probe of lead or copper if there is a twist in the fistula, until you know where the probe has reached.
But if the patient feels it around the anus, then you must insert your finger into the anus.
If you feel the probe penetrating by itself through what you have detected with your finger, beyond what you feel between your finger and the fistula or the flesh; then you will know certainly that it is penetrating; therefore, do not labor in it, because there is no cure for it, as we have said.
They say, however, that flesh heals in some men, and from the medication that is expected to be of help, it is, to apply a subtle cautery according to the size of the Fistula, as previously mentioned, and to introduce the ignited one into the Fistula until it reaches the anus. Then do this twice, or three times, until you know that all those added fleshes filtered, which are similar to the feathers of a bird's quill, have been burnt.
Then care for it with linens rolled in butter until those burnt fleshes come out; then care for it with ointments that generate flesh and consolidate it.
If therefore it heals, it is good.
And if not, then it will never heal with any other treatment.
And if it comes out and does not reach your finger that is in the anus, and there is a thick membrane of flesh or sifac between it and the probe; and you see the fistula following the skin surface, then cut the skin from the beginning of the fistula, and you go cutting with the probe until the incision reaches the end of the probe tip, and the probe is released and falls off.
Then clean those filtered fleshes similar to the feathers of a bird's quill, so that no part remains from them.
If however blood prevails over you and loosens between you and your operation, so that those fleshes fall off; then it is better what is done, and more expedient for help, to cauterize it with fire or with a sharp medicine.
Because the cautery with fire brings good results, the burning of those added fleshes and the removal of blood, and the drying out of moisture.
Then treat that with linen wound dressings soaked in butter, or boiled calves' horns, until the place emits pus, and the burnt flesh emerges into the pus.
Then treat the wound with hardening ointments that cause tough skin to grow: there are remedies which contain styptic and astringent substances.
For when it is being restored, then it will heal; do not fear repeated treatment.
If the fistula has reached into the deep of the anus and is extending from the body, then insert your finger into the anus and examine it.
If you feel a tumor between yourself and her, and it is covered with skin or flesh, and is near to penetration: then the operation should not be performed on that, except according to the way of trust and hope.
Because it is treated in one of three ways: either to cauterize it as we have said; or to cut it off, until you follow the depression of its hollow so that it is possible for you to insert linen and treatment from close by. And do not proceed too much with the cutting, so as not to cut the muscle containing the anus, and an accidental discharge of excrement without will occur. Then treat it with what I have said.
Perhaps it will heal itself; or stretch the skin, and cleanse it after you have cut it as we have said, either when there is a tumor, or with another tool of sharp point. Then cleanse the fleshy parts that are cut, until you can with examination.
Then attempt the restoration of the entire wound with cutting and the upper opening where it is consolidated; and the fistula remains open in the inner part of the anus, and it will be easier on the weak side.
And sometimes a fistula is drained in this manner: and it is when you insert a probe into the fistula, which is on the side of the anus near the surface of the body with skin and the edge of the anus. Then take a probe with perforated tip, which is like the aleskef point, that is, prepared from leather, in this shape. And insert into it a thread rolled up from five strands, and around it. Then insert the probe with the thread into the fistula until it reaches its concavity.
If it penetrates the edge of the anus internally, then pull out the thread from that hole in such a way that you insert your finger into the anus and draw out the end of the thread, and gather both ends together: and tighten each one, and let it go for one or two days: and the more the thread enters the flesh, tighten it well, until the flesh between the two ends of the thread falls out and drops: then take care of the wound until it heals.
But if the opening of the fistula is not penetrating: then make it penetrate in any way that you can prepare it, as long as it is not too deep. For you have no reason to do this for the sake of saving flesh, if you cut into it.
Then proceed as we said until it heals.
The form of the spatulis-spined probe for draining a fistula, whose sharpness is very acute on one side and the other side is not sharp, as you can see.
Chapter 81.
Chapter on the sewing of hemorrhoids from which blood flows upon their incision, and care for fissures.
Hemorrhoids are of two kinds. Within the anus are things resembling charcoal or plums; or as if they were grains of wheat. They are small and large; blood flows from them constantly, and there is one, and there are many of them. They are outside the anus, and at its extremities.
However, those that are outside the anus are usually of a little moisture, from which runs citrus water or not much blood with a constant flow; and they are according to the body's color.
The treatment of that which is within the anus is to instruct the patient to take a laxative; and it is expressed until it appears from the anus, and the athelia becomes apparent to you. Therefore, hang them with hooks; or hold them with your nail. Then cut them at their roots.
If they are not held by hooks due to their moisture and softening; then take them with a rough cloth or with a glove made of double wool, and pull them out with your fingers. Then cut them and sprinkle some hot powders over them after cutting to keep the area hot for cauterization. Or cauterize them according to what was stated in the previous chapter on cauterization. Then treat them with the rest of the treatment until they are healed.
If the anus does not obey the expulsion, then administer a laxative to the patient with a small purge, so that it cleanses what is in the anus, and the expulsion quickly obeys when the patient empties himself.
If the athelia are outside the anus, then their situation is light and easy; you take them with your nail or take them with a hook and cut them. Then take care of them as we have said, until they are healed.
If the incision is with iron, then one must administer suture in this manner. Take a thread rolled up and insert it into the point. Then pull out the athelil towards the upper part and make it penetrate with the point into the root on the other side; and roll up two ends of the thread, one on the lower part of the needle, and they should be broad; and tie the athelil tightly with a strong knot. Then tie the thread and draw out the needle.
Do this with all the athelils and leave one; do not sew it up, so as to avoid excess bleeding.
Then place a linen cloth soaked in rose oil or pitch over the anus and put it on the anus; and order the sick person to rest. Then let him go until he falls asleep.
When the athelils have fallen, take care of them with ointments, and with the remaining treatment, until they are healed.
Chapter on the Treatment of Fissures. For many times it happens due to drying of feces and constriction of nature.
If they have hardened and medicine does not work for them: then one must shave with a razor or with the nail until they become moist and remove the superficial layer that prevents their consolidation. Then take care of them until they consolidate as required.
If they do not consolidate: then shave them again with a stronger razor than the first, until they bleed a lot and then take care of them until they are healed.
Chapter on the Treatment of Worms and those not affected by worms; and on the Scurfy and Ants.
Head, LXXXII.
You should know that Almirmar is not anything other than a round knot resembling the head of a nail; it forms in the whole body but especially in the lower parts of the feet and fingers, and it causes pain during walking.
Therefore, it must be cut what is around the nail head and held with forceps or a tweezers and removed from its root.
Then take care of that (the wound) and, if you wish, cauterize it as described in the previous chapter.
From the athelil (a type of wart), one is a small, rough, filtered outgrowth that is round on the surface of the body. And they frequently occur in children's hands.
And its treatment is to stretch the athelil, cut it; or stitch it with silk thread or wool until it falls off. And if you wish, cauterize it with fire or a sharp medicine, as mentioned before; and the inverse athelils are now removed and not the normal ones with the tool I will mention.
A formica (ant) is also a small, filtered outgrowth, thick, on the surface of the body, extending deeply; when cold is felt, it feels like an ant bite and appears throughout the body; and they most frequently occur in hands.
And its treatment is to take a reed from the goose feather or strong vulture feather; and place the reed on the formica (ant) until it holds the circumference of the reed with its parts. Then turn your hand with the reed until you cut what is around the formica (ant); and place it in deep flesh and remove the formica from its root.
And if you wish, do this with a reed of brass or iron in this way.
The cannula should be placed above, drawing it upwards so as to loop around the finger for its relief and its own reversal.
And if you wish to cauterize a scabies, as previously mentioned in the cauterization of Athilih in the chapter on cauteries.
Chapter LXXXIII.
Chapter on the shapes of instruments used for enemas in diseases of the anus, and the dissolution of the abdomen, and colics.
When an enema is made from silver, or gold, or brass melted down, or mallet-work.
And sometimes these instruments are small, and large, according to those in whom they are administered.
Therefore what is administered in the cure of small children should be small; and those with weak or painful anuses, so should their enemas.
Large enema.
The cannula of this, i.e., the upper part where the uterus is tied, should be wide according to this method; and it should have a distinction so that the uterus can be tied as you see, and its lower end which is inserted into the anus, should be closed, i.e., not open, soft, very thin, drawing towards subtlety; and in one of its sides there should be two holes, and in the other side one hole.
And the size of the hole should be according to the thickness of rods, and slightly smaller, and the uterus in which the medicines are placed should be from the bladder of an animal; or from a sheep's parchment, which should be small like a little ewer; whose root should be one palm.
And it should be pierced with many holes as it is turned, and the space between each hole should be the thickness of a finger. Then insert into those holes a thread, for example, from raw flax, which should be from ten threads or about that much, and tie it together with the bladder like an ewer. When a bladder is placed within it (the patient), tighten at the neck with a strong constriction of a clyster, using two distinct parts. Then clysterize it afterwards.
And this is the form of the circle depicted here and the holes (or perforations).
The quality of clysterizing it is that you should fill the bladder or the urinary bladder with medicine which is heated according to the tolerance of the sick person: and be careful that it is not too hot or too cold.
Then the sick person lies down on his back and raises his legs towards above: and place under him a sheet, that is skin upon which men lie or linen.
Then anoint the end of the clyster with oil, or with white egg yolk, or with mucilage of fenugreek or similar substances. Then introduce it (the clyster) into the anus with care. Then let the attendant take hold of the bladder with both his hands at once, and squeeze it with force, until everything that is in the clyster passes into the intestines.
Then remove the clyster, and let the sick person raise his legs towards the wall (or side of the bed).
If the medicine forces him to evacuate, then hold it as much as possible. And if he sleeps all that night with it, it is more beneficial for his recovery.
But if you clysterize him in cases of the disease of the bowels (or intestines) and his evacuation is hastened: then repeat the clyster until he is cured.
If there are hemorrhoids or painful sores in the anus, then let the clyster be very subtle, soft, from the clysters with which children are clysterized.
And this is the shape of a subtle clyster over which the skin is to be tightened.
Head LXXXIIII. (This seems to be a Roman numeral, which is not
I have previously spoken about the division of treatment for wounds in another book; here I will speak about their treatment with hands and remedies as a supplement.
Therefore, I say that wounds are classified according to the cause of the wound and according to the place where the wound falls.
Therefore, the kinds of wounds are as numerous as the blows of a stone: either an incision with a sword or knife: or a blow with a spear, log, arrow, and similar things from many other objects.
Wounds that occur according to the parts of the body are such as a wound on the head, neck, chest, abdomen, or back, and similar from these members.
And I am the one telling the treatments for some wounds, in order to set forth my reasoning and rule for the remaining wounds.
And I shall begin with simple head wounds, because the description of compound wounds will come at the beginning of Chapter Three.
Therefore. (It appears that this sentence does not follow any previous statement When a simple wound occurs on the head and there is no bone fracture, consider whether it was caused by a blow of a stone or something similar, and the skin is only broken; the wound is large and one fears an abscess forming from hot suppurations; then rush, and make a cephalic vein let-down at once; and do not delay this; and draw out from the blood according to the strength of its potency; if there is nothing prohibiting venesection, especially if the blood flowing from the wound is scant. And let the venesection be from the opposite side of the wounded part. (This could mean letting blood from the unaffected or healthy side of the body, to help reduce pressure on the
And let the venesection be from the opposite side of the wounded part. (This could mean letting blood from the unaffected or healthy side of the body, to help reduce pressure on the And let the sick avoid filling himself with food and thick drinks.
If something forbids reduction (diet), then reduce from food, not approach meat or wine.
And place on the wound if it happens to him an abscess that is hot, a hot mustard poultice soaked in rose oil alone, or with wine containing hysop (hyssop).
If you are secure from a hot abscess, then place on the wound if it is new with its own blood and has not changed the air around it; and if already the air around it has changed, then place some ointments on it until it heals.
If the wound is large or from a sword cut, and similar: do not gather its edges together with stitches, then gather it with ligatures, as I will tell you about for wounds of the belly concerning their suturing.
If the wound has been detected to be from a bone and hangs and there is no retention of it except for a small suspension, then cut it. Then take care of the wound with medicines and restore the hard flesh to its place where there is skin; and order the sick one to be fed with foods that are thick, such as heads, cooked wheat, until it becomes soft; and similar things.
If you find decay on the skin that does not adhere to the bone: then cut off all the decay and throw it away; then take care of it.
If in these wounds there is an artery or a vein from which blood flows and it cannot be cut off with medicines, then search for the artery. If you find it uncut, then cut it with a spatula or tie it. If necessity compels and it does not comply with what was said, then cauterize it until the blood is cut off.
If the wounds are small and simple, their state is easy and light; in this way, you should sprinkle this powder on them, because it solidifies them before the air alters them.
Method of the powder for healing. Take one part of olibanum, two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of unslaked lime; grind it all well and sieve it; then fill the wound with this powder and apply a good bandage until it sticks well to the wound, and coagulate it with blood.
Then bind it on top with small bandages, and let it remain unopened until it does not come off. For the medicine will not be removed from him until he is healed.
