And sometimes lime alone does this, when there is no olibanum or dragon's blood available to you; it performs the same operation on many large wounds, when it must be placed over them and bound, and the wounds are recent with their own blood which has not been altered by air.
If the air has already altered [the wound] in some way, especially when it is during summertime, then this powder's purpose is not suitable; so take care of it with what I said, namely by placing something soothing on them, such as certain ointments; or place poultices made from barley flour, boiled with water and honey over them until they release pus. Then take care of the rest of the healing, until they are healed.
But if a fracture happens on the bone with the wound and it is small, then extract it using Gesthi; and I will now say the treatment for fractures of the skull that will follow.
Chapter on Neck Wounds.
If a wound occurs on the neck, then there is no difference in treatment between it and a simple wound of the head.
If the nerve of the neck or an artery has already been cut, if it is a nerve: then there is no skill in treating it except to divert its cure along with that which causes violent stiffness, such as ziniar and zegi and similar ones. Since nerves are harmful and contract them.
And do not put anything cold at all on the wound: since the substance of nerves is cold and their continuity is with the brain, which is above the organs; and let it be treated with soft medicines such as lime mixed with sweet water several times infused with oil or with rose oil, or turpentine when it is washed even with sweet water; and other mineral stones in this way, and moist unguents.
If the wound is large, then administer suture or sew its edges with strips of skin (or fat). Then care for it until it heals.
If the wound is deep or a cavity appears at its lower part where pus accumulates, then pierce it in a more depressed place.
If the artery has already been cut in the wound and blood flow follows: then separate it, or cut it off, and tie it; or cauterize it if necessity requires this.
If a fracture of the neck of the mandible or the entire mandible has occurred and the molars have been saved: then attach strips of skin to it with suture above the cervix of the throat, and do not touch the throat, but instead lay it down, and reduce it to its natural shape. Then tie it with a suitable suture and leave it for some days. Then take care of it yourself with ointments containing styptic and astringent properties until it heals.
If the wound has already made an impression on the bone, then inspect it thoroughly. If there are any bone fragments in it, remove all of them, or as many as possible: and what cannot be prepared, leave it until the wound rots, separates, and heals by itself.
If the wound is recent, then sprinkle powder on it as I previously mentioned. If it appears that a bone is present in the wound and a fistula forms, then treat it as described in its respective chapter.
Chapter on Wounds Treated with Spatulas.
If it is a wound made by a lance or knife and you see its depth, then assess it. If pus is coming out of the wound when the person who has been wounded breathes heavily, then you know that the wound is fatal.
If the depth is not great and the wound is fresh with blood, then do not put powder on it for the first hour or compress it, so that blood does not accumulate in its depth and return to the heart and kill the wounded person: instead, apply astringent ointment and solve it twice daily.
If astringent ointment is not available to you, then place a piece of old cotton over the wound opening to absorb what comes out of it due to moisture: and make sure that the wounded person sleeps on the wound so that what accumulates in it runs off.
If three days or more have passed since the wound occurred and the wounded person does not experience spasms, no bad heart tremors, no constriction of breathing, and the rest of its conditions are good: then you know that the wound is healed. Care for yourself and with linen cloths, and the rest of the treatment, until you are healed.
If it is cut open for healing and already opens up always, then know that it has become a Fistula. Care for it from its own chapter.
And if it is a wound from sword or knife cut, and simple on the surface of the chest or back, then care for it with what has preceded from stitching, if it is large; or with dust, if it is small.
If it has already made an impression on the bone and cut out fragments from it: then examine the wound, and hasten to extract those fragments, if they are separated. If they are not separated, then leave them until the wound rots, for extraction of them is painful.
For wounds happening to other parts of the body, the judgment in treatment is the same as what we have said.
Chapter on abdominal wounds and the outlet of the intestine, and their evacuation.
A rupture that happens to the abdomen is large, medium, or small.
From a large rupture, at times, the intestine comes out, or the number of intestines.
Therefore, their insertion and suturing is required, and their stitching is more arduous and difficult.
And even a small rupture may be difficult in another way. Therefore, the reduction of them is more difficult if you do not hasten to their insertion to their place immediately; because it swells, opens up, and becomes enlarged; therefore, the entrance of it is difficult.
Therefore, a medium rupture is more advantageous because with it the reduction of the intestine is not difficult, as it is with these two types.
You should know that suturing a vein is according to four modes.
Two common sutures meet in suturing the abdomen, and in suturing other wounds of the body; and two other sutures communicate specifically with the remaining wounds. However, they are more appropriate for suturing the abdomen: and I tell you one each with an explanation and a declaration.
Therefore, when a wound is small and something from the intestine comes out of it, and it becomes difficult to reduce it; then it is due to one of the two modes. Either because of the small size of the rupture, as we said; Or because there is an inflation in the intestine due to cold air.
When that is the case, then it is necessary to heat it up, so that you immerse a sponge or damp cloth in warm water alone. Or boil in water squill, cumin, fennel, and wormwood with the intestine until the inflation is resolved.
Sometimes it does vinegar in which there is a stoppage; and it is better than water alone in the resolution of inflation.
When you see that the inflation has been resolved, then moisten the intestine with water in which wormwood or mallow was boiled. For this reason, the entry is stimulated with it when the wound is small.
If, however, the return occurs after this treatment, then plug the rupture with a little, with an instrument with which hemorrhoids are cut.
And the first treatment is better when it is prepared, than cutting; and no pressure to cut is made after necessity and lack of instruments.
Let the part of it be twisted, sharp, and the other part not sharp, and let the fine end not be as subtle as a spatula, but rather slightly blunt; and this is the one that resembles a thorn, as you can see.
When the wound is enlarged and enters the intestine, then it is necessary that its reduction be according to its natural form in its own place, if possible on top of it: because it is better.
When the wound is wide at the lower part of the abdomen: then it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back and place his legs higher than his head. And if it is in the upper part of the abdomen, then put his head and his chest higher than his lower parts.
And similarly if the wound is in one of the two parts of the abdomen, then direct your attention and thought always in this: that the part where the wound is should be higher than the other part.
And so, it is necessary to insert this into large wounds and into medium-sized wounds.
In small wounds, place it according to what you have prepared.
Then cause a faithful servant to be present between your hands, who holds the entire wound with his hand and binds it up. Then cut out some thread following something for the one who follows to sew; and this is the common method of suturing one.
And it is that you receive a needle or a number of needles according to the size of the wound. Then cut off from the end of the wound a length equal to one finger of a ring, that is to say, of a doctor; and insert one needle beyond which you introduce thread in both edges of the skin, with both edges of the sifac that is under the skin from the inside, until it penetrates through another part; and you have already bound together the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the sifac; and there are four rows.
Then sew with double thread around the needle several times from both parts at once, until the two edges of the wound are bound together properly.
Then release the thickness of the finger also, and tie another needle: afterwards draw it straight with thread, as you did with the first needle. Do not cease to do that with the needle that you need until you complete the constriction of the whole wound.
Let the needle be of medium thickness between thickness and subtlety, because subtle needles deeply penetrate flesh quickly; and large ones have a difficult entrance into the skin; for this reason, they should be medium in subtlety and thickness.
And it is not fitting that the needle be shaped at both ends near the skin closely so as not to penetrate the flesh quickly and open the wound before its consolidation, and so that they do not elongate even with suturing, preventing the wound from consolidating.
Then cut the tips of the needles so as not to hurt the weak when sleeping; and place small pieces of cloth from all sides that hold the tips of the needle; and release them until you know that the wound is already consolidated.
And this form of suturing with needles in this manner is more suitable for small wounds. Because it suffices for their suturing one or two needles or around them.
The second kind of suturing is common, namely when you gather with suturing the four extremities; the four skin extremities, and the two sifac extremities as one, with a needle on which the thread is rolled equally in subtlety and thickness.
Then when you penetrate with the needle these four extremities, draw back the needle from the part where you started so that the thread falls down from the upper part of the wound; thus it is a suture, just like the suture of cloth when they are sewn together, and place between every stitch a quantity equal to the thickness of a little finger.
Humans know this stitch.
And with this stitch, I myself sewed the wound that had happened to a man in his belly, who had been wounded with a knife, and the wound was larger than one palm: and from the intestines there came out about two palms from the middle intestine, and the tear was in the middle of the abdomen.
I then brought it back after his intestines were set outside for 24 hours.
The wound therefore healed up in a space that was about 15 days: and I cured him, and he got well: and he lived after that for many years, turned back to his ways.
And the doctors had judged that he would not get well.
And it was a miracle that I did not cure it with an ointment. Because I was in the place where no ointment could be found, nor any medicine. Therefore I put over the wound a warm cloth twice a day, and I washed it with water of honey until it got well.
However, I shall speak about two kinds of stitches according to the report in speech.
And it is to begin with sharp stitching: and you insert a needle from the outside to the inside part.
When the needle goes through the skin and along the length and width of the whole body: then release the end of the sifac on the side where you inserted the needle, and make it penetrate to the end at the other side from the inside out at the opposite end.
When you make it penetrate in this way, then make it penetrate thus in the same end: and release the end of the sifac on that side, and let the needle penetrate to the end from the inside out at the other end: and let it penetrate with your penetration where you are causing it to penetrate into the sifac end, which is in that part, until it enters entirely.
Then also start from this same side, and take it together with the end that is from sifac on the other side, and pull out the point from the skin which it has penetrated.
Bring it back to the same skin, and take together with it the end of sifac that is on the other side with this end of mirach: pull it out from the skin that is on its side, and do this alternately and in reverse order until you have pulled it all out according to this example.
The sum of this suture is that you should make the sutures of skin, which are the skins themselves: thus, you should sew one end of sifac with one part of the skin's edge: and you should release it with the other part, until you have finished.
The second species of suture mentioned by Galen.
This discourse is told as if you should tie it up in the same way as some healers do, that is to gather all parts that are fitting by nature and bring together: and apply one end of sifac to its other end, and apply one end of mirach to another end of it. And this is done as I tell you.
You should bend the point towards the end of mirach that is near you from the outside part, and make it penetrate to the inside: and release both ends of sifac. Then bend back the point, and make it penetrate from the outside to the inside in both ends of sifac.
Then turn both (of them) back and make both penetrate from the inside to the outside in two ends of mirach that are on the opposite side.
And this method of suture is better than the common easy suture and is the suture that was mentioned earlier.
This is therefore the saying of Galen.
And some said. The repair of the abdominal suture is done with two needles. What is to be done, insert one thread into each of them, and begin with the introduction of the needle from what is near you, and make it pass through until the other side, according to the equal stitch of those who sew leather equally.
And know that when the rupture is in the middle of the abdomen, then the suture of it is more difficult than the other parts of the abdomen.
The judgment of the medicine for wounds is the judgment for other wounds.
What is to be done, when you seize a recent wound with its own blood before it changes through air, and you reduce the bowel, and tie it, and make it fit, then place it on powder of lime.
If the air has already altered the wound: then place on it certain ointments which are present to you, until they make pus; and let the threads fall, and bind with sifac, and press with a mirror. Then care for it as is the treatment of other wounds until it is healed.
If there are no medicines present to you, then immediately place on it, as soon as it begins to emit pus, old cloth; and change it twice a day, as I taught you, until it is healed.
For you do not need another medicine in many positions when the wounds are simple.
If you fear that the wound communicates with the main parts in injury, then it is necessary to immerse a soft wool in oil of temperate heat, or rose oil; and place it in the girdle around the parts which are between the groins, and under the armpits.
If he feels pain, or punctures, or putrefaction in his intestines (for this often happens), then clisterize him with warm stiptic wine: especially if the putrefaction has already reached the intestine, and an opening has been made penetrating to the concavity of it.
And know that what is from the large intestine is easier to heal; and what is from the small intestines is more difficult to heal.
The jejunum intestine, which is named so, does not receive healing from a wound that occurs in it at all: and this is because of the multitude of its veins, and the size of them, and because of the subtlety of its body, and because of the proximity of its nerves to nature.
If what proceeds from the wound is pus, and you find it fresh: bring it back as you bring back the intestines equally.
But if time has passed and it has become green or black: then you must stitch it with a thread above the place that has become blackened, so that there is no bleeding. For in pus there are veins and arteries.
Then cut what is beyond that ligament, and place two ends of the thread hanging from below on the lower part of the wound outside it: so as to relieve your pressure upon it, and the extraction of the pus at the site of the wound, and the emission of the wound's pus.
Chapter on the Wound that Occurs in the Intestine.
When there is a rupture in the intestine and it is small: then it is possible for it to be restored in some people: because I have seen one who was wounded in his abdomen with a lance thrust, and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and the wound was old: and it became a fistula, and exuded feces, and gases.
I therefore placed the treatment, until I was confident of its healing; neither did I cease to investigate it, until it was healed and the location was consolidated.
After I saw the location already consolidated, I feared something bad might happen to the sick man concerning his stomach; and it did not happen to him from that bad thing. And he remained in better dispositions for himself, eating and drinking, and urinating, and went into the bath, and was trained in his own diet.
And some of the experienced men said, when a wound occurs in the Intestine and it is small, then it should be tied thusly. And it is to receive ants with large heads. Then gather two lips of the wound and place one ant with an open mouth on both lips of the wound. When its head is upon them, and it closes its mouth, cut off its head, for it will stick to them and not be removed.
Then place another ant near the first one, and do not cease to make this with an ant according to the size of the wound in its entirety.
Then reduce it and sew up the wound. For those heads remain attached in the intestine until the intestine is eaten and it heals, so that no harm comes to the sick man completely.
And it is now possible to tie the intestine even with fine thread; what has been taken out of the intestine of the animal and attached to it when inserted into the point.
And it is to receive the end of this thread from the intestine and scrape off much flesh. Then tie a thin linen thread at its end. Then insert the thread into the point and sew up the intestine with it. Then reduce it to a dislocation.
This method of stitching with worms and intestines is not except by faith and hope.
Know that a large, wide wound, especially if it is on one of the slender intestines, has no other remedy except subtlety. There is no healing of it at all.
Chapter on the care of ulcers and fistulas.
Know that every wound or abscess when it becomes old and chronic, turns into an ulcer and does not consolidate, but always emits pus and does not separate: then it is called universally in whatever member it may be a fistula, and we call it a Zuchimen.
And a fistula indeed is in truth a knotted filter, hard, white: with which there is no pain, to which there is a hollow of the bird's feather: and for this reason some call it Rasa, that is, the feather.
And in certain hours it is moist, which emits pus. And perhaps the moisture is cut in certain hours. And sometimes this moisture is much, and little; and it is thick, and fine.
And I have already stated in the division, then when I said wounds, that every ulcer which does not heal and is not generated in it flesh, is not for any of the nine causes.
One of the reasons is that because of the scarcity of blood in the body; or because it is bad; or because there is hard flesh within and above it, preventing the generation of flesh; or because it is full of dirt and filth; or because the ulcer itself is rotten, and the matter emitted to it is of poor quality; or because the medicine is inappropriate for its healing; or because corruption falling in the region is a kind of pestilence, as happens in Caesaraugusta; in which difficult digestion of diseases occurs, and healing of abscesses is delayed by nature; or because there is one bone in it, or a number of bones.
I have already shown you all those causes and their signs, as well as the treatments of them with medicines in division: it is necessary here that I make you know the treatment for Fistula and Ulcer, which is done by the way of surgery with the hand.
Know therefore that Fistula occurs in all the members of the body. For among these are Fistulae that reach to great veins and arteries, or nerves, or tendons; or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs: or to any of the vertebrae in the back, or to any of the joints composed of bones; such as hands and feet: and among these are those that approach the proximity of a main member and similar ones.
What therefore among these Fistulae is according to this method, is difficult to heal from sickness and does not receive treatment, and the occupation with it is labour and ignorance.
If there is any of these Fistulae whose depth does not reach to the places which I have said: and you hope for, trust in its treatment, and desire to reach knowledge about it, then take a probe made of copper or iron, if the Fistula goes straight, and explore it with that.
If there is a twist in the Fistula, then investigate it with a probe made of delicate lead. Since lead being softened and curved towards twists.
If the Fistula has many openings, it is not possible for you to sign on it with a probe. Then close one of its openings with clisteria from among them.
Since the moisture that you clisterize it goes backward to other openings and runs out of them.
Then carefully investigate according to how it is possible for you: so that you may know whether there is bone or nerve there, and whether the hollow is a long or short fistula, or whether it is a fistula with many openings, which is on top of it all, with the strength of your hand: with the questioning you ask of the sick person, and the discovery of pain under pressure with your hand, and similar signs and causes from accidents.
When you have thus established yourself in a true position, then proceed with treatment according to your confidence: and it is for you to consider whether the fistula appearing near is in a place safe at a distance from joints, nerves, arteries, veins, or any of the places I mentioned to you: then cut the fistula according to what has been said in my narrative, and remove what is in it by filtering, and corrupt flesh that arises in its opening, or pus, and similar things: and treat it until it heals.
If the fistula is deep, and is straight: then it is necessary to cut it as deeply as possible for you. Then cleanse the fistula from all corrupted flesh.
Then administer linen wound bandages filled with sharp medicines: and insert it into the hollow of the fistula that you grasped with iron, do this several times until the sharp medicine corrodes everything that remains in the hollow of the fistula due to corruption.
Then restore the fistula with ointments that promote healthy flesh until it heals.
If it does not heal through this, then cauterize the fistula as we have said before.
If the cause of the fistula is bone, and you are certain of this: then ask for it, and cut the bone as I have told you: if nothing prevents you from doing so in a vein, nerve, or main member, as we have said before.
If therefore a bone is discovered in you, and there is something corrupted within it, and blackening: then scrape it off, until the entire corruption of it is removed. Then care for it with it, until it heals up.
If it does not heal, and discharges pus as before: then know, that you have not achieved a complete removal of the corruption.
Then dig into it again, and carefully investigate its reason, and cleanse it with your utmost strength.
Then restore it. If it heals, it is good; and if not, then know that the corruption is in a deep remote part of the body, which you have not reached. Therefore, there is no skill in it for you, except to let it go to nature.
If a small bone is corrupted and if it can be drawn out with fine forceps which suit to that purpose: draw it out with them.
If there are many bones: then carefully investigate the drawing of all of them, and do not leave anything in them with your strength.
If something from the moist areas opposes you and there is no fear or mistake in the cutting of them: then cut those moist areas and flesh, if they are present, and release the bones.
If there is no preparation to remove the bones from your time: then place over the wound something that rots it; and leave it until it rots what is around their bones from flesh and moistness.
And watch the wound so that it does not close up. And bind the incision which you cut during your operation. Or place over it, if you fear, cotton soaked in soft sulfur oil; or cotton soaked in the Egyptian ointment, or some green ointments.
When those [humidities] in question rot, and the bones are separated from them, let the excision of them be anointed, and their attraction as well.
If it is a large bone such as the leg bone or hip bone and similar [bones], and what has rotted from it is a large part: then shave it down with the finest file until that blackness and corruption is removed. Then restore the wound.
If what has rotted within it is a large part, and corruption has already reached the marrow of the bone, then it must be cut through, and it must be sawed all the way to where the corruption ends: then treat it until it heals.
And I tell you this secret, which happens to a man in his thigh: place it before yourself as an example and aid for your operation.
A young man of about thirty years had pain in his thigh, caused by something that moved within him from the inside until the matter reached the thigh, and an abscess was formed with a large abscess: there was no external cause for him.
So the time passed with the error of physicians until the abscess was opened, and many materials gathered there with him. And his treatment was delayed until the thigh became fistulous, and many openings were made in it: which all discharged pus, and humors of the body.
Therefore a multitude of physicians treated him for about two years, and there was no skilled person in the art of surgery called until I saw his thigh, and the materials that ran out of those openings with great flow: even the entire body of the man had become wasted, and his color was jaundiced.
So I inserted a probe into one of the openings, and the probe reached the bone.
Then I have examined all the openings and found that they lead to each other from all parts of the leg.
I have dug deep, and cut through one of the openings, until I exposed a part of the bone: and I found it corrupt, already rotten, decayed, putrid, and pierced through, until it had penetrated to the marrow.
I have then sawed what was exposed to me, and prepared it from the rotten bone.
And rejected that which was not in the bone except for this corruption, which I cut off and sawed. And I had already pulled it out (the pus or infection).
Then I placed the wound dressing with solidifying medicines in a long space. And it is not healed (yet).
Then I tried again, and exposed over the bone second above the first opening: and I found continuous corruption with the bone: and I sawed what appeared to me also from that corruption.
And then I attempted to dress it (the wound). And it is not dressed (yet).
I then exposed it again, and did not stop cutting the bone in pieces, and trying to dress it: and it is not dressed, until I cut out about a palm's length of bone with its marrow.
Then I dressed it with medicines, and it healed quickly, and was cured: and this repetition of the operation and section of it was not necessary except for the disposal of weakness, the frailty of the patient, and my fear of death: since it happened to him at all hours from excess evacuations with bad syncopes.
He is therefore cured completely: and flesh hard has grown at the place of the bone, and good arrangement was made in his body, and his strength returned: and he has turned back to his dispositions: and it did not cause him any harm in walking at all.
If the projecting bone in the body is already fractured, then it is necessary that you sew it up in this manner: and it is as follows: take a ligament and bind it at the end of the projecting bone; and command someone to stretch it upward; and place another thicker ligament on the first one. Then sew it to the flesh that surrounds the bone; extend its end so as to pull the flesh towards the lower parts; and remove the flesh from the place you wish to sew, so that the saw does not cut the flesh.
Place a log or board under the bone below in a good position; for when you do this, it is not forbidden to cut corrupted flesh.
And it is necessary that the saw be over the corrupted place slightly, so that there is no corruption in the hollow of the bone; and it does not appear to the senses in its view, and compel another [part] to serve in its stead.
If the bone is corrupted and not projecting, but rather continuous with another part; and corruption is in its middle or in a part of it; then remove the flesh from all parts completely. Then place a log below.
Then saw it from the first part where there is corruption, until the saw has reached the other side; and let the saw be slightly longer than the corruption, as we said before.
If the corruption is at a joint, cut away the corrupted joint itself and saw the bone where it joins with another part.
If the corruption is at the joining of two joints, then there is no remedy but abrasion [to remove the damaged tissue].
If the corruption is at the beak of the hand or foot, then there is a great difficulty in it. It is necessary for you to examine the appearance of the corruption. And grind it (the tumor) away and clean it as much as possible for you, and when it is corrected with any tool: if it does not create opposition to the Vein or the Nerve.
And know that there are many cutting and sawing tools for this bone, according to the position of the bones, their preparation, their thickness, their hardness, their size, their smallness, their density, and their rarity. Therefore, it is necessary to prepare every kind of instrument suitable for each operation.
And know that these operations signify for you the type of instrument you require, when your study is prolonged. And the knowledge of the methods of this art is a testimony to the methods of illnesses: then you will indeed find for yourself what suits it from instruments for every sickness.
And I am confirming for you at the end of this chapter the number of instruments, which you will place examples on for cutting, and proof on others.
The form of another saw.
The form of a rasp for joints. The head of this rasp should be in the shape of a star-headed nail and its points according to the shape of the points on a nail file.
It is not suitable unless it scrapes with it the heads of joints when they are broken or a large and thick bone.

Shape of a curved-tipped razor.
Shape of a small, flexible razor.
It resembles a saw and its end is like that of a chisel: it is used in many places for the reason of bones.
Shape of a razor suitable for cutting through bone.
Its end is triangular and sharp-edged.
Made of ivory. And similarly, all that I have said must be made from razors, chisels and saws.
Section of limbs and setting of bones.
Rottenness occurs at the extremities, either from an external cause or an internal one.
When you have been treated for that corruption with medicine, and the treatment does not help; and if you see corruption attacking a limb which is not struck by anything: then it is necessary to cut through that limb until the corruption passes away through it, or death, or a greater evil affecting the member.
And the sign which occurs is that a limb becomes dark, until it is thought to be rotten; it has been burnt by fire or rot sets in after it has turned black; it is cut through until the rot reaches what follows that limb and creeps over the entire body.
Approach with the incision of that limb, and similarly if the cause of the rot is from certain venomous animals such as the marine scorpion, viper, weasel, and similar creatures.
If corruption or a blow occurs at the end of a finger, then cut off the finger, and do not leave any space for the rot to spread, so that it may spread over the rest of the hand.
And similarly if it occurs in the hand, then cut off at the root of the fingers, and do not leave any space for the rot to spread until it reaches the arm bone.
And if it enters into this [joint], then cut off the arm at the elbow joint.
If the rot passes beyond this [point], and you see it approximately at the elbow: then death is approaching for the sick person. To administer treatment beyond that point is the strength of the medicine.
And similarly do with the foot, when rot sets in at a toe; then cut off that toe at one of the joints; and if it reaches the ankle bone, then cut off the entire foot. If it goes up to the knee, then cut off the leg at the knee joint.
If corruption has already reached the knee, then there is no skill in it, except for release and leaving the sick one to die.
The method of cutting a limb or sewing it is to tighten the ligament below where you wish to cut, and to tighten another ligament above the place. And extend one servant ligament downwards, and another servant ligament upwards towards the top. And you separate the flesh that is between two ligaments with a broad knife until all the flesh is exposed. Then it is cut or sewn.
It is necessary to place a linen cloth over all the parts so that the knife does not touch a healthy place; and a wound must be added to the sickness, and a hot abscess.
If there is an internal bleeding while you are operating, then quickly cauterize the place; or else place some powder on it that draws blood. Then return to your medicine until it is completed.
Then bind the wounded limb with an appropriate ligament and take care of it until it heals.
And I tell you what happened to a man on his foot, this same thing happens to you.
Because there is a blackness occurring on his foot similar to burning by fire; and corruption first begins in one of his toes until it reaches the entire foot.
Therefore the man cut himself, after seeing corruption occurring on a limb with pain and burning; and he cut himself at the joint, and he was healed.
And after a long period of time, that same corruption occurred on one of his fingers on his index hand.
Therefore he came to me and tried to recover that loss with what I put on his hand from remedies after cleansing his body; and the excess was not found, and it began to spread to another finger until corruption reached his entire hand.
He therefore called me to cut his hand; and I did not want it, hoping for reimbursement from him for the excess; and I also feared death itself during the incision of his hand. Because the man's virtue was above his fall.
Since he had given up on me, he returned to his own land; and he came back to me about it because he hurried, and he cut off his entire hand; and he was healed.
And I did not bring this story unless it is an aid for that which falls under the genus of this illness; and it is to show what needs to be shown, and according to how it should be done.
Chapter on the care of the sinuses, and the quality of cleansing with medications.
When a boil occurs in certain fleshy parts and the space of the boil extends until it collects pus; then it breaks or perforates and whatever is in the pus exits and leaves an empty spot as if it were a vessel; and the skin that is on top of it, like a cloth that has been made thin; and it does not reach final corruption nor press against bone, nerve, or ligament: it is worthy to be called a Sinus; and it is not called a Fistula, but if the space prolongs until corruption presses into one of these organs, then it is called a Fistula, or zukh.
And its care is to cut the entire skin as it rolls; especially when it has been made thin and resembles a cloth; and you trust that it will not adhere due to its own corruption.
If you hope that the skin will adhere and this final corruption does not follow as a consequence; and if there is thickness in the skin from flesh, then treat it with Clisterium; and be aware of this for the Sinus.
Then if it [the wound] is large and the pus that is emitted from it has a foul smell: then cleanse him with a clyster of Egyptian medicine, which is vinegar, oil, and honey, portions being equal, mixed in a vessel; and boil it over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes thick like honey.
Then take what is necessary from it [the substance]: and dissolve it with water and honey, and cleanse the bladder with it; and sew up its opening, and let the medicine be poured into it to the quantity of two hours.
Then remove it with pressure: do this for several days until the bladder is purified and the foul smell is removed.
And sometimes the bladder is cleansed with water and ashes when this medicine is not available to you; and it is for you to take the ashes of vinewood or the ashes from oak wood, and pour water on it. Then wash it and cleanse the bladder with it until you are confident that the bladder has been purified.
But if the patient is not able to tolerate the Egyptian medicine or water and ashes, then cleanse the bladder with water and honey, to which something has been added from crushed honey. Or cleanse the bladder with honey and wine mixed together, because it is a property of honey to purify and wash; and wine makes the bladder adhere, especially when there is an excess of hardness and dryness in the wine.
Whenever you do this and are confident that the corruption of the bladder has been removed: then cleanse the bladder with it that causes flesh to grow within it.
And it is for you to take from the plaster of dyafinicon; and dissolve it with rose oil and stiptic wine, or cleanse the bladder with certain medicines and other ointments, whose properties I have written about in the treatise on ointments.
If the orifice of the Sinus is narrow and cannot take a cannula for clysters: then expand it slightly with iron; or place linen wrapped in Egyptian ointment, or Basilicon ointment until it expands.
And similarly if the orifice is also wide, then gather its lips with suture; and let the amount that the clyster can enter go in without addition.
And similarly if the orifice from which pus flows is elevated towards the higher parts: then cut it at a lower place that is within it, so that the pus runs out below; because pus, when constrained in depth of Sinus, prevents flesh generation in it.
If it is not possible for you to cut the Sinus around its lower part as desired: then try to prepare a member in such a way that pus runs out from it with ease according to how you are prepared. Try not to retain anything from the pus within it; and take medicines for consolidation that are put on the mark, suitable for what you want. Spread them out on a linen cloth. And let the cloth be of such a size that there is communication throughout the entire Sinus. Then cut with scissors a hole directly in the orifice of the Sinus, wider than the orifice of the Sinus by a little. Then spread out on a cloth soaked with soft ointment of such size as the hole; and place it above at a distance from the orifice of the Sinus to ease the discharge of pus from it; and do not remove the large cloth unless after several days, once.
The one who is above the orifice of the Sinus is the one you remove at every hour, to expel what accumulates in it from pus; and know that, whether the discharge from it is much or little, digested or undigested.
And again consider the place of the sinus, if its lord feels pain there, or if there is no pain in it, and if there is an abscess in it, or if there is no abscess in it.
When your treatment is extended thus, and you see the matter that comes out through the opening of the sinus, then you know that the sinus is already adhering or is approaching adherence; then dissolve it in the morning, or on the third day: and when you dissolve the wound, then change the linen, and renew the ointment.
If however a subtle vapor comes out from the sinus after a long time, then do not despair of its adherence, for its healing approaches, since there are people who act slowly in the generation of flesh in their wounds, and there are those who act contrary to this.
If however an undigested pus comes out of the sinus after many days, then know that the sinus does not adhere.
If therefore the adherence of the sinus is delayed and its case prolonged: then add drying medicaments, but let the physicians do so, that the medicaments are humid in substance and dry in potency; such as unguentum dyafinicon, when excess is added to it from zegi.
And from the more distant cure that is applied, it is that you take unguentum dyafinicon, and dissolve it with rose oil, and mix upon it old wine equal in substance.
Then compound it with the above and use it.
And now make something similar to this action, when you do not have unguentum dyafinicon, honey, when you boil it until it thickens, and use it. Or take myrrh, aloe, and olibanum; grind all of them, and powder it over honey while it is above the fire. Then draw a line on the skin above the tumor and sew it onto the abscess; and draw a thread with honey that you have boiled, until it swells up; then pulverize its substance and place it on the linen cloth and sew it.
Sometimes Aristolochia longa, the root of celestial lily, and lily are administered; and flour of the plant, and knotgrass. Use them (the simple or combined remedies), crush and sift them; and pulverize the honey that I have mentioned, and use it.
If the abscess prolongs and is not cured by this treatment, then you know that there is corruption in its depth; either it has already made an impression on the bones or on other hard parts or ligaments; then cure it with fistula treatment, as previously mentioned.
Chapter on the treatment of corns and calluses, abrasion of the finger nail, and incision or section.
A corns is an abscess that arises under the nail of the thumb or big toe, or perhaps arises in other fingers.
When it prolongs and is neglected without treatment, and it becomes an abscess; or it rots and discharges pus until it corrodes the nail root; and perhaps it corrupts it completely, and perhaps corruption reaches the bone until it has a fetid smell; and the tip of the finger becomes broad, and its color becomes dark.
When you treat it (the corns), and your treatment does not produce the desired effect; then you must cut away all excess that remains from the nail with an iron. Then cauterize the wound after that. Indeed, cauterization is very beneficial.
If the bone is healthy and the nail also is healthy, and empty additions of the nail are pressing the flesh towards the inside and it begins to pierce and hurt it; then it is necessary that you place subtle Radium under the angle of the nail which is piercing the flesh, and push it up; and cut the flesh with ease, and put on top of what remains of the flesh from burning medicines, corrosives, until all of it is removed. Then take care of it with ointments, until it heals.
If corruption is already pressing into the bone, then it is necessary that you cut that bone and extract it; for the bone will never heal while there is a corrupted bone present.
If you see corrosion and corruption advancing on the finger, then cut it at one joint, according to the previously mentioned memorization. Then take care of it until it heals.
If, however, the nail is worn or struck and a violent pain occurs, then it is necessary that you use the lancet first on the weak. Then cut the nail with a sharp spatulate section from above to sight.
And keep the cut from reaching the flesh that is under the nail, for you will cause excessive painfulness over the weak by this and there will be a cause added to the growth of the skin in the place.
Then take care of the place with what eases the pain.
A finger that is born in some human hands may be entirely fleshy; and it may have bones in some of them, and it may have a nail in it; and some of these are born at the junction of the root, or its birthplace is in some joints of the finger. Therefore, the one that is born in some joints of the finger does not move; and the one that is born at the junction of the finger may move.
The operation on the fleshy one amongst them is easy. Cut him at the root with a wide spatula.
But for the one whose birth is in the junction of roots, the treatment is difficult. Therefore, avoid cutting him.
However, when he is born on the digit at the end of tendons, then one must cut the flesh of him first with a round incision up to the bone. Then, using one of those saws fitting for that, saw the bone. Then care for him until he is healed.
However, consolidation that happens in fingers often occurs either at birth of a person, meaning he is born with it, or from consolidation of a wound, or burn by fire, and similar conditions.
Therefore, one must cut away that consolidation until the fingers return to their natural shape. Then place a cloth or gauze soaked in rose oil between them, so that they do not consolidate quickly, and separate them; or place between them a thin sheet of lead until the location heals as required.
And similarly, if consolidation occurs in certain fingers with the palm, then cut away that consolidation according to its preparation and the shape of the member.
Chapter on Defects of Incisions.
Uites are swollen veins filled with melancholic superfluities that often occur in various parts of the body; and their outcome is most common in legs, especially in those traveling or working or carrying heavy loads.
Therefore, one must administer a vigorous purging of the body from black bile on several occasions.
Then make venesection from the patient using a basilica vein.
Treatment of those (afflictions) with iron is according to two modes. One of them is, that it should be scented and the black blood drawn out. And another mode is, that the vein should be elevated and everything should be drawn out.
Cutting (it) however is according to this mode. First, the leg should be embroced with much hot water until the thick, foul blood is resolved. Then bind the weakened leg from the upper part of the hipbone of it, as far as the lower part of the thigh with plaster. Then cut the vein in one place or two or three in a wide incision.
Then elevate, that is, draw blood from the lower part of the leg with your hand upwards, and it is necessary that the lancet be applied to the weakened person first. Then cut the nail downwards until there comes out from the blood a quantity that you see is sufficient and that the strength of the weakened person can bear.
Then tie it up and tell him to abstain from foods that produce black bile; and repeat the evacuation and bloodletting when the veins are full, and this will harm the weakened person.
Elevation (of the leg) however is according to this mode. Shave the weakened leg if there are many hairs on it. Then immerse it (the leg) in a bath or embroce the leg on its own with hot water until it becomes red and the veins swell; or exercise it with vigorous movement if there is no bath present for him, until the limb warms up.
Then make an incision along the vein directly for its length; or at the end of it by the knee, or at the lower part of it by the heel.
Then open the skin with awls and scrape off the vein from every side until it is apparent to the sense; and there appears at its appearance that it turns from red to blackish-blue. When it comes out from the skin, it appears white as a cord.
Then insert the Radius under it until it is raised and comes out from the skin; hang it with a blind hook, soft.
Then cut another section near that section with three fingers. Then scrape the skin from above the vein until it appears. Then lift it with radii as you did before and hang it with another hook as you did first.
Then cut another section or several sections as needed. Then scrape it and make an incision on the last section at the heel.
Then extract it to the section above it.
And do this until you extract it from the section above or from all sections when it comes out completely; then make an incision on it.
If it does not obey you to extract and lift, then insert a pointed probe with a strong thread and tie it and extract it; or insert a radii under it and rotate your hand on all sides until it comes out. And be careful not to cut it. For if it is cut, it becomes very difficult for you to lift it and harm results from it on the patient.
When you have extracted it completely, place linen soaked in wine and rose oil or olive oil over the wound site and take care of it until it heals.
If the vein is contracted and twisted with a winding in various parts, and it is not as we said according to rectitude: then you must make an incision over all parts of its twisting and the winding points of itself.
Then hang it with hooks until you lift the entire vein; be careful not to cut or wound the vein at your incision site, for it will be difficult for you to lift or extract it. Preserve therefore your prudence.
The shape in which a wound heals is the vine.
The shape of an incision in a blind man.
The scarring in this type of incision is not like that of other incisions, nor does it have a sharp point to damage the vein; rather, it has a thick folding, soft; because if it were delicate, it would pierce the vein with its delicacy; on the contrary, excess thickness is superfluous, as we said.
On the extraction of the vein of the leg.
This vein is generated in the legs on hot lands, as Alizegi says, and in the land of Arabs, and in dry, hot lands of little softness, that is, where no grass grows nor tree.
And perhaps it is generated in other places of the body apart from the legs.
Indeed, its generation is from the putrefaction that occurs beneath the skin, as it happens within the bodies of snakes and roundworms and worms generated between the skin and flesh.
And the sign of the emergence of this vein is that which happens when there is a violent inflammation in the leg. Then the place is blistered. Then the vein begins to emerge from that blistered spot, as if it were the root of a plant or an animal.
When it appears from that spot, then you should wind around it a piece of lead whose weight is half a kentenarie and the same number of knots; and let the suspended lead hang down from the leg.
Whenever something comes out of it towards the outside, wind that up in lead and knot it. If it prolongs itself much, then cut off a part of it and wind up the rest. Do not incise it rootwise before it entirely comes out. If you cut (it), it contracts and enters into the flesh: and causes an abscess to occur, and corruption at the place, and a bad ulcer.
Therefore, it is necessary that it be gently treated and slowly extracted until it entirely comes out and nothing remains of it in the body: and from this vein comes forth in some men what is along its length five palms and ten. And now it has come to me, because it came out of a man of twenty palms.
If it is cut during your treatment hour: then insert a probe into its opening and perforate it with a long hole, along with the body, until all that is in it from matter has been evacuated: and administer the corruption of the place with medicines for some days. Then take care of it with treatment for abscesses.
And this vein sometimes has many branches, especially when it appears at the junction of the foot, or in the foot itself: and there are many openings to it, and a branch comes out from every opening.
Take care of it, as we have said in the division, and with what was previously mentioned.
[Chapter heading:] Section on worms generated beneath the skin, and this is called Bouina's Disease.
This disease is called Bouina's Disease in a certain land among us: because it often happens to cows, and there is a small worm born between the skin and flesh.
It moves throughout the body, going up and down: and it is noticed by the senses during walking from one limb to another until it bursts at any place where it bursts through the skin and comes out.
The generation of it (the tumor) is from the putrefaction of certain humors. As worms and snakes, that is, earthworms and ascaris, occur in the abdomen.
And it (the stone) is feared from its malice. Because when it (the stone) moves within the body and rises to the head and reaches its location, then perhaps it opens there, and exits, and destroys the eye; and this happens frequently.
Since therefore you wish to cure it (the stone) and remove it, this can only be done during its movement (or passage) and appearance to the sense of sight.
Therefore, what is above it (the stone) must be compressed with a strong bandage and what is beneath it with a compression of the ligature. Then cut above it, and remove it.
If it (the stone) has gone deep into the flesh and you cannot find it, then place a cautery on its location with fire until it dies.
The larger one (the stone), which is feared, is its corruption that destroys the eye, as we have said.
If you see it (the stone) has already reached the head near the eye, then compress above it with a good bandage. Then cut above it, and remove it.
The sick person must use self-cleansing of the body with medications that dissolve bad humors putrid.
Let him avoid foods causing putrefaction.
Section on the pain of Nakir (a medical case or disease).
This disease is known as Nakir in our land; it is a pain that occurs in certain members, then changes from one member to another.
And indeed I myself have seen it, as I am telling you. I was summoned to a sick woman in certain villages. And she had rolled up her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
And after staying for an hour, I saw the swelling moving with a probe, as a worm moves, ascending to her shoulder more quickly than it could: like living silver when it runs from place to place.
Therefore, the pain left that place, and it was fixed in her shoulder.
Then she sat for an hour, and ran through the rest of the body until it reached another arm.
Then she told me that she was being turned over in her entire body, as I had seen.
Therefore, I marveled at the swiftness of her change from member to member. And indeed, before that, I had not seen this illness appear in my eyes in such a way as described above. Nevertheless, I have seen many who find pain changing from member to member; but I did not see it with my eyes as I saw it in the woman.
And I do not think that this is the case except for the reason that the woman was one of those who are from the dry bodies with detected veins; hence, it appears to the sense that the windiness has been changed.
And it is necessary that this does not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate and with bodies that are moist, of the hidden veins.
Since you wish to cure it and the patient feels that pain; then if it is visible to you as we have said, then press on it quickly and under it; cut above it as soon as possible, until that windiness, constricted, comes out; and cauterize the place.
If you do not see it with your eyes: then take care of it by excision of the body, and with that which expels wind, and soften them with fetid pills, and with pills of serapeo, and similar ones.
On the Extraction of Arrows.
Arrows are classified according to their types and the places in which they fall on the body.
The diversity of arrows is as follows: for there are some that have large points, and small; concave, and blunt. And among them are those that have three corners. And among them are those that have tongues.\] And among them are those with stars.\]
But as for those that fall on the limbs, they are classified into two ways.\] Either the limbs are cavities like the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar ones.\] When a arrow falls into any of these cavities and appears to you as signs of death, which I will tell you later, then it is necessary that you take out the extraction of this arrow from them, for death follows it wherever it may be, in many situations.\] And when these signs of evil do not appear to you, and the arrow is not hidden deep within the cavity, then take out the arrow itself, and care for the wound.\]
The signs of the brain are as follows when an arrow falls into it and penetrates the bone, and exits through a hole above the brain: for there follow from this sweat, dizziness, fainting, reddening of the eyes, swelling, reddening of the tongue, spasms, confusion of mind, and vomiting of cholera.\] Blood may come out from the nostrils, or the ears. The speech may be cut off, and the voice destroyed. White moisture comes out from the wound's place, like pulp. And it comes out from it resembling serous fluid of flesh.
If therefore these signs appear to you, then abstain from treatment, and draw out the arrow if it does not come out by itself.
The signs of an arrow in the heart are when it falls near the left breast, and it feels as if it is fixed in a hard thing, not in an empty one. And perhaps the arrow has a motion similar to the pulse: and black blood runs from the wound. And this is followed by coldness in the limbs, cold sweat, and fainting. Know therefore that death approaches without doubt.
The sign of an arrow in the lung is the exiting of frothy blood from the wound: and the containers that follow the neck are to be emptied, and the color of the patient is changed. And it exhales a large, deep breath: and it seeks cold air.
If the arrow falls into the pleura, which is in the chest: then it is near small ribs: and a great panting with violent pain, with sighing: and all the limbs of the shoulders are moved.
If the arrow falls into the stomach, then perhaps something undigested comes out from the wound.
If the arrow falls into the abdomen and is fixed there: something fecal comes out from the wound, or pus, or an already disrupted intestine. Therefore there is no hope for his recovery nor in drawing out the arrow.
If the arrow falls into the bladder and comes out urine: and something proceeds from it to the outside, and the pain is stronger on the patient: then know that it is mortal.
The remaining members, such as the face, neck, throat, spatula, help, dorsal spondylus, furcula, hip, leg, and similar members are saved according to several dispositions when the arrow does not strike an artery, or nerve: and the arrow is not venomous.
And I tell you what I saw regarding these arrows, so that you may understand it in relation to your treatment.
That is, because a man had an arrow fall into his tear duct of the eye, at the root of the nose. Therefore I removed it from the other side, under the ear fat of him; and he was healed, and no harm came to his eye as a result.
And I removed another arrow from a Jew, which had fallen upon him in the fat of his eye beneath the lower eyelid; and the arrow was already concealed, and I did not obtain any part of it except for its small end that adhered to the wood; and the arrow was large among arrows of the Tartars, with a soft iron tip, in which there were no feathers.
Therefore the Jew was healed, and no harm came to his eye as a result.
And I removed another arrow from the throat of a Christian.
The arrow was Arabic and it had feathers. Therefore I cut along the same (line), between two gullets; and already it was submerged in his throat. I therefore sharpened myself with that (instrument) until I removed the arrow; and the Christian was healed.
And I removed another arrow from a man who it had fallen upon his abdomen; and we thought that he was going to die as a result of it.
After thirty days had passed without any change in his condition, I made an incision along the arrow; and I opened it up, and removed the arrow; and he was healed, and no harm came to him as a result.
And I saw a man who an arrow had fallen upon his back, and the wound around it had consolidated. After seven years it came out of the root of his hipbone.
I have seen a woman to whom an arrow fell into her womb, and the wound has healed upon her, and the arrow remains within her; and none of her conditions were changed, and the woman did not find harm in any of her natural operations.
I have seen another man to whom an arrow fell on his face; and the wound has healed, and remains, not causing him much pain; and many similar things have happened.
And I extracted an arrow from a nobleman of the king, which had fallen upon him in the middle of his nose, and had already started to descend slightly towards the right; and the arrow was completely hidden.
Therefore, I was summoned for his treatment after the loss of the arrow until three days. Then I found the arrow wound to be very narrow.
Therefore, I examined it with a fine probe and did not feel it; but he himself was finding a puncture and pain under his right ear. So I hoped that the puncture was at the end of the arrow.
Then I applied the place with an ointment containing attractant and softening properties, confident that the wound would heal and the sign of the arrow would appear so that I could cut it; but this did not happen at the desired location, indicating that the arrow had healed.
Therefore, I applied the ointment for many days upon him; but it did not happen as desired, and the wound healed in the meantime; and the man remained weak from extraction of the arrow until a certain day when he felt the arrow within his nose. And he told me this.
And he told me this. Therefore, I placed a strong medicine, a corrosive upon the wound for many days until it was opened; and when I examined it with a fine probe, I felt the sharp end of the arrow which had stuck into the wood.
Then I added the sharp medication to the wound opening until it became evidently visible to us the end of the arrowhead; and it passed with that space of time approximately four months with it.
Then when the wound was expanded and I was able to insert forceps into it and move it, but it did not obey to come out; then I did not stop trying to refine and work on it with various means until on one day with well-made forceps, according to the shape that came in the end of the chapter, I pulled it out. Then I healed the wound.
And certainly the physicians judge that the nose cartilage cannot be healed. So I healed it (the wound), and the wound became sound and healthy again with strong health; nothing harmed it at all.
And I tell you the quality of the extraction of some arrows: so that you may place the rule and significance on that which I did not say.
Because the parts and divisions of this art are not grasped with the narrative; neither does the book comprehend it, and the wise craftsman compares little to much; and with what is present, over what is absent: and finds a new operation and new instrument for descent of foreign matters in this art when they occur.
Therefore I say that arrows do not come out from the limbs to which they are fixed except in two ways. Or by attraction from the place from where it entered. Or by means of the opposite part.
And that which comes out where it entered is either an arrow proceeding in a fatty place; and it attracts and comes out.
If it does not obey to come out at the hour when it falls; then it is necessary that you leave it for some days until the flesh that is around it decomposes; and the attraction of it will loosen and its exit.
If it is punctured into a bone and does not comply with you for drainage, then let it be for some days; and repeat it daily with attraction and motion, until it drains out.
If it does not comply with you for drainage after some days, then it is necessary that you pierce through the bone from all sides with a sharp awl until the sutures swell up. Then draw it out and remove it.
If the arrow has already been hidden in the body and concealed from feeling: then search for it with probing. If you feel it, then draw it out with certain tools that are suitable for drawing it.
If you cannot reach it because of the constriction of the wound and the length of the arrow in depth, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein there: then mark it until the wound swells up, and it becomes possible to extract the arrow.
If it is fixed in the ears with which it is held: then cut away the flesh attached to them from all sides as much as you can, and proceed, if you cannot reach the flesh by cutting through the fracture of the ears or by twisting them, until it breaks out.
When administering the extraction of an arrow, wherever it may be, then use twisting of your hand with forceps to all parts until it comes out. And, with utmost subtlety, so that the arrow is not broken and the attraction and extraction of it become difficult for you.
If you are unable to extract the arrow within an hour, then let it be for a number of days until what is around it becomes rotten. Then repeat the process. For indeed, a bladder will be formed around it. If, however, it causes bleeding against you, then administer what we have said in its chapter for cure: and keep your strength from cutting the vein, nerve, or sinew.
And administer every method possible for the evacuation of the arrow: let it be with ease, calmness, slowness, or firmness, as I have told you.
It is necessary that when you pull out the arrow, it should be as weak as it was at the time of the arrow's wounding in the same figure. For it is more advantageous. If, however, this is not possible for you, then administer what is possible according to the figures.
The arrow that comes out from the opposite side of the other part or has already started to come out towards the outside, or makes a hump at the end of the arrow by the sensation of the skin above it and you see it protruding: then cut above it, and make the incision according to the size that the forceps can grasp.
Then pull it out: for indeed, it becomes easy to come out.
If it is retained in the bone, then twist your hand according to its roundness until the arrow presses into the bone and swells: then pull it out.
And if not: dismiss her for some days; then return her, until she exits (heals).
If the wood of the arrow is within her, then push her along with it.
If however the wood has fallen out and there is a desire to administer a thrust: then insert into her a concave instrument so that it enters the concavity of the arrowhead; afterwards push her with it.
If however the arrow is concave, then push her along with the instrument entering into it. The arrow will be absorbed by that (medicine).
If the arrow is poisoned, then it is necessary to remove all the flesh in which there is the venom; if this is possible for you (to do so). Then take care of her with whatever suits that (medicine).
If the arrow falls into the chest, or the abdomen, or the bladder, or the side; and is close to that which you touch with a probe, and it is possible for you to cut above it: then cut it, and beware of the vein, or nerve, and extract it.
Then heal the wound, if you see it, and take care of that (the injured area) until it heals.
And this is the form of forceps with which arrows are extracted.
The tips should be similar to the beak of a bird, which are made of iron; when they grasp the arrow, they do not let it go.
And there are many shapes made of them, large, small, and medium-sized, according to the size and smallness of the arrow, and the width and depth of the wound.
